Example command line with\n480: `run_under`:\n481: \n482: ```\n483: bazel test -c dbg //test/server:backtrace_test\n484: --run_under=//tools:stack_decode --strategy=TestRunner=local\n485: --cache_test_results=no --test_output=all\n486: ```\n487: \n488: Example using input on stdin:\n489: \n490: ```\n491: bazel test -c dbg //test/server:backtrace_test --cache_test_results=no --test_output=streamed |& tools/stack_decode.py -s bazel-bin/test/server/backtrace_test\n492: ```\n493: \n494: You will need to use either a `dbg` build type or the `opt` build type to get file and line\n495: symbol information in the binaries.\n496: \n497: By default main.cc will install signal handlers to print backtraces at the\n498: location where a fatal signal occurred. The signal handler will re-raise the\n499: fatal signal with the default handler so a core file will still be dumped after\n500: the stack trace is logged. To inhibit this behavior use\n501: `--define=signal_trace=disabled` on the Bazel command line. No signal handlers will\n502: be installed.\n503: \n504: # Running a single Bazel test under GDB\n505: \n506: ```\n507: bazel build -c dbg //test/common/http:async_client_impl_test\n508: bazel build -c dbg //test/common/http:async_client_impl_test.dwp\n509: gdb bazel-bin/test/common/http/async_client_impl_test\n510: ```\n511: \n512: We need to use `-c dbg` Bazel option to generate debugging symbols and without\n513: that GDB will not be very useful. The debugging symbols are stored as separate\n514: debugging information files (`.dwp` files) and we can build a DWARF package file\n515: with `.dwp ` target. The `.dwp` file need to be presented in the same folder with the\n516: binary for a full debugging experience.\n517: \n518: # Running Bazel tests requiring privileges\n519: \n520: Some tests may require privileges (e.g. CAP_NET_ADMIN) in order to execute. One option is to run\n521: them with elevated privileges, e.g. `sudo test`. However, that may not always be possible,\n522: particularly if the test needs to run in a CI pipeline. `tools/bazel-test-docker.sh` may be used in\n523: such situations to run the tests in a privileged docker container.\n524: \n525: The script works by wrapping the test execution in the current repository's circle ci build\n526: container, then executing it either locally or on a remote docker container. In both cases, the\n527: container runs with the `--privileged` flag, allowing it to execute operations which would otherwise\n528: be restricted.\n529: \n530: The command line format is:\n531: `tools/bazel-test-docker.sh <bazel-test-target> [optional-flags-to-bazel]`\n532: \n533: The script uses two optional environment variables to control its behaviour:\n534: \n535: * `RUN_REMOTE=<yes|no>`: chooses whether to run on a remote docker server.\n536: * `LOCAL_MOUNT=<yes|no>`: copy/mount local libraries onto the docker container.\n537: \n538: Use `RUN_REMOTE=yes` when you don't want to run against your local docker instance. Note that you\n539: will need to override a few environment variables to set up the remote docker. The list of variables\n540: can be found in the [Documentation](https://docs.docker.com/engine/reference/commandline/cli/).\n541: \n542: Use `LOCAL_MOUNT=yes` when you are not building with the Envoy build container. This will ensure\n543: that the libraries against which the tests dynamically link will be available and of the correct\n544: version.\n545: \n546: ## Examples\n547: \n548: Running the http integration test in a privileged container:\n549: \n550: ```bash\n551: tools/bazel-test-docker.sh  //test/integration:integration_test --jobs=4 -c dbg\n552: ```\n553: \n554: Running the http integration test compiled locally against a privileged remote container:\n555: \n556: ```bash\n557: setup_remote_docker_variables\n558: RUN_REMOTE=yes MOUNT_LOCAL=yes tools/bazel-test-docker.sh  //test/integration:integration_test \\\n559:   --jobs=4 -c dbg\n560: ```\n561: \n562: # Additional Envoy build and test options\n563: \n564: In general, there are 3 [compilation\n565: modes](https://docs.bazel.build/versions/master/user-manual.html#flag--compilation_mode)\n566: that Bazel supports:\n567: \n568: * `fastbuild`: `-O0`, aimed at developer speed (default).\n569: * `opt`: `-O2 -DNDEBUG -ggdb3 -gsplit-dwarf`, for production builds and performance benchmarking.\n570: * `dbg`: `-O0 -ggdb3 -gsplit-dwarf`, only debug symbols, no optimization.\n571: \n572: You can use the `-c <compilation_mode>` flag to control this, e.g.\n573: \n574: ```\n575: bazel build -c opt envoy\n576: ```\n577: \n578: To override the compilation mode and optimize the build for binary size, you can\n579: use the `sizeopt` configuration:\n580: \n581: ```\n582: bazel build envoy --config=sizeopt\n583: ```\n584: \n585: ## Sanitizers\n586: \n587: To build and run tests with the gcc compiler's [address sanitizer\n588: (ASAN)](https://github.com/google/sanitizers/wiki/AddressSanitizer) and\n589: [undefined behavior\n590: (UBSAN)](https://developers.redhat.com/blog/2014/10/16/gcc-undefined-behavior-sanitizer-ubsan) sanitizer enabled:\n591: \n592: ```\n593: bazel test -c dbg --config=asan //test/...\n594: ```\n595: \n596: The ASAN failure stack traces include line numbers as a result of running ASAN with a `dbg` build above. If the\n597: stack trace is not symbolized, try setting the ASAN_SYMBOLIZER_PATH environment variable to point to the\n598: llvm-symbolizer binary (or make sure the llvm-symbolizer is in your $PATH).\n599: \n600: If you have clang-5.0 or newer, additional checks are provided with:\n601: \n602: ```\n603: bazel test -c dbg --config=clang-asan //test/...\n604: ```\n605: \n606: [Thread sanitizer (TSAN)](https://github.com/google/sanitizers/wiki/ThreadSanitizerCppManual) tests rely on\n607: a TSAN-instrumented version of libc++ and can be run under the docker sandbox:\n608: \n609: ```\n610: bazel test -c dbg --config=docker-tsan //test/...\n611: ```\n612: \n613: Alternatively, you can build a local copy of TSAN-instrumented libc++. Follow the [quick start](#quick-start-bazel-build-for-developers) instruction to setup Clang+LLVM environment. Download LLVM sources from the [LLVM official site](https://github.com/llvm/llvm-project)\n614: \n615: ```\n616: curl -sSfL \"https://github.com/llvm/llvm-project/archive/llvmorg-11.0.1.tar.gz\" | tar zx\n617: \n618: ```\n619: \n620: Configure and build a TSAN-instrumented libc++. Please note that `LLVM_USE_SANITIZER=Thread` preprocessor definition is used to enable TSAN instrumentation, and `CMAKE_INSTALL_PREFIX=\"/opt/libcxx_tsan\"` defines the installation directory path.\n621: \n622: ```\n623: mkdir tsan\n624: pushd tsan\n625: \n626: cmake -GNinja -DLLVM_ENABLE_PROJECTS=\"libcxxabi;libcxx\" -DLLVM_USE_LINKER=lld -DLLVM_USE_SANITIZER=Thread -DCMAKE_BUILD_TYPE=Release \\\n627:   -DCMAKE_C_COMPILER=clang -DCMAKE_CXX_COMPILER=clang++ -DCMAKE_INSTALL_PREFIX=\"/opt/libcxx_tsan\" \"../llvm-project-llvmorg-11.0.1/llvm\"\n628: ninja install-cxx install-cxxabi\n629: \n630: rm -rf /opt/libcxx_tsan/include\n631: ```\n632: \n633: Generate local_tsan.bazelrc containing bazel configuration for tsan tests:\n634: \n635: ```\n636: bazel/setup_local_tsan.sh </path/to/instrumented/libc++/home>\n637: \n638: ```\n639: \n640: To execute TSAN tests using the local instrumented libc++ library pass `--config=local-tsan` to bazel:\n641: \n642: ```\n643: bazel test --config=local-tsan //test/...\n644: ```\n645: \n646: For [memory sanitizer (MSAN)](https://github.com/google/sanitizers/wiki/MemorySanitizer) testing,\n647: it has to be run under the docker sandbox which comes with MSAN instrumented libc++:\n648: \n649: ```\n650: bazel test -c dbg --config=docker-msan //test/...\n651: ```\n652: \n653: To run the sanitizers on OS X, prefix `macos-` to the config option, e.g.:\n654: \n655: ```\n656: bazel test -c dbg --config=macos-asan //test/...\n657: ```\n658: \n659: ## Log Verbosity\n660: \n661: Log verbosity is controlled at runtime in all builds.\n662: \n663: To obtain `nghttp2` traces, you can set `ENVOY_NGHTTP2_TRACE` in the environment for enhanced\n664: logging at `-l trace`. For example, in tests:\n665: \n666: ```\n667: bazel test //test/integration:protocol_integration_test --test_output=streamed \\\n668:   --test_arg=\"-l trace\" --test_env=\"ENVOY_NGHTTP2_TRACE=\"\n669: ```\n670: \n671: Similarly, `QUICHE` verbose logs can be enabled by setting `ENVOY_QUICHE_VERBOSITY=n` in the\n672: environment where `n` is the desired verbosity level (e.g.\n673: `--test_env=\"ENVOY_QUICHE_VERBOSITY=2\"`.\n674: \n675: ## Disabling optional features\n676: \n677: The following optional features can be disabled on the Bazel build command-line:\n678: \n679: * Hot restart with `--define hot_restart=disabled`\n680: * Google C++ gRPC client with `--define google_grpc=disabled`\n681: * Backtracing on signals with `--define signal_trace=disabled`\n682: * Active stream state dump on signals with `--define signal_trace=disabled` or `--define disable_object_dump_on_signal_trace=disabled`\n683: * tcmalloc with `--define tcmalloc=disabled`. Also you can choose Gperftools' implementation of\n684:   tcmalloc with `--define tcmalloc=gperftools` which is the default for builds other than x86_64 and aarch64.\n685: * deprecated features with `--define deprecated_features=disabled`\n686: * http3/quic with `--//bazel:http3=False`\n687: * autolinking libraries with `--define=library_autolink=disabled`\n688: * admin HTML home page with `--define=admin_html=disabled`\n689: * admin functionality with `--define=admin_functionality=disabled`\n690: * static extension registration with `--define=static_extension_registration=disabled`\n691: * spdlogging functionality with `--define=enable_logging=disabled`\n692: \n693: ## Enabling optional features\n694: \n695: The following optional features can be enabled on the Bazel build command-line:\n696: \n697: * Exported symbols during linking with `--define exported_symbols=enabled`.\n698:   This config will exports all symbols and results in larger binary size. If partial symbols export\n699:   is required and target platform is Linux, then `bazel/exported_symbols.txt` can be used to land it.\n700: * Perf annotation with `--define perf_annotation=enabled` (see\n701:   source/common/common/perf_annotation.h for details).\n702: * BoringSSL can be built in a FIPS-compliant mode with `--define boringssl=fips`\n703:   (see [FIPS 140-2](https://www.envoyproxy.io/docs/envoy/latest/intro/arch_overview/security/ssl#fips-140-2) for details).\n704: * ASSERT() can be configured to log failures and increment a stat counter in a release build with\n705:   `--define log_fast_debug_assert_in_release=enabled`. SLOW_ASSERT()s can be included with `--define log_debug_assert_in_release=enabled`. The default behavior is to compile all debug assertions out of\n706:   release builds so that the condition is not evaluated. This option has no effect in debug builds.\n707: * memory-debugging (scribbling over memory after allocation and before freeing) with\n708:   `--define tcmalloc=debug`. Note this option cannot be used with FIPS-compliant mode BoringSSL and\n709:   tcmalloc is built from the sources of Gperftools.\n710: * Default [path normalization](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/issues/6435) with\n711:   `--define path_normalization_by_default=true`. Note this still could be disable by explicit xDS config.\n712: * Manual stamping via VersionInfo with `--define manual_stamp=manual_stamp`.\n713:   This is needed if the `version_info_lib` is compiled via a non-binary bazel rules, e.g `envoy_cc_library`.\n714:   Otherwise, the linker will fail to resolve symbols that are included via the `linktamp` rule, which is only available to binary targets.\n715:   This is being tracked as a feature in: https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/issues/6859.\n716: * Process logging for Android applications can be enabled with `--define logger=android`.\n717: * Excluding assertions for known issues with `--define disable_known_issue_asserts=true`.\n718:   A KNOWN_ISSUE_ASSERT is an assertion that should pass (like all assertions), but sometimes fails for some as-yet unidentified or unresolved reason. Because it is known to potentially fail, it can be compiled out even when DEBUG is true, when this flag is set. This allows Envoy to be run in production with assertions generally enabled, without crashing for known issues. KNOWN_ISSUE_ASSERT should only be used for newly-discovered issues that represent benign violations of expectations.\n719: * Envoy can be linked to [`zlib-ng`](https://github.com/zlib-ng/zlib-ng) instead of\n720:   [`zlib`](https://zlib.net) with `--define zlib=ng`.\n721: \n722: ## Enabling and disabling extensions\n723: \n724: Envoy uses a modular build which allows extensions to be removed if they are not needed or desired.\n725: Extensions that can be removed are contained in\n726: [extensions_build_config.bzl](../source/extensions/extensions_build_config.bzl). Contrib build\n727: extensions are contained in [contrib_build_config.bzl](../contrib/contrib_build_config.bzl). Note\n728: that contrib extensions are only included by default when building the contrib executable and in\n729: the default contrib images pushed to Docker Hub.\n730: \n731: The extensions disabled by default can be enabled by adding the following parameter to Bazel, for example to enable\n732: `envoy.filters.http.kill_request` extension, add `--//source/extensions/filters/http/kill_request:enabled`.\n733: The extensions enabled by default can be disabled by adding the following parameter to Bazel, for example to disable\n734: `envoy.wasm.runtime.v8` extension, add `--//source/extensions/wasm_runtime/v8:enabled=false`.\n735: Note not all extensions can be disabled.\n736: \n737: To enable a specific WebAssembly (Wasm) engine, you'll need to pass `--define wasm=[wasm_engine]`, e.g. `--define wasm=wasmtime` to enable the [wasmtime](https://wasmtime.dev/) engine. Supported engines are:\n738: \n739: * `v8` (the default included engine)\n740: * `wamr`\n741: * `wasmtime`\n742: \n743: If you're building from a custom build repository, the parameters need to prefixed with `@envoy`, for example\n744: `--@envoy//source/extensions/filters/http/kill_request:enabled`.\n745: \n746: You may persist those options in `user.bazelrc` in Envoy repo or your `.bazelrc`.\n747: \n748: Contrib extensions can be enabled and disabled similarly to above when building the contrib\n749: executable. For example:\n750: \n751: `bazel build //contrib/exe:envoy-static --//contrib/squash/filters/http/source:enabled=false`\n752: \n753: Will disable the squash extension when building the contrib executable.\n754: \n755: ## Customize extension build config\n756: \n757: You can also use the following procedure to customize the extensions for your build:\n758: \n759: * The Envoy build assumes that a Bazel repository named `@envoy_build_config` exists which\n760:   contains the file `@envoy_build_config//:extensions_build_config.bzl`. In the default build,\n761:   a synthetic repository is created containing [extensions_build_config.bzl](../source/extensions/extensions_build_config.bzl).\n762: * Start by creating a new Bazel workspace somewhere in the filesystem that your build can access.\n763:   This workspace should contain:\n764:   * Empty WORKSPACE file.\n765:   * Empty BUILD file.\n766:   * A copy of [extensions_build_config.bzl](../source/extensions/extensions_build_config.bzl).\n767:   * Comment out any extensions that you don't want to build in your file copy.\n768: \n769: To have your local build use your overridden configuration repository there are two options:\n770: \n771: 1. Use the [`--override_repository`](https://docs.bazel.build/versions/master/command-line-reference.html)\n772:    CLI option to override the `@envoy_build_config` repo.\n773: 2. Use the following snippet in your WORKSPACE before you load the Envoy repository. E.g.,\n774: \n775: ```\n776: workspace(name = \"envoy_filter_example\")\n777: \n778: local_repository(\n779:     name = \"envoy_build_config\",\n780:     # Relative paths are also supported.\n781:     path = \"/somewhere/on/filesystem/envoy_build_config\",\n782: )\n783: \n784: local_repository(\n785:     name = \"envoy\",\n786:     # Relative paths are also supported.\n787:     path = \"/somewhere/on/filesystem/envoy\",\n788: )\n789: \n790: ...\n791: ```\n792: \n793: When performing custom builds, it is acceptable to include contrib extensions as well. This can\n794: be done by including the desired Bazel paths from [contrib_build_config.bzl](../contrib/contrib_build_config.bzl)\n795: into the overridden `extensions_build_config.bzl`. (There is no need to specifically perform\n796: a contrib build to include a contrib extension.)\n797: \n798: ## Extra extensions\n799: \n800: If you are building your own Envoy extensions or custom Envoy builds and encounter visibility\n801: problems with, you may need to adjust the default visibility rules to be public,\n802: as documented in\n803: [extensions_build_config.bzl](../source/extensions/extensions_build_config.bzl).\n804: See the instructions above about how to create your own custom version of\n805: [extensions_build_config.bzl](../source/extensions/extensions_build_config.bzl).\n806: \n807: # Release builds\n808: \n809: Release builds should be built in `opt` mode, processed with `strip` and have a\n810: `.note.gnu.build-id` section with the Git SHA1 at which the build took place.\n811: They should also ignore any local `.bazelrc` for reproducibility. This can be\n812: achieved with:\n813: \n814: ```\n815: bazel --bazelrc=/dev/null build -c opt envoy.stripped\n816: ```\n817: \n818: One caveat to note is that the Git SHA1 is truncated to 16 bytes today as a\n819: result of the workaround in place for\n820: https://github.com/bazelbuild/bazel/issues/2805.\n821: \n822: # Coverage builds\n823: \n824: To generate coverage results, make sure you are using a Clang toolchain and have `llvm-cov` and\n825: `llvm-profdata` in your `PATH`. Then run:\n826: \n827: ```\n828: test/run_envoy_bazel_coverage.sh\n829: ```\n830: \n831: **Note** that it is important to ensure that the versions of `clang`, `llvm-cov` and `llvm-profdata`\n832: are consistent and that they match the most recent Clang/LLVM toolchain version in use by Envoy (see\n833: the [build container\n834: toolchain](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy-build-tools/blob/main/build_container/build_container_ubuntu.sh) for reference).\n835: \n836: The summary results are printed to the standard output and the full coverage\n837: report is available in `generated/coverage/coverage.html`.\n838: \n839: To generate coverage results for fuzz targets, use the `FUZZ_COVERAGE` environment variable, e.g.:\n840: ```\n841: FUZZ_COVERAGE=true VALIDATE_COVERAGE=false test/run_envoy_bazel_coverage.sh\n842: ```\n843: This generates a coverage report for fuzz targets after running the target for one minute against fuzzing engine libfuzzer using its coprus as initial seed inputs. The full coverage report will be available in `generated/fuzz_coverage/coverage.html`.\n844: \n845: Coverage for every PR is available in Circle in the \"artifacts\" tab of the coverage job. You will\n846: need to navigate down and open \"coverage.html\" but then you can navigate per normal. NOTE: We\n847: have seen some issues with seeing the artifacts tab. If you can't see it, log out of Circle, and\n848: then log back in and it should start working.\n849: \n850: The latest coverage report for main is available\n851: [here](https://storage.googleapis.com/envoy-postsubmit/main/coverage/index.html). The latest fuzz coverage report for main is available [here](https://storage.googleapis.com/envoy-postsubmit/main/fuzz_coverage/index.html).\n852: \n853: It's also possible to specialize the coverage build to a specified test or test dir. This is useful\n854: when doing things like exploring the coverage of a fuzzer over its corpus. This can be done by\n855: passing coverage targets as the command-line arguments and using the `VALIDATE_COVERAGE` environment\n856: variable, e.g. for a fuzz test:\n857: \n858: ```\n859: FUZZ_COVERAGE=true VALIDATE_COVERAGE=false test/run_envoy_bazel_coverage.sh //test/common/common:base64_fuzz_test\n860: ```\n861: \n862: # Cleaning the build and test artifacts\n863: \n864: `bazel clean` will nuke all the build/test artifacts from the Bazel cache for\n865: Envoy proper. To remove the artifacts for the external dependencies run\n866: `bazel clean --expunge`.\n867: \n868: If something goes really wrong and none of the above work to resolve a stale build issue, you can\n869: always remove your Bazel cache completely. It is likely located in `~/.cache/bazel`.\n870: \n871: # Adding or maintaining Envoy build rules\n872: \n873: See the [developer guide for writing Envoy Bazel rules](DEVELOPER.md).\n874: \n875: # Bazel performance on (virtual) machines with low resources\n876: \n877: If the (virtual) machine that is performing the build is low on memory or CPU\n878: resources, you can override Bazel's default job parallelism determination with\n879: `--jobs=N` to restrict the build to at most `N` simultaneous jobs, e.g.:\n880: \n881: ```\n882: bazel build --jobs=2 envoy\n883: ```\n884: \n885: # Debugging the Bazel build\n886: \n887: When trying to understand what Bazel is doing, the `-s` and `--explain` options\n888: are useful. To have Bazel provide verbose output on which commands it is executing:\n889: \n890: ```\n891: bazel build -s envoy\n892: ```\n893: \n894: To have Bazel emit to a text file the rationale for rebuilding a target:\n895: \n896: ```\n897: bazel build --explain=file.txt envoy\n898: ```\n899: \n900: To get more verbose explanations:\n901: \n902: ```\n903: bazel build --explain=file.txt --verbose_explanations envoy\n904: ```\n905: \n906: # Resolving paths in bazel build output\n907: \n908: Sometimes it's useful to see real system paths in bazel error message output (vs. symbolic links).\n909: `tools/path_fix.sh` is provided to help with this. See the comments in that file.\n910: \n911: # Compilation database\n912: \n913: Run `tools/gen_compilation_database.py` to generate\n914: a [JSON Compilation Database](https://clang.llvm.org/docs/JSONCompilationDatabase.html). This could be used\n915: with any tools (e.g. clang-tidy) compatible with the format. It is recommended to run this script\n916: with `TEST_TMPDIR` set, so the Bazel artifacts doesn't get cleaned up in next `bazel build` or `bazel test`.\n917: \n918: The compilation database could also be used to setup editors with cross reference, code completion.\n919: For example, you can use [You Complete Me](https://valloric.github.io/YouCompleteMe/) or\n920: [clangd](https://clangd.llvm.org/) with supported editors.\n921: \n922: This requires Python 3.8.0+, download from [here](https://www.python.org/downloads/) if you do not have it installed already.\n923: \n924: Use the following command to prepare a compilation database:\n925: \n926: ```\n927: TEST_TMPDIR=/tmp tools/gen_compilation_database.py\n928: ```\n929: \n930: \n931: # Running format linting without docker\n932: \n933: Note that if you run the `check_spelling.py` script you will need to have `aspell` installed.\n934: \n935: You can run clang-format directly, without docker:\n936: \n937: ```shell\n938: bazel run //tools/code_format:check_format -- check\n939: ./tools/spelling/check_spelling_pedantic.py check\n940: bazel run //tools/code_format:check_format -- fix\n941: ./tools/spelling/check_spelling_pedantic.py fix\n942: ```\n943: \n944: # Advanced caching setup\n945: \n946: Setting up an HTTP cache for Bazel output helps optimize Bazel performance and resource usage when\n947: using multiple compilation modes or multiple trees.\n948: \n949: ## Setup local cache\n950: \n951: You may use any [Remote Caching](https://docs.bazel.build/versions/master/remote-caching.html) backend\n952: as an alternative to this.\n953: \n954: This requires Go 1.11+, follow the [instructions](https://golang.org/doc/install#install) to install\n955: if you don't have one. To start the cache, run the following from the root of the Envoy repository (or anywhere else\n956: that the Go toolchain can find the necessary dependencies):\n957: \n958: ```\n959: go run github.com/buchgr/bazel-remote --dir ${HOME}/bazel_cache --host 127.0.0.1 --port 28080 --max_size 64\n960: ```\n961: \n962: See [Bazel remote cache](https://github.com/buchgr/bazel-remote) for more information on the parameters.\n963: The command above will setup a maximum 64 GiB cache at `~/bazel_cache` on port 28080. You might\n964: want to setup a larger cache if you run ASAN builds.\n965: \n966: NOTE: Using docker to run remote cache server described in remote cache docs will likely have\n967: slower cache performance on macOS due to slow disk performance on Docker for Mac.\n968: \n969: Adding the following parameter to Bazel everytime or persist them in `.bazelrc`.\n970: \n971: ```\n972: --remote_cache=http://127.0.0.1:28080/\n973: ```\n974: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/envoy--v1.32.1@b35dd17bea856e19fc4e65fb05e68170841d3726/-/blob/bazel/README.md"}}}

Configure, build and/or install the [Envoy dependencies](https://www.envoyproxy.io/docs/envoy/latest/start/building#requirements).\\n33: 1. `bazel build -c opt envoy` from the repository root.\\n34: \\n35: ### Building from a release tarball\\n36: \\n37: To build Envoy from a release tarball, you can download a release tarball from Assets section in each release in project [Releases page](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/releases).\\n38: Given all required [Envoy dependencies](https://www.envoyproxy.io/docs/envoy/latest/start/building#requirements) are installed, the following steps should be followed:\\n39: \\n40: 1. Download and extract source code of a release tarball from the Releases page. For example: https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/releases/tag/v1.24.0.\\n41: 1. `python3 tools/github/write_current_source_version.py` from the repository root.\\n42: 1. `bazel build -c opt envoy` from the repository root.\\n43: \\n44: > **Note**: If the the `write_current_source_version.py` script is missing from the extracted source code directory, you can download it from [here](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/envoyproxy/envoy/main/tools/github/write_current_source_version.py).\\n45: > This script is used to generate SOURCE_VERSION that is required by [`bazel/get_workspace_status`](./get_workspace_status) to \\\"stamp\\\" the binary in a non-git directory.\\n46: \\n47: > **Note**: To avoid rate-limiting by GitHub API, you can provide [a valid GitHub token](https://docs.github.com/en/authentication/keeping-your-account-and-data-secure/about-authentication-to-github#githubs-token-formats) to `GITHUB_TOKEN` environment variable.\\n48: > The environment variable name that holds the token can also be customized by setting `--github_api_token_env_name`.\\n49: > In a GitHub Actions workflow file, you can set this token from [`secrets.GITHUB_TOKEN`](https://docs.github.com/en/actions/security-guides/automatic-token-authentication#about-the-github_token-secret).\\n50: \\n51: Examples:\\n52: \\n53: ```console\\n54: GITHUB_TOKEN=<GITHUB_TOKEN> python3 tools/github/write_current_source_version.py\\n55: MY_TOKEN=<GITHUB_TOKEN> python3 tools/github/write_current_source_version.py --github_api_token_env_name=MY_TOKEN\\n56: ```\\n57: \\n58: ## Quick start Bazel build for developers\\n59: \\n60: This section describes how to and what dependencies to install to get started building Envoy with Bazel.\\n61: If you would rather use a pre-build Docker image with required tools installed, skip to [this section](#building-envoy-with-the-ci-docker-image).\\n62: \\n63: As a developer convenience, a [WORKSPACE](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/WORKSPACE) and\\n64: [rules for building a recent\\n65: version](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/bazel/repositories.bzl) of the various Envoy\\n66: dependencies are provided. These are provided as is, they are only suitable for development and\\n67: testing purposes. The specific versions of the Envoy dependencies used in this build may not be\\n68: up-to-date with the latest security patches. See\\n69: [this doc](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/bazel/EXTERNAL_DEPS.md#updating-an-external-dependency-version)\\n70: for how to update or override dependencies.\\n71: \\n72: 1. Install external dependencies.\\n73:     ### Ubuntu\\n74:     On Ubuntu, run the following:\\n75:     ```console\\n76:     sudo apt-get install \\\\\\n77:        autoconf \\\\\\n78:        curl \\\\\\n79:        libtool \\\\\\n80:        patch \\\\\\n81:        python3-pip \\\\\\n82:        unzip \\\\\\n83:        virtualenv\\n84:     ```\\n85: \\n86:     ### Fedora\\n87:     On Fedora (maybe also other red hat distros), run the following:\\n88:     ```console\\n89:     dnf install \\\\\\n90:         aspell-en \\\\\\n91:         libatomic \\\\\\n92:         libstdc++ \\\\\\n93:         libstdc++-static \\\\\\n94:         libtool \\\\\\n95:         lld \\\\\\n96:         patch \\\\\\n97:         python3-pip\\n98:     ```\\n99: \\n100:     ### Linux\\n101:     On Linux, we recommend using the prebuilt Clang+LLVM package from [LLVM official site](http://releases.llvm.org/download.html) for Clang 14.\\n102: \\n103:     Extract the tar.xz and run the following:\\n104:     ```console\\n105:     bazel/setup_clang.sh <PATH_TO_EXTRACTED_CLANG_LLVM>\\n106:     ```\\n107: \\n108:     This will setup a `clang.bazelrc` file in Envoy source root. If you want to make clang as default, run the following:\\n109:     ```console\\n110:     echo \\\"build --config=clang\\\" >> user.bazelrc\\n111:     ```\\n112: \\n113:     Note: Either `libc++` or `libstdc++-7-dev` (or higher) must be installed.\\n114: \\n115:     #### Config Flag Choices\\n116:     Different [config](https://docs.bazel.build/versions/master/guide.html#--config) flags specify the compiler libraries:\\n117: \\n118:     - `--config=libc++` means using `clang` + `libc++`\\n119:     - `--config=clang` means using `clang` + `libstdc++`\\n120:     - no config flag means using `gcc` + `libstdc++`\\n121: \\n122: \\n123:     ### macOS\\n124:     On macOS, you'll need to install several dependencies. This can be accomplished via [Homebrew](https://brew.sh/):\\n125:     ```console\\n126:     brew install coreutils wget libtool go bazelisk clang-format autoconf aspell\\n127:     ```\\n128:     _notes_: `coreutils` is used for `realpath`, `gmd5sum` and `gsha256sum`\\n129: \\n130:     _notes_: See Homebrew python setup notes: https://docs.brew.sh/Homebrew-and-Python.\\n131: \\n132:     The full version of Xcode (not just Command Line Tools) is also required to build Envoy on macOS.\\n133:     Envoy compiles and passes tests with the version of clang installed by Xcode 11.1:\\n134:     Apple clang version 11.0.0 (clang-1100.0.33.8).\\n135: \\n136:     #### Troubleshooting\\n137:     If you see some error messages like the following:\\n138:     ```console\\n139:     xcrun: error: SDK \\\"macosx12.1\\\" cannot be located\\n140:     xcrun: error: SDK \\\"macosx12.1\\\" cannot be located\\n141:     xcrun: error: unable to lookup item 'Path' in SDK 'macosx12.1'\\n142:     ```\\n143:     please check the installed sdk version.\\n144:     ```console\\n145:     xcrun --show-sdk-version\\n146:     ```\\n147: \\n148:     If the sdk version is lower than the one in the error message, upgrade your Command Line Tools using the following commands:\\n149:     ```console\\n150:     sudo rm -rf /Library/Developer/CommandLineTools\\n151:     softwareupdate --all --install --force\\n152:     sudo xcode-select --install\\n153:     ```\\n154: \\n155:     If the following error occurs during the compilation process:\\n156:     ```console\\n157:     xcode-select: error: tool 'xcodebuild' requires Xcode, but active developer directory '/Library/Developer/CommandLineTools' is a command line tools instance\\n158:     ```\\n159:     please execute the following command and retry:\\n160:     ```console\\n161:     sudo xcode-select -s /Applications/Xcode.app/Contents/Developer\\n162:     ```\\n163: \\n164:     Having the binutils keg installed in Brew is known to cause issues due to putting an incompatible\\n165:     version of `ar` on the PATH, so if you run into issues building third party code like luajit\\n166:     consider uninstalling binutils.\\n167: \\n168:     ### Windows\\n169: \\n170:     > Note: These instructions apply to **Windows 10 SDK, version 1803 (10.0.17134.12)**. Earlier versions will not compile because the `afunix.h` header is not available. **The recommended Windows version is equal or later than Windows 10 SDK, version 1903 (10.0.18362.1)**\\n171: \\n172:     Install bazelisk in the PATH using the `bazel.exe` executable name as described above in the first section.\\n173: \\n174:     When building Envoy, Bazel creates very long path names. One way to work around these excessive path\\n175:     lengths is to change the output base directory for bazel to a very short root path. An example Bazel configuration\\n176:     to help with this is to use `C:\\\\_eb` as the bazel base path. This and other preferences should be set up by placing\\n177:     the following bazelrc configuration line in a system `%ProgramData%\\\\bazel.bazelrc` file or the individual\\n178:     user's `%USERPROFILE%\\\\.bazelrc` file (rather than including it on every bazel command line):\\n179: \\n180:     ```\\n181:     startup --output_base=C:/_eb\\n182:     ```\\n183: \\n184:     Another option to shorten the output root for Bazel is to set the `USERNAME` environment variable in your shell\\n185:     session to a short value. Bazel uses this value when constructing its output root path if no explicit `--output_base`\\n186:     is set.\\n187: \\n188:     Bazel also creates file symlinks when building Envoy. It's strongly recommended to enable file symlink support\\n189:     using [Bazel's instructions](https://docs.bazel.build/versions/master/windows.html#enable-symlink-support).\\n190:     For other common issues, see the\\n191:     [Using Bazel on Windows](https://docs.bazel.build/versions/master/windows.html) page.\\n192: \\n193:     > The paths in this document are given as\\n194:     examples, make sure to verify you are using the correct paths for your environment. Also note\\n195:     that these examples assume using a `cmd.exe` shell to set environment variables etc., be sure\\n196:     to do the equivalent if using a different shell.\\n197: \\n198:     [python3](https://www.python.org/downloads/): Specifically, the Windows-native flavor distributed\\n199:     by python.org. The POSIX flavor available via MSYS2, the Windows Store flavor and other distributions\\n200:     will not work. Add a symlink for `python3.exe` pointing to the installed `python.exe` for Envoy scripts\\n201:     and Bazel rules which follow POSIX python conventions. Add `pip.exe` to the PATH and install the `wheel`\\n202:     package.\\n203:     ```cmd\\n204:     mklink %USERPROFILE%\\\\Python39\\\\python3.exe %USERPROFILE%\\\\Python39\\\\python.exe\\n205:     set PATH=%USERPROFILE%\\\\Python39;%PATH%\\n206:     set PATH=%USERPROFILE%\\\\Python39\\\\Scripts;%PATH%\\n207:     pip install wheel\\n208:     ```\\n209: \\n210:     [Build Tools for Visual Studio 2019](https://visualstudio.microsoft.com/downloads/#build-tools-for-visual-studio-2019):\\n211:     For building with MSVC, you must install at least the VC++ workload.\\n212:     You may alternately install the entire Visual Studio 2019 and use the Build Tools installed in that\\n213:     package. Earlier versions of VC++ Build Tools/Visual Studio are not recommended or supported.\\n214:     If installed in a non-standard filesystem location, be sure to set the `BAZEL_VC` environment variable\\n215:     to the path of the VC++ package to allow Bazel to find your installation of VC++. NOTE: ensure that\\n216:     the `link.exe` that resolves on your PATH is from VC++ Build Tools and not `/usr/bin/link.exe` from MSYS2,\\n217:     which is determined by their relative ordering in your PATH.\\n218:     ```cmd\\n219:     set BAZEL_VC=%USERPROFILE%\\\\VSBT2019\\\\VC\\n220:     set PATH=%USERPROFILE%\\\\VSBT2019\\\\VC\\\\Tools\\\\MSVC\\\\14.26.28801\\\\bin\\\\Hostx64\\\\x64;%PATH%\\n221:     ```\\n222: \\n223:     The Windows SDK contains header files and libraries you need when building Windows applications. Bazel always uses the latest, but you can specify a different version by setting the environment variable `BAZEL_WINSDK_FULL_VERSION`. See [bazel/windows](https://docs.bazel.build/versions/master/windows.html)\\n224: \\n225:     [MSYS2 shell](https://msys2.github.io/): Install to a path with no spaces, e.g. C:\\\\msys64.\\n226: \\n227:     Set the `BAZEL_SH` environment variable to the path of the installed MSYS2 `bash.exe`\\n228:     executable. Additionally, setting the `MSYS2_ARG_CONV_EXCL` environment variable to a value\\n229:     of `*` is often advisable to ensure argument parsing in the MSYS2 shell behaves as expected.\\n230:     ```cmd\\n231:     set PATH=%USERPROFILE%\\\\msys64\\\\usr\\\\bin;%PATH%\\n232:     set BAZEL_SH=%USERPROFILE%\\\\msys64\\\\usr\\\\bin\\\\bash.exe\\n233:     set MSYS2_ARG_CONV_EXCL=*\\n234:     set MSYS2_PATH_TYPE=inherit\\n235:     ```\\n236: \\n237:     Set the `TMPDIR` environment variable to a path usable as a temporary directory (e.g.\\n238:     `C:\\\\Windows\\\\TEMP`), and create a directory symlink `C:\\\\c` to `C:\\\\`, so that the MSYS2\\n239:     path `/c/Windows/TEMP` is equivalent to the Windows path `C:/Windows/TEMP`:\\n240:     ```cmd\\n241:     set TMPDIR=C:/Windows/TEMP\\n242:     mklink /d C:\\\\c C:\\\\\\n243:     ```\\n244: \\n245:     The TMPDIR path and MSYS2 `mktemp` command are used frequently by the `rules_foreign_cc`\\n246:     component of Bazel as well as Envoy's test scripts, causing problems if not set to a path\\n247:     accessible to both Windows and msys commands. [Note the `ci/windows_ci_steps.sh` script\\n248:     which builds envoy and run tests in CI creates this symlink automatically.]\\n249: \\n250:     In the MSYS2 shell, install additional packages via pacman:\\n251:     ```\\n252:     pacman -S diffutils patch unzip zip\\n253:     ```\\n254: \\n255:     [Git](https://git-scm.com/downloads): This version from the Git project, or the version\\n256:     distributed using pacman under MSYS2 will both work, ensure one is on the PATH:.\\n257:     ```cmd\\n258:     set PATH=%USERPROFILE%\\\\Git\\\\bin;%PATH%\\n259:     ```\\n260: \\n261:     Lastly, persist environment variable changes.\\n262:     ``` cmd\\n263:     setx PATH \\\"%PATH%\\\"\\n264:     setx BAZEL_SH \\\"%BAZEL_SH%\\\"\\n265:     setx MSYS2_ARG_CONV_EXCL \\\"%MSYS2_ARG_CONV_EXCL%\\\"\\n266:     setx BAZEL_VC \\\"%BAZEL_VC%\\\"\\n267:     setx TMPDIR \\\"%TMPDIR%\\\"\\n268:     setx MSYS2_PATH_TYPE \\\"%MSYS2_PATH_TYPE%\\\"\\n269:     ```\\n270:     > On Windows the supported/recommended shell to interact with bazel is MSYS2. This means that all the bazel commands (i.e. build, test) should be executed from MSYS2.\\n271: \\n272: 1. Install Golang on your machine. This is required as part of building [BoringSSL](https://boringssl.googlesource.com/boringssl/+/HEAD/BUILDING.md)\\n273:    and also for [Buildifer](https://github.com/bazelbuild/buildtools) which is used for formatting bazel BUILD files.\\n274:    Make sure you have go version 1.17 or later.\\n275: 1. `go install github.com/bazelbuild/buildtools/buildifier@latest` to install buildifier. You may need to set `BUILDIFIER_BIN` to `$GOPATH/bin/buildifier`\\n276:    in your shell for buildifier to work. If GOPATH is not set, it is $HOME/go by default.\\n277: 1. `go install github.com/bazelbuild/buildtools/buildozer@latest` to install buildozer. You may need to set `BUILDOZER_BIN` to `$GOPATH/bin/buildozer`\\n278:    in your shell for buildozer to work. If GOPATH is not set, it is $HOME/go by default.\\n279: 1. `bazel build envoy` from the Envoy source directory. Add `-c opt` for an optimized release build or\\n280:    `-c dbg` for an unoptimized, fully instrumented debugging build.\\n281: \\n282: ## Building Envoy with the CI Docker image\\n283: \\n284: Envoy can also be built with the Docker image used for CI, by installing Docker and executing the following.\\n285: \\n286: On Linux, run:\\n287: \\n288: ```\\n289: ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh dev'\\n290: ```\\n291: \\n292: From a Windows host with Docker installed, the Windows containers feature enabled, and bash (installed via\\n293: MSYS2 or Git bash), run:\\n294: \\n295: **Note: the command below executes the whole Windows CI and unlike Linux you are not able to set specific build targets. You can modify `./ci/windows_ci_steps.sh` to modify `bazel` arguments, tests to run, etc. as well as set environment variables to adjust your container build environment.**\\n296: \\n297: ```\\n298: ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/windows_ci_steps.sh'\\n299: ```\\n300: \\n301: See also the [documentation](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/tree/main/ci) for developer use of the\\n302: CI Docker image.\\n303: \\n304: ## Building Envoy with Remote Execution\\n305: \\n306: Envoy can also be built with Bazel [Remote Execution](https://docs.bazel.build/versions/master/remote-execution.html),\\n307: part of the CI is running with the hosted [GCP RBE](https://blog.bazel.build/2018/10/05/remote-build-execution.html) service.\\n308: \\n309: To build Envoy with a remote build services, run Bazel with your remote build service flags and with `--config=remote-clang`.\\n310: For example the following command runs build with the GCP RBE service used in CI:\\n311: \\n312: ```\\n313: bazel build envoy --config=remote-clang \\\\\\n314:     --remote_cache=grpcs://remotebuildexecution.googleapis.com \\\\\\n315:     --remote_executor=grpcs://remotebuildexecution.googleapis.com \\\\\\n316:     --remote_instance_name=projects/envoy-ci/instances/default_instance\\n317: ```\\n318: \\n319: Change the value of `--remote_cache`, `--remote_executor` and `--remote_instance_name` for your remote build services. Tests can\\n320: be run in remote execution too.\\n321: \\n322: Note: Currently the test run configuration in `.bazelrc` doesn't download test binaries and test logs,\\n323: to override the behavior set [`--remote_download_outputs`](https://docs.bazel.build/versions/master/command-line-reference.html#flag--remote_download_outputs)\\n324: accordingly.\\n325: \\n326: ## Building Envoy with Docker sandbox\\n327: \\n328: Building Envoy with Docker sandbox uses the same Docker image used in CI with fixed C++ toolchain configuration. It produces more consistent\\n329: output which is not depending on your local C++ toolchain. It can also help debugging issues with RBE. To build Envoy with Docker sandbox:\\n330: \\n331: ```\\n332: bazel build envoy --config=docker-clang\\n333: ```\\n334: \\n335: Tests can be run in docker sandbox too. Note that the network environment, such as IPv6, may be different in the docker sandbox so you may want\\n336: set different options. See below to configure test IP versions.\\n337: \\n338: ## Linking against libc++ on Linux\\n339: \\n340: To link Envoy against libc++, follow the [quick start](#quick-start-bazel-build-for-developers) to setup Clang+LLVM and run:\\n341: ```\\n342: bazel build --config=libc++ envoy\\n343: ```\\n344: \\n345: Or use our configuration with Remote Execution or Docker sandbox, pass `--config=remote-clang-libc++` or\\n346: `--config=docker-clang-libc++` respectively.\\n347: \\n348: If you want to make libc++ as default, add a line `build --config=libc++` to the `user.bazelrc` file in Envoy source root.\\n349: \\n350: ## Using a compiler toolchain in a non-standard location\\n351: \\n352: By setting the `CC` and `LD_LIBRARY_PATH` in the environment that Bazel executes from as\\n353: appropriate, an arbitrary compiler toolchain and standard library location can be specified. One\\n354: slight caveat is that (at the time of writing), Bazel expects the binutils in `$(dirname $CC)` to be\\n355: unprefixed, e.g. `as` instead of `x86_64-linux-gnu-as`.\\n356: \\n357: Note: this configuration currently doesn't work with Remote Execution or Docker sandbox, you have to generate a\\n358: custom toolchains configuration for them. See [bazelbuild/bazel-toolchains](https://github.com/bazelbuild/bazel-toolchains)\\n359: for more details.\\n360: \\n361: ## Supported compiler versions\\n362: \\n363: We now require Clang >= 9 due to C++17 support and tcmalloc requirement. GCC >= 9 is also known to work.\\n364: Currently the CI is running with Clang 14.\\n365: \\n366: ## Clang STL debug symbols\\n367: \\n368: By default Clang drops some debug symbols that are required for pretty printing to work correctly.\\n369: More information can be found [here](https://bugs.llvm.org/show_bug.cgi?id=24202). The easy solution\\n370: is to set ```--copt=-fno-limit-debug-info``` on the CLI or in your .bazelrc file.\\n371: \\n372: ## Removing debug info\\n373: \\n374: If you don't want your debug or release binaries to contain debug info\\n375: to reduce binary size, pass `--define=no_debug_info=1` when building.\\n376: This is primarily useful when building envoy as a static library. When\\n377: building a linked envoy binary you can build the implicit `.stripped`\\n378: target from [`cc_binary`](https://docs.bazel.build/versions/master/be/c-cpp.html#cc_binary)\\n379: or pass [`--strip=always`](https://docs.bazel.build/versions/master/command-line-reference.html#flag--strip)\\n380: instead.\\n381: \\n382: # Running the built Envoy binary on the host system\\n383: \\n384: After Envoy is built, it can be executed via CLI.\\n385: \\n386: For example, if Envoy was built using the `bazel build -c opt //source/exe:envoy-static` command, then it can be executed from the project's root directory by running:\\n387: \\n388: ```console\\n389: $(bazel info bazel-genfiles)/source/exe/envoy-static --config-path /path/to/your/envoy/config.yaml\\n390: ```\\n391: \\n392: # Testing Envoy with Bazel\\n393: \\n394: All the Envoy tests can be built and run with:\\n395: \\n396: ```\\n397: bazel test //test/...\\n398: ```\\n399: \\n400: An individual test target can be run with a more specific Bazel\\n401: [label](https://bazel.build/versions/master/docs/build-ref.html#Labels), e.g. to build and run only\\n402: the units tests in\\n403: [test/common/http/async_client_impl_test.cc](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/test/common/http/async_client_impl_test.cc):\\n404: \\n405: ```\\n406: bazel test //test/common/http:async_client_impl_test\\n407: ```\\n408: \\n409: To observe more verbose test output:\\n410: \\n411: ```\\n412: bazel test --test_output=streamed //test/common/http:async_client_impl_test\\n413: ```\\n414: \\n415: It's also possible to pass into an Envoy test additional command-line args via `--test_arg`. For\\n416: example, for extremely verbose test debugging:\\n417: \\n418: ```\\n419: bazel test --test_output=streamed //test/common/http:async_client_impl_test --test_arg=\\\"-l trace\\\"\\n420: ```\\n421: \\n422: By default, testing exercises both IPv4 and IPv6 address connections. In IPv4 or IPv6 only\\n423: environments, set the environment variable ENVOY_IP_TEST_VERSIONS to \\\"v4only\\\" or\\n424: \\\"v6only\\\", respectively.\\n425: \\n426: ```\\n427: bazel test //test/... --test_env=ENVOY_IP_TEST_VERSIONS=v4only\\n428: bazel test //test/... --test_env=ENVOY_IP_TEST_VERSIONS=v6only\\n429: ```\\n430: \\n431: By default, tests are run with the [gperftools](https://github.com/gperftools/gperftools) heap\\n432: checker enabled in \\\"normal\\\" mode to detect leaks. For other mode options, see the gperftools\\n433: heap checker [documentation](https://gperftools.github.io/gperftools/heap_checker.html). To\\n434: disable the heap checker or change the mode, set the HEAPCHECK environment variable:\\n435: \\n436: ```\\n437: # Disables the heap checker\\n438: bazel test //test/... --test_env=HEAPCHECK=\\n439: # Changes the heap checker to \\\"minimal\\\" mode\\n440: bazel test //test/... --test_env=HEAPCHECK=minimal\\n441: ```\\n442: \\n443: If you see a leak detected, by default the reported offsets will require `addr2line` interpretation.\\n444: You can run under `--config=clang-asan` to have this automatically applied.\\n445: \\n446: Bazel will by default cache successful test results. To force it to rerun tests:\\n447: \\n448: ```\\n449: bazel test //test/common/http:async_client_impl_test --cache_test_results=no\\n450: ```\\n451: \\n452: Bazel will by default run all tests inside a sandbox, which disallows access to the\\n453: local filesystem. If you need to break out of the sandbox (for example to run under a\\n454: local script or tool with [`--run_under`](https://docs.bazel.build/versions/master/user-manual.html#flag--run_under)),\\n455: you can run the test with `--strategy=TestRunner=local`, e.g.:\\n456: \\n457: ```\\n458: bazel test //test/common/http:async_client_impl_test --strategy=TestRunner=local --run_under=/some/path/foobar.sh\\n459: ```\\n460: # Stack trace symbol resolution\\n461: \\n462: Envoy can produce backtraces on demand and from assertions and other fatal\\n463: actions like segfaults. Where supported, stack traces will contain resolved\\n464: symbols, though not include line numbers. On systems where absl::Symbolization is\\n465: not supported, the stack traces written in the log or to stderr contain addresses rather\\n466: than resolved symbols. If the symbols were resolved, the address is also included at\\n467: the end of the line.\\n468: \\n469: The `tools/stack_decode.py` script exists to process the output and do additional symbol\\n470: resolution including file names and line numbers. It requires the `addr2line` program be\\n471: installed and in your path. Any log lines not relevant to the backtrace capability are\\n472: passed through the script unchanged (it acts like a filter). File and line information\\n473: is appended to the stack trace lines.\\n474: \\n475: The script runs in one of two modes. To process log input from stdin, pass `-s` as the first\\n476: argument, followed by the executable file path. You can postprocess a log or pipe the output\\n477: of an Envoy process. If you do not specify the `-s` argument it runs the arguments as a child\\n478: process. This enables you to run a test with backtrace post processing. Bazel sandboxing must\\n479: be disabled by specifying local execution. Example command line with\\n480: `run_under`:\\n481: \\n482: ```\\n483: bazel test -c dbg //test/server:backtrace_test\\n484: --run_under=//tools:stack_decode --strategy=TestRunner=local\\n485: --cache_test_results=no --test_output=all\\n486: ```\\n487: \\n488: Example using input on stdin:\\n489: \\n490: ```\\n491: bazel test -c dbg //test/server:backtrace_test --cache_test_results=no --test_output=streamed |& tools/stack_decode.py -s bazel-bin/test/server/backtrace_test\\n492: ```\\n493: \\n494: You will need to use either a `dbg` build type or the `opt` build type to get file and line\\n495: symbol information in the binaries.\\n496: \\n497: By default main.cc will install signal handlers to print backtraces at the\\n498: location where a fatal signal occurred. The signal handler will re-raise the\\n499: fatal signal with the default handler so a core file will still be dumped after\\n500: the stack trace is logged. To inhibit this behavior use\\n501: `--define=signal_trace=disabled` on the Bazel command line. No signal handlers will\\n502: be installed.\\n503: \\n504: # Running a single Bazel test under GDB\\n505: \\n506: ```\\n507: bazel build -c dbg //test/common/http:async_client_impl_test\\n508: bazel build -c dbg //test/common/http:async_client_impl_test.dwp\\n509: gdb bazel-bin/test/common/http/async_client_impl_test\\n510: ```\\n511: \\n512: We need to use `-c dbg` Bazel option to generate debugging symbols and without\\n513: that GDB will not be very useful. The debugging symbols are stored as separate\\n514: debugging information files (`.dwp` files) and we can build a DWARF package file\\n515: with `.dwp ` target. The `.dwp` file need to be presented in the same folder with the\\n516: binary for a full debugging experience.\\n517: \\n518: # Running Bazel tests requiring privileges\\n519: \\n520: Some tests may require privileges (e.g. CAP_NET_ADMIN) in order to execute. One option is to run\\n521: them with elevated privileges, e.g. `sudo test`. However, that may not always be possible,\\n522: particularly if the test needs to run in a CI pipeline. `tools/bazel-test-docker.sh` may be used in\\n523: such situations to run the tests in a privileged docker container.\\n524: \\n525: The script works by wrapping the test execution in the current repository's circle ci build\\n526: container, then executing it either locally or on a remote docker container. In both cases, the\\n527: container runs with the `--privileged` flag, allowing it to execute operations which would otherwise\\n528: be restricted.\\n529: \\n530: The command line format is:\\n531: `tools/bazel-test-docker.sh <bazel-test-target> [optional-flags-to-bazel]`\\n532: \\n533: The script uses two optional environment variables to control its behaviour:\\n534: \\n535: * `RUN_REMOTE=<yes|no>`: chooses whether to run on a remote docker server.\\n536: * `LOCAL_MOUNT=<yes|no>`: copy/mount local libraries onto the docker container.\\n537: \\n538: Use `RUN_REMOTE=yes` when you don't want to run against your local docker instance. Note that you\\n539: will need to override a few environment variables to set up the remote docker. The list of variables\\n540: can be found in the [Documentation](https://docs.docker.com/engine/reference/commandline/cli/).\\n541: \\n542: Use `LOCAL_MOUNT=yes` when you are not building with the Envoy build container. {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_0159zVPLMrs7v5bJh1nDaRCK","type":"tool_result","content":"{\"content\":\"1: # Envoy tests\\n2: \\n3: Envoy uses the [Google Test framework](https://github.com/google/googletest) for\\n4: tests, including\\n5: [Google Mock](https://github.com/google/googletest/blob/master/googlemock/README.md) for\\n6: mocks and matchers. See the documentation on those pages for information on the\\n7: various classes, macros, and matchers that Envoy uses from those frameworks.\\n8: \\n9: ## Integration tests\\n10: \\n11: Envoy contains an integration testing framework, for testing\\n12: downstream-Envoy-upstream communication.\\n13: [See the framework's README for more information.](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/test/integration/README.md)\\n14: \\n15: ## Custom matchers\\n16: \\n17: Envoy includes some custom Google Mock matchers to make test expectation\\n18: statements simpler to write and easier to understand.\\n19: \\n20: ### HeaderValueOf\\n21: \\n22: Tests that a HeaderMap argument contains exactly one header with the given key,\\n23: whose value satisfies the given expectation. The expectation can be a matcher,\\n24: or a string that the value should equal.\\n25: \\n26: Examples:\\n27: \\n28: ```cpp\\n29: EXPECT_THAT(response->headers(), HeaderValueOf(Headers::get().Server, \\\"envoy\\\"));\\n30: ```\\n31: \\n32: ```cpp\\n33: using testing::HasSubstr;\\n34: EXPECT_THAT(request->headers(),\\n35:             HeaderValueOf(Headers::get().AcceptEncoding, HasSubstr(\\\"gzip\\\")));\\n36: ```\\n37: \\n38: ### HttpStatusIs\\n39: \\n40: Tests that a HeaderMap argument has the provided HTTP status code. The status\\n41: code can be passed in as a string or an integer.\\n42: \\n43: Example:\\n44: \\n45: ```cpp\\n46: EXPECT_THAT(response->headers(), HttpStatusIs(\\\"200\\\"));\\n47: ```\\n48: \\n49: ### HeaderMapEqual and HeaderMapEqualRef\\n50: \\n51: `HeaderMapEqualRef` tests that two `HeaderMap` arguments are equal.\\n52: `HeaderMapEqual` is the same, but it compares two pointers to `HeaderMap`s, and\\n53: the matcher's argument must be a `HeaderMapPtr`.\\n54: \\n55: Example:\\n56: \\n57: ```cpp\\n58: EXPECT_THAT(response->headers(), HeaderMapEqualRef(expected_headers));\\n59: ```\\n60: \\n61: ### ProtoEq, ProtoEqIgnoringField, RepeatedProtoEq\\n62: \\n63: Tests equality of protobufs, with a variant that ignores the value (including\\n64: presence) of a single named field. Another variant can be used to compare two\\n65: instances of Protobuf::RepeatedPtrField element-by-element.\\n66: \\n67: Example:\\n68: \\n69: ```cpp\\n70: envoy::service::discovery::v3::DeltaDiscoveryRequest expected_request;\\n71: // (not shown: set some fields of expected_request...)\\n72: EXPECT_CALL(async_stream_, sendMessage(ProtoEqIgnoringField(expected_request, \\\"response_nonce\\\"), false));\\n73: \\n74: response->mutable_resources()->Add();\\n75: response->mutable_resources()->Add();\\n76: response->mutable_resources()->Add();\\n77: // (not shown: do something to populate those empty added items...)\\n78: EXPECT_CALL(callbacks_, onConfigUpdate(RepeatedProtoEq(response->resources()), version));\\n79: ```\\n80: \\n81: ### IsSubsetOfHeaders and IsSupersetOfHeaders\\n82: \\n83: Tests that one `HeaderMap` argument contains every header in another\\n84: `HeaderMap`.\\n85: \\n86: Examples:\\n87: \\n88: ```cpp\\n89: EXPECT_THAT(response->headers(), IsSubsetOfHeaders(allowed_headers));\\n90: EXPECT_THAT(response->headers(), IsSupersetOfHeaders(required_headers));\\n91: ```\\n92: \\n93: ## Controlling time in tests\\n94: \\n95: In Envoy production code, time and timers are managed via\\n96: [`Event::TimeSystem`](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/include/envoy/event/timer.h),\\n97: which provides a mechanism for querying the time and setting up time-based\\n98: callbacks. Bypassing this abstraction in Envoy code is flagged as a format\\n99: violation in CI.\\n100: \\n101: In tests we use a derivation\\n102: [`Event::TestTimeSystem`](test_common/test_time_system.h) which adds the ability\\n103: to sleep or do a blocking timed wait on a condition variable. There are two\\n104: implementations of the `Event::TestTimeSystem` interface:\\n105: `Event::TestRealTimeSystem`, and `Event::SimulatedTimeSystem`. The latter is\\n106: recommended for all new tests, as it helps avoid flaky tests on slow machines,\\n107: and makes tests run faster.\\n108: \\n109: Typically we do not want to have both real-time and simulated-time in the same\\n110: test; that could lead to hard-to-reproduce results. Thus both implementations\\n111: have a mechanism to enforce that only one of them can be instantiated at once.\\n112: A runtime assertion occurs if an `Event::TestRealTimeSystem` and\\n113: `Event::SimulatedTimeSystem` are instantiated at the same time. Once the\\n114: time-system goes out of scope, usually at the end of a test method, the slate\\n115: is clean and a new test-method can use a different time system.\\n116: \\n117: There is also `Event::GlobalTimeSystem`, which can be instantiated in shared\\n118: test infrastructure that wants to be agnostic to which `TimeSystem` is used in a\\n119: test. When no `TimeSystem` is instantiated in a test, the `Event::GlobalTimeSystem`\\n120: will lazy-initialize itself into a concrete `TimeSystem`. Currently this is\\n121: `TestRealTimeSystem` but will be changed in the future to `SimulatedTimeSystem`.\\n122: \\n123: \\n124: ## Benchmark tests\\n125: \\n126: Envoy uses [Google Benchmark](https://github.com/google/benchmark/) for\\n127: microbenchmarks. There are custom bazel rules, `envoy_cc_benchmark_binary` and\\n128: `envoy_benchmark_test`, to execute them locally and in CI environments\\n129: respectively. `envoy_benchmark_test` rules call the benchmark binary from a\\n130: [script](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/bazel/test_for_benchmark_wrapper.sh)\\n131: which runs the benchmark with a minimal number of iterations and skipping\\n132: expensive benchmarks to quickly verify that the binary is able to run to\\n133: completion. In order to collect meaningful bechmarks, `bazel run -c opt` the\\n134: benchmark binary target on a quiescent machine.\\n135: \\n136: If you would like to detect when your benchmark test is running under the\\n137: wrapper, call\\n138: [`Envoy::benchmark::skipExpensiveBechmarks()`](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/test/benchmark/main.h).\\n139: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/envoy--v1.32.1@b35dd17bea856e19fc4e65fb05e68170841d3726/-/blob/test/README.md\"}"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"e91147b7-778e-4396-9da9-831fcb6d3019","uuid":"1d2a6646-b9a4-4370-8f09-4376ec34396a","tool_use_result":{"content":"{\"content\":\"1: # Envoy tests\\n2: \\n3: Envoy uses the [Google Test framework](https://github.com/google/googletest) for\\n4: tests, including\\n5: [Google Mock](https://github.com/google/googletest/blob/master/googlemock/README.md) for\\n6: mocks and matchers. The expectation can be a matcher,\n24: or a string that the value should equal.\n25: \n26: Examples:\n27: \n28: ```cpp\n29: EXPECT_THAT(response->headers(), HeaderValueOf(Headers::get().Server, \"envoy\"));\n30: ```\n31: \n32: ```cpp\n33: using testing::HasSubstr;\n34: EXPECT_THAT(request->headers(),\n35:             HeaderValueOf(Headers::get().AcceptEncoding, HasSubstr(\"gzip\")));\n36: ```\n37: \n38: ### HttpStatusIs\n39: \n40: Tests that a HeaderMap argument has the provided HTTP status code. The status\n41: code can be passed in as a string or an integer.\n42: \n43: Example:\n44: \n45: ```cpp\n46: EXPECT_THAT(response->headers(), HttpStatusIs(\"200\"));\n47: ```\n48: \n49: ### HeaderMapEqual and HeaderMapEqualRef\n50: \n51: `HeaderMapEqualRef` tests that two `HeaderMap` arguments are equal.\n52: `HeaderMapEqual` is the same, but it compares two pointers to `HeaderMap`s, and\n53: the matcher's argument must be a `HeaderMapPtr`.\n54: \n55: Example:\n56: \n57: ```cpp\n58: EXPECT_THAT(response->headers(), HeaderMapEqualRef(expected_headers));\n59: ```\n60: \n61: ### ProtoEq, ProtoEqIgnoringField, RepeatedProtoEq\n62: \n63: Tests equality of protobufs, with a variant that ignores the value (including\n64: presence) of a single named field. Another variant can be used to compare two\n65: instances of Protobuf::RepeatedPtrField element-by-element.\n66: \n67: Example:\n68: \n69: ```cpp\n70: envoy::service::discovery::v3::DeltaDiscoveryRequest expected_request;\n71: // (not shown: set some fields of expected_request...)\n72: EXPECT_CALL(async_stream_, sendMessage(ProtoEqIgnoringField(expected_request, \"response_nonce\"), false));\n73: \n74: response->mutable_resources()->Add();\n75: response->mutable_resources()->Add();\n76: response->mutable_resources()->Add();\n77: // (not shown: do something to populate those empty added items...)\n78: EXPECT_CALL(callbacks_, onConfigUpdate(RepeatedProtoEq(response->resources()), version));\n79: ```\n80: \n81: ### IsSubsetOfHeaders and IsSupersetOfHeaders\n82: \n83: Tests that one `HeaderMap` argument contains every header in another\n84: `HeaderMap`.\n85: \n86: Examples:\n87: \n88: ```cpp\n89: EXPECT_THAT(response->headers(), IsSubsetOfHeaders(allowed_headers));\n90: EXPECT_THAT(response->headers(), IsSupersetOfHeaders(required_headers));\n91: ```\n92: \n93: ## Controlling time in tests\n94: \n95: In Envoy production code, time and timers are managed via\n96: [`Event::TimeSystem`](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/include/envoy/event/timer.h),\n97: which provides a mechanism for querying the time and setting up time-based\n98: callbacks. Bypassing this abstraction in Envoy code is flagged as a format\n99: violation in CI.\n100: \n101: In tests we use a derivation\n102: [`Event::TestTimeSystem`](test_common/test_time_system.h) which adds the ability\n103: to sleep or do a blocking timed wait on a condition variable. There are two\n104: implementations of the `Event::TestTimeSystem` interface:\n105: `Event::TestRealTimeSystem`, and `Event::SimulatedTimeSystem`. The latter is\n106: recommended for all new tests, as it helps avoid flaky tests on slow machines,\n107: and makes tests run faster.\n108: \n109: Typically we do not want to have both real-time and simulated-time in the same\n110: test; that could lead to hard-to-reproduce results. Thus both implementations\n111: have a mechanism to enforce that only one of them can be instantiated at once.\n112: A runtime assertion occurs if an `Event::TestRealTimeSystem` and\n113: `Event::SimulatedTimeSystem` are instantiated at the same time. Once the\n114: time-system goes out of scope, usually at the end of a test method, the slate\n115: is clean and a new test-method can use a different time system.\n116: \n117: There is also `Event::GlobalTimeSystem`, which can be instantiated in shared\n118: test infrastructure that wants to be agnostic to which `TimeSystem` is used in a\n119: test. When no `TimeSystem` is instantiated in a test, the `Event::GlobalTimeSystem`\n120: will lazy-initialize itself into a concrete `TimeSystem`. Currently this is\n121: `TestRealTimeSystem` but will be changed in the future to `SimulatedTimeSystem`.\n122: \n123: \n124: ## Benchmark tests\n125: \n126: Envoy uses [Google Benchmark](https://github.com/google/benchmark/) for\n127: microbenchmarks. There are custom bazel rules, `envoy_cc_benchmark_binary` and\n128: `envoy_benchmark_test`, to execute them locally and in CI environments\n129: respectively. `envoy_benchmark_test` rules call the benchmark binary from a\n130: [script](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/bazel/test_for_benchmark_wrapper.sh)\n131: which runs the benchmark with a minimal number of iterations and skipping\n132: expensive benchmarks to quickly verify that the binary is able to run to\n133: completion. In order to collect meaningful bechmarks, `bazel run -c opt` the\n134: benchmark binary target on a quiescent machine.\n135: \n136: If you would like to detect when your benchmark test is running under the\n137: wrapper, call\n138: [`Envoy::benchmark::skipExpensiveBechmarks()`](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/test/benchmark/main.h).\n139: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/envoy--v1.32.1@b35dd17bea856e19fc4e65fb05e68170841d3726/-/blob/test/README.md"}}}
