Developers\\n10: may work with the latest build image SHA in [envoy-build-tools](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy-build-tools/blob/main/toolchains/rbe_toolchains_config.bzl#L8)\\n11: repo to provide a self-contained environment for building Envoy binaries and running tests that reflects the latest built Ubuntu Envoy image.\\n12: Moreover, the Docker image at [`envoyproxy/envoy:dev-<hash>`](https://hub.docker.com/r/envoyproxy/envoy/tags?name=dev) is an image that has an Envoy binary at `/usr/local/bin/envoy`.\\n13: The `<hash>` corresponds to the main commit at which the binary was compiled. Lastly, `envoyproxy/envoy:dev` contains an Envoy\\n14: binary built from the latest tip of main that passed tests.\\n15: \\n16: ## Distroless Envoy image\\n17: \\n18: Minimal images based on a [distroless](https://github.com/GoogleContainerTools/distroless) allow for quicker deployment of Envoy.\\n19: \\n20: The Distroless base image is only built with symbols stripped.\\n21: \\n22: ## Debug Envoy image\\n23: \\n24: To get the binary with symbols, use the corresponding Ubuntu based debug image. The image is pushed with two different tags:\\n25: `<hash>` and `latest`. Parallel to the Ubuntu images above, `<hash>` corresponds to the\\n26: main commit at which the binary was compiled, and `latest` corresponds to a binary built from the latest tip of main that passed tests.\\n27: \\n28: ## Windows 2019 Envoy image\\n29: \\n30: On August 31, 2023 the Envoy project ended official Windows support due to a lack of resources.\\n31: We will continue to accept patches related to the Windows build. Until further notice, Windows\\n32: builds are excluded from Envoy CI, as well as the Envoy release and security processes.\\n33: \\n34: The Windows 2019 based Envoy Docker image at [`envoyproxy/envoy-build-windows2019:<hash>`](https://hub.docker.com/r/envoyproxy/envoy-build-windows2019/)\\n35: is used for CI checks, where `<hash>` is specified in [`envoy_build_sha.sh`](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/ci/envoy_build_sha.sh).\\n36: Developers may work with the most recent `envoyproxy/envoy-build-windows2019` image to provide a self-contained environment for building Envoy binaries and\\n37: running tests that reflects the latest built Windows 2019 Envoy image.\\n38: \\n39: # Build image base and compiler versions\\n40: \\n41: Currently there are three build images for Linux and one for Windows:\\n42: \\n43: * `envoyproxy/envoy-build` &mdash; alias to `envoyproxy/envoy-build-ubuntu`.\\n44: * `envoyproxy/envoy-build-ubuntu` &mdash; based on Ubuntu 20.04 (Focal) with GCC 9 and Clang 14 compiler.\\n45: * `envoyproxy/envoy-build-centos` &mdash; based on CentOS 7 with GCC 9 and Clang 14 compiler, this image is experimental and not well tested.\\n46: * `envoyproxy/envoy-build-windows2019` &mdash; based on Windows ltsc2019 with VS 2019 Build Tools, as well as LLVM.\\n47: \\n48: The source for these images is located in the [envoyproxy/envoy-build-tools](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy-build-tools)\\n49: repository.\\n50: \\n51: We use the Clang compiler for all Linux CI runs with tests. We have an additional Linux CI run with GCC which builds binary only.\\n52: \\n53: # C++ standard library\\n54: \\n55: As of November 2019 after [#8859](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/pull/8859) the official released binary is\\n56: [linked against libc++ on Linux](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/bazel/README.md#linking-against-libc-on-linux).\\n57: To override the C++ standard library in your build, set environment variable `ENVOY_STDLIB` to `libstdc++` or `libc++` and\\n58: run `./ci/do_ci.sh` as described below.\\n59: \\n60: # Building and running tests as a developer\\n61: \\n62: The `./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh` script can be used to set up a Docker container on Linux and Windows\\n63: to build an Envoy static binary and run tests.\\n64: \\n65: The build image defaults to `envoyproxy/envoy-build-ubuntu` on Linux and\\n66: `envoyproxy/envoy-build-windows2019` on Windows, but you can choose build image by setting\\n67: `IMAGE_NAME` in the environment.\\n68: \\n69: In case your setup is behind a proxy, set `http_proxy` and `https_proxy` to the proxy servers before\\n70: invoking the build.\\n71: \\n72: ```bash\\n73: IMAGE_NAME=envoyproxy/envoy-build-ubuntu http_proxy=http://proxy.foo.com:8080 https_proxy=http://proxy.bar.com:8080 ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh <build_script_args>\\n74: ```\\n75: \\n76: Besides `http_proxy` and `https_proxy`, maybe you need to set `go_proxy` to replace the default GOPROXY in China.\\n77: \\n78: ```bash\\n79: IMAGE_NAME=envoyproxy/envoy-build-ubuntu go_proxy=https://goproxy.cn,direct http_proxy=http://proxy.foo.com:8080 https_proxy=http://proxy.bar.com:8080 ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh <build_script_args>\\n80: ```\\n81: \\n82: To force the Envoy build image to be refreshed by Docker you can set `ENVOY_DOCKER_PULL=true`.\\n83: \\n84: ```bash\\n85: ENVOY_DOCKER_PULL=true ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh <build_script_args>\\n86: ```\\n87: \\n88: \\n89: # Generating compile commands\\n90: \\n91: The `./ci/do_ci.sh` script provides a CI target that generates compile commands for clangd or other tools.\\n92: \\n93: ```bash\\n94: ENVOY_GEN_COMPDB_OPTIONS=\\\"--vscode --exclude_contrib\\\" ./ci/do_ci.sh refresh_compdb\\n95: ```\\n96: \\n97: ## On Linux\\n98: \\n99: An example basic invocation to build a developer version of the Envoy static binary (using the Bazel `fastbuild` type) is:\\n100: \\n101: ```bash\\n102: ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh dev'\\n103: ```\\n104: \\n105: The Envoy binary can be found in `/tmp/envoy-docker-build/envoy/source/exe/envoy-fastbuild` on the Docker host. You\\n106: can control this by setting `ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR` in the environment, e.g. to\\n107: generate the binary in `~/build/envoy/source/exe/envoy-fastbuild` you can run:\\n108: \\n109: ```bash\\n110: ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR=~/build ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh dev'\\n111: ```\\n112: \\n113: For a release version of the Envoy binary you can run:\\n114: \\n115: ```bash\\n116: ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh release.server_only'\\n117: ```\\n118: \\n119: The build artifact can be found in `/tmp/envoy-docker-build/envoy/source/exe/envoy` (or wherever\\n120: `$ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR` points).\\n121: \\n122: To enable the previous behavior of the `release.server_only` target where the final binary was copied to a tar.gz file\\n123: (e.g. envoy-binary.tar.gz), you can run:\\n124: \\n125:   ```bash\\n126:   ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh release.server_only.binary'\\n127:   ```\\n128: \\n129: For a debug version of the Envoy binary you can run:\\n130: \\n131: ```bash\\n132: ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh debug.server_only'\\n133: ```\\n134: \\n135: The build artifact can be found in `/tmp/envoy-docker-build/envoy/source/exe/envoy-debug` (or wherever\\n136: `$ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR` points).\\n137: \\n138: To leverage a [bazel remote cache](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/tree/main/bazel#advanced-caching-setup):\\n139: 1. add bazel options like `--remote_cache` and/or `--remote_cache_header` to a `.bazelrc` file, such as `user.bazelrc`. For example\\n140: \\n141: ```bash\\n142: build:my-remote-cache --remote_cache=grpcs://remotecache.googleapis.com\\n143: build:my-remote-cache --remote_cache_header=Authorization=\\\"Bearer <token>\\\"\\n144: ```\\n145: \\n146: 2. specify the config in the `BAZEL_BUILD_EXTRA_OPTIONS` environment variable. Run\\n147: \\n148: ```bash\\n149: export BAZEL_BUILD_EXTRA_OPTIONS=--config=my-remote-cache\\n150: ```\\n151: \\n152: The `./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh <TARGET>'` targets are:\\n153: \\n154: * `api` &mdash; build and run API tests under `-c fastbuild` with clang.\\n155: * `asan` &mdash; build and run tests under `-c dbg --config=clang-asan` with clang.\\n156: * `asan <test>` &mdash; build and run a specified test or test dir under `-c dbg --config=clang-asan` with clang.\\n157: * `debug` &mdash; build Envoy static binary and run tests under `-c dbg`.\\n158: * `debug <test>` &mdash; build Envoy static binary and run a specified test or test dir under `-c dbg`.\\n159: * `debug.server_only` &mdash; build Envoy static binary under `-c dbg`.\\n160: * `docker` &mdash; build Docker images, expects `release` or `release.server_only` to have been run first.\\n161: * `dev` &mdash; build Envoy static binary and run tests under `-c fastbuild` with clang.\\n162: * `dev <test>` &mdash; build Envoy static binary and run a specified test or test dir under `-c fastbuild` with clang.\\n163: * `dev.contrib` &mdash; build Envoy static binary with contrib and run tests under `-c fastbuild` with clang.\\n164: * `dev.contrib <test>` &mdash; build Envoy static binary with contrib and run a specified test or test dir under `-c fastbuild` with clang.\\n165: * `release` &mdash; build Envoy static binary and run tests under `-c opt` with clang.\\n166: * `release <test>` &mdash; build Envoy static binaries and run a specified test or test dir under `-c opt` with clang.\\n167: * `release.server_only` &mdash; build Envoy static binaries under `-c opt` with clang.\\n168: * `sizeopt` &mdash; build Envoy static binary and run tests under `-c opt --config=sizeopt` with clang.\\n169: * `sizeopt <test>` &mdash; build Envoy static binary and run a specified test or test dir under `-c opt --config=sizeopt` with clang.\\n170: * `sizeopt.server_only` &mdash; build Envoy static binary under `-c opt --config=sizeopt` with clang.\\n171: * `coverage` &mdash; build and run tests under `-c dbg` with gcc, generating coverage information in `$ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR/envoy/generated/coverage/coverage.html`.\\n172: * `coverage <test>` &mdash; build and run a specified test or test dir under `-c dbg` with gcc, generating coverage information in `$ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR/envoy/generated/coverage/coverage.html`. Specify `//contrib/...` to get contrib coverage.\\n173: * `msan` &mdash; build and run tests under `-c dbg --config=clang-msan` with clang.\\n174: * `msan <test>` &mdash; build and run a specified test or test dir under `-c dbg --config=clang-msan` with clang.\\n175: * `tsan` &mdash; build and run tests under `-c dbg --config=clang-tsan` with clang.\\n176: * `tsan <test>` &mdash; build and run a specified test or test dir under `-c dbg --config=clang-tsan` with clang.\\n177: * `fuzz` &mdash; build and run fuzz tests under `-c dbg --config=asan-fuzzer` with clang.\\n178: * `fuzz <test>` &mdash; build and run a specified fuzz test or test dir under `-c dbg --config=asan-fuzzer` with clang. If specifying a single fuzz test, must use the full target name with \\\"_with_libfuzzer\\\" for `<test>`.\\n179: * `compile_time_options` &mdash; build Envoy and run tests with various compile-time options toggled to their non-default state, to ensure they still build.\\n180: * `compile_time_options <test>` &mdash; build Envoy and run a specified test or test dir with various compile-time options toggled to their non-default state, to ensure they still build.\\n181: * `clang_tidy <files>` &mdash; build and run clang-tidy specified source files, if no files specified, runs against the diff with the last GitHub commit.\\n182: * `check_proto_format`&mdash; check configuration, formatting and build issues in API proto files.\\n183: * `fix_proto_format`&mdash; fix configuration, formatting and build issues in API proto files.\\n184: * `check_and_fix_proto_format` &mdash; check and fix configuration, fomatting and build issues in API proto files.\\n185: * `format`&mdash; run validation, linting and formatting tools.\\n186: * `docs`&mdash; build documentation tree in `generated/docs`.\\n187: \\n188: ## On Windows\\n189: \\n190: An example basic invocation to build the Envoy static binary and run tests is:\\n191: \\n192: ```bash\\n193: ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/windows_ci_steps.sh'\\n194: ```\\n195: \\n196: You can pass additional command line arguments to `./ci/windows_ci_steps.sh` to list specific `bazel` arguments and build/test targets.\\n197: as set environment variables to adjust your container build environment as described above.\\n198: \\n199: The Envoy binary can be found in `${TEMP}\\\\envoy-docker-build\\\\envoy\\\\source\\\\exe` on the Docker host. You\\n200: can control this by setting `ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR` in the environment, e.g. to\\n201: generate the binary in `C:\\\\Users\\\\foo\\\\build\\\\envoy\\\\source\\\\exe` you can run:\\n202: \\n203: ```bash\\n204: ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR=\\\"C:\\\\Users\\\\foo\\\\build\\\" ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/windows_ci_steps.sh'\\n205: ```\\n206: \\n207: Note the quotations around the `ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR` value to preserve the backslashes in the\\n208: path.\\n209: \\n210: If you would like to run an interactive session to keep the build container running (to persist your local build environment), run:\\n211: \\n212: ```bash\\n213: ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh 'bash'\\n214: ```\\n215: \\n216: From an interactive session, you can invoke `bazel` directly, or use the `./ci/windows_ci_steps.sh` script to build and run tests.\\n217: Bazel will look for .bazelrc in the `${HOME}` path, which is mapped to the persistent path `${TEMP}\\\\envoy-docker-build\\\\` on the\\n218: Docker host.\\n219: \\n220: # Testing changes to the build image as a developer\\n221: \\n222: The base build image used in the CI flows here lives in the [envoy-build-tools](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy-build-tools)\\n223: repository. If you need to make and/or test changes to the build image, instructions to do so can be found in\\n224: the [build_container](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy-build-tools/blob/main/build_container/README.md) folder.\\n225: See the Dockerfiles and build scripts there for building a new image.\\n226: \\n227: # macOS Build Flow\\n228: \\n229: The macOS CI build is part of the [Azure Pipelines](https://dev.azure.com/cncf/envoy/_build) workflow.\\n230: Dependencies are installed by the `ci/mac_ci_setup.sh` script, via [Homebrew](https://brew.sh),\\n231: which is pre-installed on the [Azure Pipelines macOS image](https://github.com/actions/virtual-environments/blob/main/images/macos/macos-10.15-Readme.md).\\n232: The dependencies are cached and re-installed on every build. You\\n106: can control this by setting `ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR` in the environment, e.g. to\\n107: generate the binary in `~/build/envoy/source/exe/envoy-fastbuild` you can run:\\n108: \\n109: ```bash\\n110: ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR=~/build ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh dev'\\n111: ```\\n112: \\n113: For a release version of the Envoy binary you can run:\\n114: \\n115: ```bash\\n116: ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh release.server_only'\\n117: ```\\n118: \\n119: The build artifact can be found in `/tmp/envoy-docker-build/envoy/source/exe/envoy` (or wherever\\n120: `$ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR` points).\\n121: \\n122: To enable the previous behavior of the `release.server_only` target where the final binary was copied to a tar.gz file\\n123: (e.g. envoy-binary.tar.gz), you can run:\\n124: \\n125:   ```bash\\n126:   ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh release.server_only.binary'\\n127:   ```\\n128: \\n129: For a debug version of the Envoy binary you can run:\\n130: \\n131: ```bash\\n132: ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh debug.server_only'\\n133: ```\\n134: \\n135: The build artifact can be found in `/tmp/envoy-docker-build/envoy/source/exe/envoy-debug` (or wherever\\n136: `$ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR` points).\\n137: \\n138: To leverage a [bazel remote cache](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/tree/main/bazel#advanced-caching-setup):\\n139: 1. add bazel options like `--remote_cache` and/or `--remote_cache_header` to a `.bazelrc` file, such as `user.bazelrc`. For example\\n140: \\n141: ```bash\\n142: build:my-remote-cache --remote_cache=grpcs://remotecache.googleapis.com\\n143: build:my-remote-cache --remote_cache_header=Authorization=\\\"Bearer <token>\\\"\\n144: ```\\n145: \\n146: 2. specify the config in the `BAZEL_BUILD_EXTRA_OPTIONS` environment variable. Run\\n147: \\n148: ```bash\\n149: export BAZEL_BUILD_EXTRA_OPTIONS=--config=my-remote-cache\\n150: ```\\n151: \\n152: The `./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh <TARGET>'` targets are:\\n153: \\n154: * `api` &mdash; build and run API tests under `-c fastbuild` with clang.\\n155: * `asan` &mdash; build and run tests under `-c dbg --config=clang-asan` with clang.\\n156: * `asan <test>` &mdash; build and run a specified test or test dir under `-c dbg --config=clang-asan` with clang.\\n157: * `debug` &mdash; build Envoy static binary and run tests under `-c dbg`.\\n158: * `debug <test>` &mdash; build Envoy static binary and run a specified test or test dir under `-c dbg`.\\n159: * `debug.server_only` &mdash; build Envoy static binary under `-c dbg`.\\n160: * `docker` &mdash; build Docker images, expects `release` or `release.server_only` to have been run first.\\n161: * `dev` &mdash; build Envoy static binary and run tests under `-c fastbuild` with clang.\\n162: * `dev <test>` &mdash; build Envoy static binary and run a specified test or test dir under `-c fastbuild` with clang.\\n163: * `dev.contrib` &mdash; build Envoy static binary with contrib and run tests under `-c fastbuild` with clang.\\n164: * `dev.contrib <test>` &mdash; build Envoy static binary with contrib and run a specified test or test dir under `-c fastbuild` with clang.\\n165: * `release` &mdash; build Envoy static binary and run tests under `-c opt` with clang.\\n166: * `release <test>` &mdash; build Envoy static binaries and run a specified test or test dir under `-c opt` with clang.\\n167: * `release.server_only` &mdash; build Envoy static binaries under `-c opt` with clang.\\n168: * `sizeopt` &mdash; build Envoy static binary and run tests under `-c opt --config=sizeopt` with clang.\\n169: * `sizeopt <test>` &mdash; build Envoy static binary and run a specified test or test dir under `-c opt --config=sizeopt` with clang.\\n170: * `sizeopt.server_only` &mdash; build Envoy static binary under `-c opt --config=sizeopt` with clang.\\n171: * `coverage` &mdash; build and run tests under `-c dbg` with gcc, generating coverage information in `$ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR/envoy/generated/coverage/coverage.html`.\\n172: * `coverage <test>` &mdash; build and run a specified test or test dir under `-c dbg` with gcc, generating coverage information in `$ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR/envoy/generated/coverage/coverage.html`. Specify `//contrib/...` to get contrib coverage.\\n173: * `msan` &mdash; build and run tests under `-c dbg --config=clang-msan` with clang.\\n174: * `msan <test>` &mdash; build and run a specified test or test dir under `-c dbg --config=clang-msan` with clang.\\n175: * `tsan` &mdash; build and run tests under `-c dbg --config=clang-tsan` with clang.\\n176: * `tsan <test>` &mdash; build and run a specified test or test dir under `-c dbg --config=clang-tsan` with clang.\\n177: * `fuzz` &mdash; build and run fuzz tests under `-c dbg --config=asan-fuzzer` with clang.\\n178: * `fuzz <test>` &mdash; build and run a specified fuzz test or test dir under `-c dbg --config=asan-fuzzer` with clang. If specifying a single fuzz test, must use the full target name with \\\"_with_libfuzzer\\\" for `<test>`.\\n179: * `compile_time_options` &mdash; build Envoy and run tests with various compile-time options toggled to their non-default state, to ensure they still build.\\n180: * `compile_time_options <test>` &mdash; build Envoy and run a specified test or test dir with various compile-time options toggled to their non-default state, to ensure they still build.\\n181: * `clang_tidy <files>` &mdash; build and run clang-tidy specified source files, if no files specified, runs against the diff with the last GitHub commit.\\n182: * `check_proto_format`&mdash; check configuration, formatting and build issues in API proto files.\\n183: * `fix_proto_format`&mdash; fix configuration, formatting and build issues in API proto files.\\n184: * `check_and_fix_proto_format` &mdash; check and fix configuration, fomatting and build issues in API proto files.\\n185: * `format`&mdash; run validation, linting and formatting tools.\\n186: * `docs`&mdash; build documentation tree in `generated/docs`.\\n187: \\n188: ## On Windows\\n189: \\n190: An example basic invocation to build the Envoy static binary and run tests is:\\n191: \\n192: ```bash\\n193: ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/windows_ci_steps.sh'\\n194: ```\\n195: \\n196: You can pass additional command line arguments to `./ci/windows_ci_steps.sh` to list specific `bazel` arguments and build/test targets.\\n197: as set environment variables to adjust your container build environment as described above.\\n198: \\n199: The Envoy binary can be found in `${TEMP}\\\\envoy-docker-build\\\\envoy\\\\source\\\\exe` on the Docker host. You\\n200: can control this by setting `ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR` in the environment, e.g. to\\n201: generate the binary in `C:\\\\Users\\\\foo\\\\build\\\\envoy\\\\source\\\\exe` you can run:\\n202: \\n203: ```bash\\n204: ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR=\\\"C:\\\\Users\\\\foo\\\\build\\\" ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/windows_ci_steps.sh'\\n205: ```\\n206: \\n207: Note the quotations around the `ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR` value to preserve the backslashes in the\\n208: path.\\n209: \\n210: If you would like to run an interactive session to keep the build container running (to persist your local build environment), run:\\n211: \\n212: ```bash\\n213: ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh 'bash'\\n214: ```\\n215: \\n216: From an interactive session, you can invoke `bazel` directly, or use the `./ci/windows_ci_steps.sh` script to build and run tests.\\n217: Bazel will look for .bazelrc in the `${HOME}` path, which is mapped to the persistent path `${TEMP}\\\\envoy-docker-build\\\\` on the\\n218: Docker host.\\n219: \\n220: # Testing changes to the build image as a developer\\n221: \\n222: The base build image used in the CI flows here lives in the [envoy-build-tools](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy-build-tools)\\n223: repository. If you need to make and/or test changes to the build image, instructions to do so can be found in\\n224: the [build_container](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy-build-tools/blob/main/build_container/README.md) folder.\\n225: See the Dockerfiles and build scripts there for building a new image.\\n226: \\n227: # macOS Build Flow\\n228: \\n229: The macOS CI build is part of the [Azure Pipelines](https://dev.azure.com/cncf/envoy/_build) workflow.\\n230: Dependencies are installed by the `ci/mac_ci_setup.sh` script, via [Homebrew](https://brew.sh),\\n231: which is pre-installed on the [Azure Pipelines macOS image](https://github.com/actions/virtual-environments/blob/main/images/macos/macos-10.15-Readme.md).\\n232: The dependencies are cached and re-installed on every build. The `ci/mac_ci_steps.sh` script executes the specific commands that\\n233: build and test Envoy. Note that the full version of Xcode (not just Command Line Tools) is required.\\n234: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/envoy--v1.32.1@b35dd17bea856e19fc4e65fb05e68170841d3726/-/blob/ci/README.md\"}","structuredContent":{"content":"1: # Developer use of CI Docker images\n2: \n3: There are two available flavors of Envoy Docker images for Linux, based on Ubuntu and Alpine Linux\n4: and an image based on Windows2019.\n5: \n6: ## Ubuntu Envoy image\n7: \n8: The Ubuntu based Envoy Docker image at [`envoyproxy/envoy-build-ubuntu:<hash>`](https://hub.docker.com/r/envoyproxy/envoy-build/) is used for CI checks,\n9: where `<hash>` is specified in [`envoy_build_sha.sh`](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/ci/envoy_build_sha.sh). Developers\n10: may work with the latest build image SHA in [envoy-build-tools](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy-build-tools/blob/main/toolchains/rbe_toolchains_config.bzl#L8)\n11: repo to provide a self-contained environment for building Envoy binaries and running tests that reflects the latest built Ubuntu Envoy image.\n12: Moreover, the Docker image at [`envoyproxy/envoy:dev-<hash>`](https://hub.docker.com/r/envoyproxy/envoy/tags?name=dev) is an image that has an Envoy binary at `/usr/local/bin/envoy`.\n13: The `<hash>` corresponds to the main commit at which the binary was compiled. Lastly, `envoyproxy/envoy:dev` contains an Envoy\n14: binary built from the latest tip of main that passed tests.\n15: \n16: ## Distroless Envoy image\n17: \n18: Minimal images based on a [distroless](https://github.com/GoogleContainerTools/distroless) allow for quicker deployment of Envoy.\n19: \n20: The Distroless base image is only built with symbols stripped.\n21: \n22: ## Debug Envoy image\n23: \n24: To get the binary with symbols, use the corresponding Ubuntu based debug image. The image is pushed with two different tags:\n25: `<hash>` and `latest`. Parallel to the Ubuntu images above, `<hash>` corresponds to the\n26: main commit at which the binary was compiled, and `latest` corresponds to a binary built from the latest tip of main that passed tests.\n27: \n28: ## Windows 2019 Envoy image\n29: \n30: On August 31, 2023 the Envoy project ended official Windows support due to a lack of resources.\n31: We will continue to accept patches related to the Windows build. Until further notice, Windows\n32: builds are excluded from Envoy CI, as well as the Envoy release and security processes.\n33: \n34: The Windows 2019 based Envoy Docker image at [`envoyproxy/envoy-build-windows2019:<hash>`](https://hub.docker.com/r/envoyproxy/envoy-build-windows2019/)\n35: is used for CI checks, where `<hash>` is specified in [`envoy_build_sha.sh`](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/ci/envoy_build_sha.sh).\n36: Developers may work with the most recent `envoyproxy/envoy-build-windows2019` image to provide a self-contained environment for building Envoy binaries and\n37: running tests that reflects the latest built Windows 2019 Envoy image.\n38: \n39: # Build image base and compiler versions\n40: \n41: Currently there are three build images for Linux and one for Windows:\n42: \n43: * `envoyproxy/envoy-build` &mdash; alias to `envoyproxy/envoy-build-ubuntu`.\n44: * `envoyproxy/envoy-build-ubuntu` &mdash; based on Ubuntu 20.04 (Focal) with GCC 9 and Clang 14 compiler.\n45: * `envoyproxy/envoy-build-centos` &mdash; based on CentOS 7 with GCC 9 and Clang 14 compiler, this image is experimental and not well tested.\n46: * `envoyproxy/envoy-build-windows2019` &mdash; based on Windows ltsc2019 with VS 2019 Build Tools, as well as LLVM.\n47: \n48: The source for these images is located in the [envoyproxy/envoy-build-tools](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy-build-tools)\n49: repository.\n50: \n51: We use the Clang compiler for all Linux CI runs with tests. We have an additional Linux CI run with GCC which builds binary only.\n52: \n53: # C++ standard library\n54: \n55: As of November 2019 after [#8859](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/pull/8859) the official released binary is\n56: [linked against libc++ on Linux](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/bazel/README.md#linking-against-libc-on-linux).\n57: To override the C++ standard library in your build, set environment variable `ENVOY_STDLIB` to `libstdc++` or `libc++` and\n58: run `./ci/do_ci.sh` as described below.\n59: \n60: # Building and running tests as a developer\n61: \n62: The `./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh` script can be used to set up a Docker container on Linux and Windows\n63: to build an Envoy static binary and run tests.\n64: \n65: The build image defaults to `envoyproxy/envoy-build-ubuntu` on Linux and\n66: `envoyproxy/envoy-build-windows2019` on Windows, but you can choose build image by setting\n67: `IMAGE_NAME` in the environment.\n68: \n69: In case your setup is behind a proxy, set `http_proxy` and `https_proxy` to the proxy servers before\n70: invoking the build.\n71: \n72: ```bash\n73: IMAGE_NAME=envoyproxy/envoy-build-ubuntu http_proxy=http://proxy.foo.com:8080 https_proxy=http://proxy.bar.com:8080 ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh <build_script_args>\n74: ```\n75: \n76: Besides `http_proxy` and `https_proxy`, maybe you need to set `go_proxy` to replace the default GOPROXY in China.\n77: \n78: ```bash\n79: IMAGE_NAME=envoyproxy/envoy-build-ubuntu go_proxy=https://goproxy.cn,direct http_proxy=http://proxy.foo.com:8080 https_proxy=http://proxy.bar.com:8080 ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh <build_script_args>\n80: ```\n81: \n82: To force the Envoy build image to be refreshed by Docker you can set `ENVOY_DOCKER_PULL=true`.\n83: \n84: ```bash\n85: ENVOY_DOCKER_PULL=true ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh <build_script_args>\n86: ```\n87: \n88: \n89: # Generating compile commands\n90: \n91: The `./ci/do_ci.sh` script provides a CI target that generates compile commands for clangd or other tools.\n92: \n93: ```bash\n94: ENVOY_GEN_COMPDB_OPTIONS=\"--vscode --exclude_contrib\" ./ci/do_ci.sh refresh_compdb\n95: ```\n96: \n97: ## On Linux\n98: \n99: An example basic invocation to build a developer version of the Envoy static binary (using the Bazel `fastbuild` type) is:\n100: \n101: ```bash\n102: ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh dev'\n103: ```\n104: \n105: The Envoy binary can be found in `/tmp/envoy-docker-build/envoy/source/exe/envoy-fastbuild` on the Docker host. You\n106: can control this by setting `ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR` in the environment, e.g. to\n107: generate the binary in `~/build/envoy/source/exe/envoy-fastbuild` you can run:\n108: \n109: ```bash\n110: ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR=~/build ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh dev'\n111: ```\n112: \n113: For a release version of the Envoy binary you can run:\n114: \n115: ```bash\n116: ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh release.server_only'\n117: ```\n118: \n119: The build artifact can be found in `/tmp/envoy-docker-build/envoy/source/exe/envoy` (or wherever\n120: `$ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR` points).\n121: \n122: To enable the previous behavior of the `release.server_only` target where the final binary was copied to a tar.gz file\n123: (e.g. envoy-binary.tar.gz), you can run:\n124: \n125:   ```bash\n126:   ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh release.server_only.binary'\n127:   ```\n128: \n129: For a debug version of the Envoy binary you can run:\n130: \n131: ```bash\n132: ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh debug.server_only'\n133: ```\n134: \n135: The build artifact can be found in `/tmp/envoy-docker-build/envoy/source/exe/envoy-debug` (or wherever\n136: `$ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR` points).\n137: \n138: To leverage a [bazel remote cache](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/tree/main/bazel#advanced-caching-setup):\n139: 1. add bazel options like `--remote_cache` and/or `--remote_cache_header` to a `.bazelrc` file, such as `user.bazelrc`. For example\n140: \n141: ```bash\n142: build:my-remote-cache --remote_cache=grpcs://remotecache.googleapis.com\n143: build:my-remote-cache --remote_cache_header=Authorization=\"Bearer <token>\"\n144: ```\n145: \n146: 2. specify the config in the `BAZEL_BUILD_EXTRA_OPTIONS` environment variable. Run\n147: \n148: ```bash\n149: export BAZEL_BUILD_EXTRA_OPTIONS=--config=my-remote-cache\n150: ```\n151: \n152: The `./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh <TARGET>'` targets are:\n153: \n154: * `api` &mdash; build and run API tests under `-c fastbuild` with clang.\n155: * `asan` &mdash; build and run tests under `-c dbg --config=clang-asan` with clang.\n156: * `asan <test>` &mdash; build and run a specified test or test dir under `-c dbg --config=clang-asan` with clang.\n157: * `debug` &mdash; build Envoy static binary and run tests under `-c dbg`.\n158: * `debug <test>` &mdash; build Envoy static binary and run a specified test or test dir under `-c dbg`.\n159: * `debug.server_only` &mdash; build Envoy static binary with contrib and run a specified test or test dir under `-c fastbuild` with clang.\n165: * `release` &mdash; build Envoy static binary and run tests under `-c opt` with clang.\n166: * `release <test>` &mdash; build Envoy static binaries and run a specified test or test dir under `-c opt` with clang.\n167: * `release.server_only` &mdash; build Envoy static binaries under `-c opt` with clang.\n168: * `sizeopt` &mdash; build Envoy static binary and run tests under `-c opt --config=sizeopt` with clang.\n169: * `sizeopt <test>` &mdash; build Envoy static binary and run a specified test or test dir under `-c opt --config=sizeopt` with clang.\n170: * `sizeopt.server_only` &mdash; If specifying a single fuzz test, must use the full target name with \"_with_libfuzzer\" for `<test>`.\n179: * `compile_time_options` &mdash; build Envoy and run tests with various compile-time options toggled to their non-default state, to ensure they still build.\n180: * `compile_time_options <test>` &mdash; build Envoy and run a specified test or test dir with various compile-time options toggled to their non-default state, to ensure they still build.\n181: * `clang_tidy <files>` &mdash; build and run clang-tidy specified source files, if no files specified, runs against the diff with the last GitHub commit.\n182: * `check_proto_format`&mdash; check configuration, formatting and build issues in API proto files.\n183: * `fix_proto_format`&mdash; fix configuration, formatting and build issues in API proto files.\n184: * `check_and_fix_proto_format` &mdash; check and fix configuration, fomatting and build issues in API proto files.\n185: * `format`&mdash; run validation, linting and formatting tools.\n186: * `docs`&mdash; build documentation tree in `generated/docs`.\n187: \n188: ## On Windows\n189: \n190: An example basic invocation to build the Envoy static binary and run tests is:\n191: \n192: ```bash\n193: ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/windows_ci_steps.sh'\n194: ```\n195: \n196: You can pass additional command line arguments to `./ci/windows_ci_steps.sh` to list specific `bazel` arguments and build/test targets.\n197: as set environment variables to adjust your container build environment as described above.\n198: \n199: The Envoy binary can be found in `${TEMP}\\envoy-docker-build\\envoy\\source\\exe` on the Docker host. {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_017TNKJjL1xc9k3U8TbD8S4b","type":"tool_result","content":"{\"content\":\"1: # C++ coding style\\n2: \\n3: * The Envoy source code is formatted using clang-format. Thus all white spaces, etc.\\n4:   issues are taken care of automatically. The Azure Pipelines will automatically check\\n5:   the code format and fail. There are make targets that can both check the format\\n6:   (check_format) as well as fix the code format for you (fix_format). Errors in\\n7:   .clang-tidy are enforced while other warnings are suggestions. Note that code and\\n8:   comment blocks designated `clang-format off` must be closed with `clang-format on`.\\n9:   To run these checks locally, see [Support Tools](support/README.md).\\n10: * Beyond code formatting, for the most part Envoy uses the\\n11:   [Google C++ style guidelines](https://google.github.io/styleguide/cppguide.html).\\n12:   The following section covers the major areas where we deviate from the Google\\n13:   guidelines.\\n14: \\n15: # Repository file layout\\n16: \\n17: * Please see [REPO_LAYOUT.md](REPO_LAYOUT.md).\\n18: \\n19: # Documentation\\n20: \\n21: * If you are modifying the data plane structurally, please keep the [Life of a\\n22:   Request](https://www.envoyproxy.io/docs/envoy/latest/intro/life_of_a_request) documentation up-to-date.\\n23: \\n24: # Deviations from Google C++ style guidelines\\n25: \\n26: * Exceptions are allowed on the control plane, though now discouraged in new code. Adding exceptions is disallowed on the data plane.\\n27: * References are always preferred over pointers when the reference cannot be null. This\\n28:   includes both const and non-const references.\\n29: * Function names should all use camel case starting with a lower case letter (e.g., `doFoo()`).\\n30: * Struct/Class member variables have a `_` postfix (e.g., `int foo_;`).\\n31: * Enum values using PascalCase (e.g., `RoundRobin`).\\n32: * 100 columns is the line limit.\\n33: * Use your GitHub name in TODO comments, e.g. `TODO(foobar): blah`.\\n34: * Smart pointers are type aliased:\\n35:   * `using FooPtr = std::unique_ptr<Foo>;`\\n36:   * `using BarSharedPtr = std::shared_ptr<Bar>;`\\n37:   * `using BlahConstSharedPtr = std::shared_ptr<const Blah>;`\\n38:   * Regular pointers (e.g. `int* foo`) should not be type aliased.\\n39: * `absl::optional<std::reference_wrapper<T>>` has a helper class in `envoy/common/optref.h`, and is type aliased:\\n40:   * `using FooOptRef = OptRef<T>;`\\n41:   * `using FooOptConstRef = OptRef<const T>;`\\n42: * If move semantics are intended, prefer specifying function arguments with `&&`.\\n43:   E.g., `void onHeaders(Http::HeaderMapPtr&& headers, ...)`. The rationale for this is that it\\n44:   forces the caller to specify `std::move(...)` or pass a temporary and makes the intention at\\n45:   the callsite clear. Otherwise, it's difficult to tell if a const reference is actually being\\n46:   passed to the called function. This is true even for `std::unique_ptr`.\\n47: * Prefer `unique_ptr` over `shared_ptr` wherever possible. `unique_ptr` makes ownership in\\n48:   production code easier to reason about. Note that this creates some test oddities where\\n49:   production code requires a `unique_ptr` but the test must still have access to the memory\\n50:   the production code is using (mock or otherwise). In these cases it is acceptable to allocate\\n51:   raw memory in a test and return it to the production code with the expectation that the\\n52:   production code will hold it in a `unique_ptr` and free it. Envoy uses the factory pattern\\n53:   quite a bit for these cases. (Search the code for \\\"factory\\\").\\n54: * Prefer explicitly sized integer types, such as uint64_t rather than size_t. In particular, use\\n55:   explicitly sized integers for data that is written to disk or involved in math that might overflow.\\n56: * The Google C++ style guide points out that [non-PoD static and global variables are forbidden](https://google.github.io/styleguide/cppguide.html#Static_and_Global_Variables).\\n57:   This _includes_ types such as `std::string`. We encourage the use of the\\n58:   advice in the [C++ FAQ on the static initialization\\n59:   fiasco](https://isocpp.org/wiki/faq/ctors#static-init-order-on-first-use) for\\n60:   how to best handle this.\\n61: * The Google C++ style guide points out that [constant vars should be named `kConstantVar`](https://google.github.io/styleguide/cppguide.html#Constant_Names).\\n62:   In the Envoy codebase we use `ConstantVar` or `CONSTANT_VAR`. If you pick `CONSTANT_VAR`,\\n63:   please be certain the name is globally significant to avoid potential conflicts with #defines,\\n64:   which are not namespace-scoped, and may appear in externally controlled header files.\\n65: * API-level comments should follow normal Doxygen conventions. Use `@param` to describe\\n66:   parameters and `@return <return-type>` for return values. Internal comments for\\n67:   methods and member variables may be regular C++ `//` comments or Doxygen at\\n68:   developer discretion. Where possible, methods should have meaningful\\n69:   documentation on expected input and state preconditions.\\n70: * Header guards should use `#pragma once`.\\n71: * All code should be inside a top-level Envoy namespace. There are some\\n72:   exceptions such as `main()` functions. When code cannot be placed inside the\\n73:   Envoy namespace there should be a comment of the form `// NOLINT(namespace-envoy)` at\\n74:   the top of the file.\\n75: * If a method that must be defined outside the `test` directory is intended to be called only\\n76:   from test code then it should have a name that ends in `ForTest()` such as `aMethodForTest()`.\\n77:   In most cases tests can and should be structured so this is not necessary.\\n78: * Tests default to StrictMock so will fail if hitting unexpected warnings. Feel free to use\\n79:   NiceMock for mocks whose behavior is not the focus of a test.\\n80: * [Thread\\n81:   annotations](https://github.com/abseil/abseil-cpp/blob/master/absl/base/thread_annotations.h),\\n82:   such as `ABSL_GUARDED_BY`, should be used for shared state guarded by\\n83:   locks/mutexes.\\n84: * Functions intended to be local to a cc file should be declared in an anonymous namespace,\\n85:   rather than using the 'static' keyword. Note that the\\n86:   [Google C++ style guide](https://google.github.io/styleguide/cppguide.html#Unnamed_Namespaces_and_Static_Variables)\\n87:    allows either, but in Envoy we prefer anonymous namespaces.\\n88: * Braces are required for all control statements include single line if, while, etc. statements.\\n89: * Don't use [mangled Protobuf enum\\n90:   names](https://developers.google.com/protocol-buffers/docs/reference/cpp-generated#enum).\\n91: \\n92: # Error handling\\n93: \\n94: A few general notes on our error handling philosophy:\\n95: \\n96: * All error code returns should be checked.\\n97: * At a very high level, our philosophy is that errors should be handled gracefully when caused by:\\n98:   - Untrusted network traffic (from downstream, upstream, or extensions like filters)\\n99:   - Raised by the Envoy process environment and are *likely* to happen\\n100:   - Third party dependency return codes\\n101: * Examples of likely environnmental errors include any type of network error, disk IO error, bad\\n102:   data returned by an API call, bad data read from runtime files, etc. This includes loading\\n103:   configuration at runtime.\\n104: * Third party dependency return codes should be checked and gracefully handled. Examples include\\n105:   HTTP/2 or JSON parsers. Some return codes may be handled by continuing, for example, in case of an\\n106:   out of process RPC failure.\\n107: * Testing should cover any serious cases that may result in infinite loops, crashes, or serious\\n108:   errors. Non-trivial invariants are also encouraged to have testing. Internal, localized invariants\\n109:   may not need testing.\\n110: * Errors in the Envoy environment that are *unlikely* to happen after process initialization, should\\n111:   lead to process death, under the assumption that the additional burden of defensive coding and\\n112:   testing is not an effective use of time for an error that should not happen given proper system\\n113:   setup. Examples of these types of errors include not being able to open the shared memory region,\\n114:   system calls that should not fail assuming correct parameters (which should be validated via\\n115:   tests), etc. Examples of system calls that should not fail when passed valid parameters include\\n116:   the kernel returning a valid `sockaddr` after a successful call to `accept()`, `pthread_create()`,\\n117:   `pthread_join()`, etc. However, system calls that require permissions may cause likely errors in\\n118:   some deployments and need graceful error handling.\\n119: * OOM events (both memory and FDs) or ENOMEM errors are considered fatal crashing errors. An OOM\\n120:   error should never silently be ignored and should crash the process either via the C++ allocation\\n121:   error exception, an explicit `RELEASE_ASSERT` following a third party library call, or an obvious\\n122:   crash on a subsequent line via null pointer dereference. This rule is again based on the\\n123:   philosophy that the engineering costs of properly handling these cases are not worth it. Time is\\n124:   better spent designing proper system controls that shed load if resource usage becomes too high,\\n125:   etc.\\n126: * The \\\"less is more\\\" error handling philosophy described in the previous points is primarily\\n127:   based on the fact that restarts are designed to be fast, reliable and cheap.\\n128: * Although we strongly recommend that any type of startup error leads to a fatal error, since this\\n129:   is almost always a result of faulty configuration which should be caught during a canary process,\\n130:   there may be cases in which we want some classes of startup errors to be non-fatal. For example,\\n131:   if a misconfigured option is not necessary for server operation. Although this is discouraged, we\\n132:   will discuss these on a case by case basis during code review (an example of this\\n133:   is the `--admin-address-path` option). **If degraded mode error handling is implemented, we require\\n134:   that there is complete test coverage for the degraded case.** Additionally, the user should be\\n135:   aware of the degraded state minimally via an error log of level warn or greater and via the\\n136:   increment of a stat.\\n137: * If you do need to log a non-fatal warning or error, you can unit-test it with EXPECT_LOG_CONTAINS\\n138:   or EXPECT_NO_LOGS from [logging.h](test/test_common/logging.h). It's generally bad practice to\\n139:   test by depending on log messages unless the actual behavior being validated is logging.\\n140:   It's preferable to export statistics to enable consumption by external monitoring for any\\n141:   behavior that should be externally consumed or to introduce appropriate internal interfaces\\n142:   such as mocks for internal behavior.\\n143: * The error handling philosophy described herein is based on the assumption that Envoy is deployed\\n144:   using industry best practices (primarily canary). Major and obvious errors should always be\\n145:   caught in canary. If a low rate error leads to periodic crash cycling when deployed to\\n146:   production, the error rate should allow for rollback without large customer impact.\\n147: * Tip: If the thought of adding the extra test coverage, logging, and stats to handle an error and\\n148:   continue seems ridiculous because *\\\"this should never happen\\\"*, it's a very good indication that\\n149:   the appropriate behavior is to terminate the process and not handle the error. When in doubt,\\n150:   please discuss.\\n151: \\n152: # Macro Usage\\n153: \\n154: * The following macros are available:\\n155:   - `RELEASE_ASSERT`: fatal check.\\n156:   - `ASSERT`: fatal check in debug-only builds. These should be used to document (and check in\\n157:     debug-only builds) program invariants.\\n158:   - `ENVOY_BUG`: logs and increments a stat in release mode, fatal check in debug builds. These\\n159:     should be used where it may be useful to detect if an efficient condition is violated in\\n160:     production (and fatal check in debug-only builds). This will also log a stack trace\\n161:     of the previous calls leading up to `ENVOY_BUG`.\\n162: \\n163: * Sub-macros alias the macros above and can be used to annotate specific situations:\\n164:   - `ENVOY_BUG_ALPHA` (alias `ENVOY_BUG`): Used for alpha or rapidly changing protocols that need\\n165:   detectability on probable conditions or invariants.\\n166: \\n167: * Per above it's acceptable to turn failures into crash semantics via `RELEASE_ASSERT(condition)` or\\n168:   `PANIC(message)` if there is no other sensible behavior, e.g. in OOM (memory/FD) scenarios.\\n169: * Do not `ASSERT` on conditions imposed by the external environment. Either add error handling\\n170:   (potentially with an `ENVOY_BUG` for detectability) or `RELEASE_ASSERT` if the condition indicates\\n171:   that the process is unrecoverable.\\n172: * Use `ASSERT` and `ENVOY_BUG` liberally, but do not use them for things that will crash in an obvious\\n173:   way in a subsequent line. E.g., do not do `ASSERT(foo != nullptr); foo->doSomething();`.\\n174: * Use `ASSERT`s for true invariants and well-defined conditions that are useful for tests,\\n175:   debug-only checks and documentation. They may be `ENVOY_BUG`s if performance allows, see point\\n176:   below.\\n177: * `ENVOY_BUG`s provide detectability and more confidence than an `ASSERT`. They are useful for\\n178:   non-trivial conditions, those with complex control flow, and rapidly changing protocols. Testing\\n179:   should be added to ensure that Envoy can continue to operate even if an `ENVOY_BUG` condition is\\n180:   violated.\\n181: * Annotate conditions with comments on belief or reasoning, for example `Condition is guaranteed by\\n182:   caller foo` or `Condition is likely to hold after processing through external library foo`.\\n183: * Macro usage should be understandable to a reader. Add comments if not. They should be robust to\\n184:   future changes.\\n185: * Note that there is a gray line between external environment failures and program invariant\\n186:   violations. For example, memory corruption due to a security issue (a bug, deliberate buffer\\n187:   overflow etc.) might manifest as a violation of program invariants or as a detectable condition in\\n188:   the external environment (e.g. some library returning a highly unexpected error code or buffer\\n189:   contents). Unfortunately no rule can cleanly cover when to use `RELEASE_ASSERT` vs. `ASSERT`. In\\n190:   general we view `ASSERT` as the common case and `RELEASE_ASSERT` as the uncommon case, but\\n191:   experience and judgment may dictate a particular approach depending on the situation. The risk of\\n192:   process death from `RELEASE_ASSERT` should be justified with the severity and possibility of the\\n193:   condition to avoid unintentional crashes. You may use the following guide:\\n194:     * If a violation is high risk (will cause a crash in subsequent data processing or indicates a\\n195:       failure state beyond recovery), use `RELEASE_ASSERT`.\\n196:     * If a violation is medium or low risk (Envoy can continue safely) and is not expensive,\\n197:       consider `ENVOY_BUG`.\\n198:     * Otherwise (if a condition is expensive or test-only), use `ASSERT`.\\n199: \\n200: Below is a guideline for macro usage. The left side of the table has invariants and the right side\\n201: has error conditions that can be triggered and should be gracefully handled. `ENVOY_BUG` represents\\n202: a middle ground that can be used for uncertain conditions that need detectability. `ENVOY_BUG`s can\\n203: also be added for errors if they warrant detection.\\n204: \\n205: | `ASSERT`/`RELEASE_ASSERT` | `ENVOY_BUG` | Error handling and Testing |\\n206: | --- | --- | --- |\\n207: | Low level invariants in data structures | | |\\n208: | Simple, provable internal class invariants | Complex, uncertain internal class invariants (e.g. need detectability if violated) | |\\n209: | Provable (pre/post)-conditions | Complicated but likely (pre-/post-) conditions that are low-risk (Envoy can continue safely) | Triggerable or uncertain conditions, may be based on untrusted data plane traffic or an extensions’ contract. |\\n210: |                                                                                     | Conditions in alpha or changing extensions that need detectability. (`ENVOY_BUG_ALPHA`) | |\\n211: | Unlikely environment errors after process initialization that would otherwise crash | | Likely environment errors, e.g. return codes from untrusted extensions, dependencies or system calls, network error, bad data read, permission based errors, etc. |\\n212: | Fatal crashing events. e.g. OOMs, deadlocks, no process recovery possible | | |\\n213: \\n214: # Hermetic and deterministic tests\\n215: \\n216: Tests should be hermetic, i.e. have all dependencies explicitly captured and not depend on the local\\n217: environment. In general, there should be no non-local network access. In addition:\\n218: \\n219: * Port numbers should not be hardcoded. Tests should bind to port zero and then discover the bound\\n220:   port when needed. This avoids flakes due to conflicting ports and allows tests to be executed\\n221:   concurrently by Bazel. See\\n222:   [`test/integration/integration_test.h`](test/integration/integration_test.h) and\\n223:   [`test/common/network/listener_impl_test.cc`](test/common/network/listener_impl_test.cc)\\n224:   for examples of tests that do this.\\n225: \\n226: * Paths should be constructed using:\\n227:   * The methods in [`TestEnvironment`](test/test_common/environment.h) for C++ tests.\\n228:   * With `${TEST_TMPDIR}` (for writable temporary space) or `${TEST_SRCDIR}` for read-only access to\\n229:     test inputs in shell tests.\\n230:   * With `{{ test_tmpdir }}`, `{{ test_rundir }}` and `{{ test_udsdir }}` respectively for JSON templates.\\n231:     `{{ test_udsdir }}` is provided for pathname based Unix Domain Sockets, which must fit within a\\n232:     108 character limit on Linux, a property that might not hold for `{{ test_tmpdir }}`.\\n233: \\n234: Tests should be deterministic. They should not rely on randomness or details\\n235: such as the current time. Instead, mocks such as\\n236: [`MockRandomGenerator`](test/mocks/common.h) and\\n237: [`SimulatedTimeSystem`](test/test_common/simulated_time_system.h) should be used.\\n238: \\n239: # Google style guides for other languages\\n240: \\n241: * [Python](https://google.github.io/styleguide/pyguide.html)\\n242: * [Bash](https://google.github.io/styleguide/shell.xml)\\n243: * [Bazel](https://bazel.build/versions/master/docs/skylark/build-style.html)\\n244: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/envoy--v1.32.1@b35dd17bea856e19fc4e65fb05e68170841d3726/-/blob/STYLE.md\"}"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"e91147b7-778e-4396-9da9-831fcb6d3019","uuid":"976bd05f-3f07-43ce-8642-6d7b9ec9e84f","tool_use_result":{"content":"{\"content\":\"1: # C++ coding style\\n2: \\n3: * The Envoy source code is formatted using clang-format. Thus all white spaces, etc.\\n4:   issues are taken care of automatically. The Azure Pipelines will automatically check\\n5:   the code format and fail. There are make targets that can both check the format\\n6:   (check_format) as well as fix the code format for you (fix_format). Errors in\\n7:   .clang-tidy are enforced while other warnings are suggestions. Note that code and\\n8:   comment blocks designated `clang-format off` must be closed with `clang-format on`.\\n9:   To run these checks locally, see [Support Tools](support/README.md).\\n10: * Beyond code formatting, for the most part Envoy uses the\\n11:   [Google C++ style guidelines](https://google.github.io/styleguide/cppguide.html).\\n12:   The following section covers the major areas where we deviate from the Google\\n13:   guidelines.\\n14: \\n15: # Repository file layout\\n16: \\n17: * Please see [REPO_LAYOUT.md](REPO_LAYOUT.md).\\n18: \\n19: # Documentation\\n20: \\n21: * If you are modifying the data plane structurally, please keep the [Life of a\\n22:   Request](https://www.envoyproxy.io/docs/envoy/latest/intro/life_of_a_request) documentation up-to-date.\\n23: \\n24: # Deviations from Google C++ style guidelines\\n25: \\n26: * Exceptions are allowed on the control plane, though now discouraged in new code. Adding exceptions is disallowed on the data plane.\\n27: * References are always preferred over pointers when the reference cannot be null. This\\n28:   includes both const and non-const references.\\n29: * Function names should all use camel case starting with a lower case letter (e.g., `doFoo()`).\\n30: * Struct/Class member variables have a `_` postfix (e.g., `int foo_;`).\\n31: * Enum values using PascalCase (e.g., `RoundRobin`).\\n32: * 100 columns is the line limit.\\n33: * Use your GitHub name in TODO comments, e.g. `TODO(foobar): blah`.\\n34: * Smart pointers are type aliased:\\n35:   * `using FooPtr = std::unique_ptr<Foo>;`\\n36:   * `using BarSharedPtr = std::shared_ptr<Bar>;`\\n37:   * `using BlahConstSharedPtr = std::shared_ptr<const Blah>;`\\n38:   * Regular pointers (e.g. `int* foo`) should not be type aliased.\\n39: * `absl::optional<std::reference_wrapper<T>>` has a helper class in `envoy/common/optref.h`, and is type aliased:\\n40:   * `using FooOptRef = OptRef<T>;`\\n41:   * `using FooOptConstRef = OptRef<const T>;`\\n42: * If move semantics are intended, prefer specifying function arguments with `&&`.\\n43:   E.g., `void onHeaders(Http::HeaderMapPtr&& headers, ...)`. The rationale for this is that it\\n44:   forces the caller to specify `std::move(...)` or pass a temporary and makes the intention at\\n45:   the callsite clear. Otherwise, it's difficult to tell if a const reference is actually being\\n46:   passed to the called function. This is true even for `std::unique_ptr`.\\n47: * Prefer `unique_ptr` over `shared_ptr` wherever possible. `unique_ptr` makes ownership in\\n48:   production code easier to reason about. Note that this creates some test oddities where\\n49:   production code requires a `unique_ptr` but the test must still have access to the memory\\n50:   the production code is using (mock or otherwise). In these cases it is acceptable to allocate\\n51:   raw memory in a test and return it to the production code with the expectation that the\\n52:   production code will hold it in a `unique_ptr` and free it. Envoy uses the factory pattern\\n53:   quite a bit for these cases. (Search the code for \\\"factory\\\").\\n54: * Prefer explicitly sized integer types, such as uint64_t rather than size_t. In particular, use\\n55:   explicitly sized integers for data that is written to disk or involved in math that might overflow.\\n56: * The Google C++ style guide points out that [non-PoD static and global variables are forbidden](https://google.github.io/styleguide/cppguide.html#Static_and_Global_Variables).\\n57:   This _includes_ types such as `std::string`. We encourage the use of the\\n58:   advice in the [C++ FAQ on the static initialization\\n59:   fiasco](https://isocpp.org/wiki/faq/ctors#static-init-order-on-first-use) for\\n60:   how to best handle this.\\n61: * The Google C++ style guide points out that [constant vars should be named `kConstantVar`](https://google.github.io/styleguide/cppguide.html#Constant_Names).\\n62:   In the Envoy codebase we use `ConstantVar` or `CONSTANT_VAR`. If you pick `CONSTANT_VAR`,\\n63:   please be certain the name is globally significant to avoid potential conflicts with #defines,\\n64:   which are not namespace-scoped, and may appear in externally controlled header files.\\n65: * API-level comments should follow normal Doxygen conventions. Use `@param` to describe\\n66:   parameters and `@return <return-type>` for return values. Internal comments for\\n67:   methods and member variables may be regular C++ `//` comments or Doxygen at\\n68:   developer discretion. Where possible, methods should have meaningful\\n69:   documentation on expected input and state preconditions.\\n70: * Header guards should use `#pragma once`.\\n71: * All code should be inside a top-level Envoy namespace. There are some\\n72:   exceptions such as `main()` functions. When code cannot be placed inside the\\n73:   Envoy namespace there should be a comment of the form `// NOLINT(namespace-envoy)` at\\n74:   the top of the file.\\n75: * If a method that must be defined outside the `test` directory is intended to be called only\\n76:   from test code then it should have a name that ends in `ForTest()` such as `aMethodForTest()`.\\n77:   In most cases tests can and should be structured so this is not necessary.\\n78: * Tests default to StrictMock so will fail if hitting unexpected warnings. Feel free to use\\n79:   NiceMock for mocks whose behavior is not the focus of a test.\\n80: * [Thread\\n81:   annotations](https://github.com/abseil/abseil-cpp/blob/master/absl/base/thread_annotations.h),\\n82:   such as `ABSL_GUARDED_BY`, should be used for shared state guarded by\\n83:   locks/mutexes.\\n84: * Functions intended to be local to a cc file should be declared in an anonymous namespace,\\n85:   rather than using the 'static' keyword. Note that the\\n86:   [Google C++ style guide](https://google.github.io/styleguide/cppguide.html#Unnamed_Namespaces_and_Static_Variables)\\n87:    allows either, but in Envoy we prefer anonymous namespaces.\\n88: * Braces are required for all control statements include single line if, while, etc. statements.\\n89: * Don't use [mangled Protobuf enum\\n90:   names](https://developers.google.com/protocol-buffers/docs/reference/cpp-generated#enum).\\n91: \\n92: # Error handling\\n93: \\n94: A few general notes on our error handling philosophy:\\n95: \\n96: * All error code returns should be checked.\\n97: * At a very high level, our philosophy is that errors should be handled gracefully when caused by:\\n98:   - Untrusted network traffic (from downstream, upstream, or extensions like filters)\\n99:   - Raised by the Envoy process environment and are *likely* to happen\\n100:   - Third party dependency return codes\\n101: * Examples of likely environnmental errors include any type of network error, disk IO error, bad\\n102:   data returned by an API call, bad data read from runtime files, etc. This includes loading\\n103:   configuration at runtime.\\n104: * Third party dependency return codes should be checked and gracefully handled. Internal, localized invariants\\n109:   may not need testing.\\n110: * Errors in the Envoy environment that are *unlikely* to happen after process initialization, should\\n111:   lead to process death, under the assumption that the additional burden of defensive coding and\\n112:   testing is not an effective use of time for an error that should not happen given proper system\\n113:   setup. Examples of these types of errors include not being able to open the shared memory region,\\n114:   system calls that should not fail assuming correct parameters (which should be validated via\\n115:   tests), etc. Examples of system calls that should not fail when passed valid parameters include\\n116:   the kernel returning a valid `sockaddr` after a successful call to `accept()`, `pthread_create()`,\\n117:   `pthread_join()`, etc. However, system calls that require permissions may cause likely errors in\\n118:   some deployments and need graceful error handling.\\n119: * OOM events (both memory and FDs) or ENOMEM errors are considered fatal crashing errors. Time is\\n124:   better spent designing proper system controls that shed load if resource usage becomes too high,\\n125:   etc.\\n126: * The \\\"less is more\\\" error handling philosophy described in the previous points is primarily\\n127:   based on the fact that restarts are designed to be fast, reliable and cheap.\\n128: * Although we strongly recommend that any type of startup error leads to a fatal error, since this\\n129:   is almost always a result of faulty configuration which should be caught during a canary process,\\n130:   there may be cases in which we want some classes of startup errors to be non-fatal. For example,\\n131:   if a misconfigured option is not necessary for server operation. Although this is discouraged, we\\n132:   will discuss these on a case by case basis during code review (an example of this\\n133:   is the `--admin-address-path` option). **If degraded mode error handling is implemented, we require\\n134:   that there is complete test coverage for the degraded case.** Additionally, the user should be\\n135:   aware of the degraded state minimally via an error log of level warn or greater and via the\\n136:   increment of a stat.\\n137: * If you do need to log a non-fatal warning or error, you can unit-test it with EXPECT_LOG_CONTAINS\\n138:   or EXPECT_NO_LOGS from [logging.h](test/test_common/logging.h). It's generally bad practice to\\n139:   test by depending on log messages unless the actual behavior being validated is logging.\\n140:   It's preferable to export statistics to enable consumption by external monitoring for any\\n141:   behavior that should be externally consumed or to introduce appropriate internal interfaces\\n142:   such as mocks for internal behavior.\\n143: * The error handling philosophy described herein is based on the assumption that Envoy is deployed\\n144:   using industry best practices (primarily canary). Major and obvious errors should always be\\n145:   caught in canary. If a low rate error leads to periodic crash cycling when deployed to\\n146:   production, the error rate should allow for rollback without large customer impact.\\n147: * Tip: If the thought of adding the extra test coverage, logging, and stats to handle an error and\\n148:   continue seems ridiculous because *\\\"this should never happen\\\"*, it's a very good indication that\\n149:   the appropriate behavior is to terminate the process and not handle the error. When in doubt,\\n150:   please discuss.\\n151: \\n152: # Macro Usage\\n153: \\n154: * The following macros are available:\\n155:   - `RELEASE_ASSERT`: fatal check.\\n156:   - `ASSERT`: fatal check in debug-only builds. These should be used to document (and check in\\n157:     debug-only builds) program invariants.\\n158:   - `ENVOY_BUG`: logs and increments a stat in release mode, fatal check in debug builds. These\\n159:     should be used where it may be useful to detect if an efficient condition is violated in\\n160:     production (and fatal check in debug-only builds). This will also log a stack trace\\n161:     of the previous calls leading up to `ENVOY_BUG`.\\n162: \\n163: * Sub-macros alias the macros above and can be used to annotate specific situations:\\n164:   - `ENVOY_BUG_ALPHA` (alias `ENVOY_BUG`): Used for alpha or rapidly changing protocols that need\\n165:   detectability on probable conditions or invariants.\\n166: \\n167: * Per above it's acceptable to turn failures into crash semantics via `RELEASE_ASSERT(condition)` or\\n168:   `PANIC(message)` if there is no other sensible behavior, e.g. in OOM (memory/FD) scenarios.\\n169: * Do not `ASSERT` on conditions imposed by the external environment. Either add error handling\\n170:   (potentially with an `ENVOY_BUG` for detectability) or `RELEASE_ASSERT` if the condition indicates\\n171:   that the process is unrecoverable.\\n172: * Use `ASSERT` and `ENVOY_BUG` liberally, but do not use them for things that will crash in an obvious\\n173:   way in a subsequent line.
