They may be `ENVOY_BUG`s if performance allows, see point\\n176:   below.\\n177: * `ENVOY_BUG`s provide detectability and more confidence than an `ASSERT`. They are useful for\\n178:   non-trivial conditions, those with complex control flow, and rapidly changing protocols. Testing\\n179:   should be added to ensure that Envoy can continue to operate even if an `ENVOY_BUG` condition is\\n180:   violated.\\n181: * Annotate conditions with comments on belief or reasoning, for example `Condition is guaranteed by\\n182:   caller foo` or `Condition is likely to hold after processing through external library foo`.\\n183: * Macro usage should be understandable to a reader. Add comments if not. They should be robust to\\n184:   future changes.\\n185: * Note that there is a gray line between external environment failures and program invariant\\n186:   violations. For example, memory corruption due to a security issue (a bug, deliberate buffer\\n187:   overflow etc.) might manifest as a violation of program invariants or as a detectable condition in\\n188:   the external environment (e.g. some library returning a highly unexpected error code or buffer\\n189:   contents). Unfortunately no rule can cleanly cover when to use `RELEASE_ASSERT` vs. `ASSERT`. In\\n190:   general we view `ASSERT` as the common case and `RELEASE_ASSERT` as the uncommon case, but\\n191:   experience and judgment may dictate a particular approach depending on the situation. The risk of\\n192:   process death from `RELEASE_ASSERT` should be justified with the severity and possibility of the\\n193:   condition to avoid unintentional crashes. You may use the following guide:\\n194:     * If a violation is high risk (will cause a crash in subsequent data processing or indicates a\\n195:       failure state beyond recovery), use `RELEASE_ASSERT`.\\n196:     * If a violation is medium or low risk (Envoy can continue safely) and is not expensive,\\n197:       consider `ENVOY_BUG`.\\n198:     * Otherwise (if a condition is expensive or test-only), use `ASSERT`.\\n199: \\n200: Below is a guideline for macro usage. The left side of the table has invariants and the right side\\n201: has error conditions that can be triggered and should be gracefully handled. `ENVOY_BUG` represents\\n202: a middle ground that can be used for uncertain conditions that need detectability. `ENVOY_BUG`s can\\n203: also be added for errors if they warrant detection.\\n204: \\n205: | `ASSERT`/`RELEASE_ASSERT` | `ENVOY_BUG` | Error handling and Testing |\\n206: | --- | --- | --- |\\n207: | Low level invariants in data structures | | |\\n208: | Simple, provable internal class invariants | Complex, uncertain internal class invariants (e.g. need detectability if violated) | |\\n209: | Provable (pre/post)-conditions | Complicated but likely (pre-/post-) conditions that are low-risk (Envoy can continue safely) | Triggerable or uncertain conditions, may be based on untrusted data plane traffic or an extensions’ contract. |\\n210: |                                                                                     | Conditions in alpha or changing extensions that need detectability. (`ENVOY_BUG_ALPHA`) | |\\n211: | Unlikely environment errors after process initialization that would otherwise crash | | Likely environment errors, e.g. return codes from untrusted extensions, dependencies or system calls, network error, bad data read, permission based errors, etc. |\\n212: | Fatal crashing events. e.g. OOMs, deadlocks, no process recovery possible | | |\\n213: \\n214: # Hermetic and deterministic tests\\n215: \\n216: Tests should be hermetic, i.e. have all dependencies explicitly captured and not depend on the local\\n217: environment. In general, there should be no non-local network access. In addition:\\n218: \\n219: * Port numbers should not be hardcoded. Tests should bind to port zero and then discover the bound\\n220:   port when needed. This avoids flakes due to conflicting ports and allows tests to be executed\\n221:   concurrently by Bazel. See\\n222:   [`test/integration/integration_test.h`](test/integration/integration_test.h) and\\n223:   [`test/common/network/listener_impl_test.cc`](test/common/network/listener_impl_test.cc)\\n224:   for examples of tests that do this.\\n225: \\n226: * Paths should be constructed using:\\n227:   * The methods in [`TestEnvironment`](test/test_common/environment.h) for C++ tests.\\n228:   * With `${TEST_TMPDIR}` (for writable temporary space) or `${TEST_SRCDIR}` for read-only access to\\n229:     test inputs in shell tests.\\n230:   * With `{{ test_tmpdir }}`, `{{ test_rundir }}` and `{{ test_udsdir }}` respectively for JSON templates.\\n231:     `{{ test_udsdir }}` is provided for pathname based Unix Domain Sockets, which must fit within a\\n232:     108 character limit on Linux, a property that might not hold for `{{ test_tmpdir }}`.\\n233: \\n234: Tests should be deterministic. They should not rely on randomness or details\\n235: such as the current time. Instead, mocks such as\\n236: [`MockRandomGenerator`](test/mocks/common.h) and\\n237: [`SimulatedTimeSystem`](test/test_common/simulated_time_system.h) should be used.\\n238: \\n239: # Google style guides for other languages\\n240: \\n241: * [Python](https://google.github.io/styleguide/pyguide.html)\\n242: * [Bash](https://google.github.io/styleguide/shell.xml)\\n243: * [Bazel](https://bazel.build/versions/master/docs/skylark/build-style.html)\\n244: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/envoy--v1.32.1@b35dd17bea856e19fc4e65fb05e68170841d3726/-/blob/STYLE.md\"}","structuredContent":{"content":"1: # C++ coding style\n2: \n3: * The Envoy source code is formatted using clang-format. Thus all white spaces, etc.\n4:   issues are taken care of automatically. The Azure Pipelines will automatically check\n5:   the code format and fail. There are make targets that can both check the format\n6:   (check_format) as well as fix the code format for you (fix_format). Errors in\n7:   .clang-tidy are enforced while other warnings are suggestions. Note that code and\n8:   comment blocks designated `clang-format off` must be closed with `clang-format on`.\n9:   To run these checks locally, see [Support Tools](support/README.md).\n10: * Beyond code formatting, for the most part Envoy uses the\n11:   [Google C++ style guidelines](https://google.github.io/styleguide/cppguide.html).\n12:   The following section covers the major areas where we deviate from the Google\n13:   guidelines.\n14: \n15: # Repository file layout\n16: \n17: * Please see [REPO_LAYOUT.md](REPO_LAYOUT.md).\n18: \n19: # Documentation\n20: \n21: * If you are modifying the data plane structurally, please keep the [Life of a\n22:   Request](https://www.envoyproxy.io/docs/envoy/latest/intro/life_of_a_request) documentation up-to-date.\n23: \n24: # Deviations from Google C++ style guidelines\n25: \n26: * Exceptions are allowed on the control plane, though now discouraged in new code. Adding exceptions is disallowed on the data plane.\n27: * References are always preferred over pointers when the reference cannot be null. This\n28:   includes both const and non-const references.\n29: * Function names should all use camel case starting with a lower case letter (e.g., `doFoo()`).\n30: * Struct/Class member variables have a `_` postfix (e.g., `int foo_;`).\n31: * Enum values using PascalCase (e.g., `RoundRobin`).\n32: * 100 columns is the line limit.\n33: * Use your GitHub name in TODO comments, e.g. `TODO(foobar): blah`.\n34: * Smart pointers are type aliased:\n35:   * `using FooPtr = std::unique_ptr<Foo>;`\n36:   * `using BarSharedPtr = std::shared_ptr<Bar>;`\n37:   * `using BlahConstSharedPtr = std::shared_ptr<const Blah>;`\n38:   * Regular pointers (e.g. `int* foo`) should not be type aliased.\n39: * `absl::optional<std::reference_wrapper<T>>` has a helper class in `envoy/common/optref.h`, and is type aliased:\n40:   * `using FooOptRef = OptRef<T>;`\n41:   * `using FooOptConstRef = OptRef<const T>;`\n42: * If move semantics are intended, prefer specifying function arguments with `&&`.\n43:   E.g., `void onHeaders(Http::HeaderMapPtr&& headers, ...)`. The rationale for this is that it\n44:   forces the caller to specify `std::move(...)` or pass a temporary and makes the intention at\n45:   the callsite clear. Otherwise, it's difficult to tell if a const reference is actually being\n46:   passed to the called function. This is true even for `std::unique_ptr`.\n47: * Prefer `unique_ptr` over `shared_ptr` wherever possible. `unique_ptr` makes ownership in\n48:   production code easier to reason about. Note that this creates some test oddities where\n49:   production code requires a `unique_ptr` but the test must still have access to the memory\n50:   the production code is using (mock or otherwise). In these cases it is acceptable to allocate\n51:   raw memory in a test and return it to the production code with the expectation that the\n52:   production code will hold it in a `unique_ptr` and free it. Envoy uses the factory pattern\n53:   quite a bit for these cases. (Search the code for \"factory\").\n54: * Prefer explicitly sized integer types, such as uint64_t rather than size_t. In particular, use\n55:   explicitly sized integers for data that is written to disk or involved in math that might overflow.\n56: * The Google C++ style guide points out that [non-PoD static and global variables are forbidden](https://google.github.io/styleguide/cppguide.html#Static_and_Global_Variables).\n57:   This _includes_ types such as `std::string`. We encourage the use of the\n58:   advice in the [C++ FAQ on the static initialization\n59:   fiasco](https://isocpp.org/wiki/faq/ctors#static-init-order-on-first-use) for\n60:   how to best handle this.\n61: * The Google C++ style guide points out that [constant vars should be named `kConstantVar`](https://google.github.io/styleguide/cppguide.html#Constant_Names).\n62:   In the Envoy codebase we use `ConstantVar` or `CONSTANT_VAR`. If you pick `CONSTANT_VAR`,\n63:   please be certain the name is globally significant to avoid potential conflicts with #defines,\n64:   which are not namespace-scoped, and may appear in externally controlled header files.\n65: * API-level comments should follow normal Doxygen conventions. Use `@param` to describe\n66:   parameters and `@return <return-type>` for return values. Internal comments for\n67:   methods and member variables may be regular C++ `//` comments or Doxygen at\n68:   developer discretion. Where possible, methods should have meaningful\n69:   documentation on expected input and state preconditions.\n70: * Header guards should use `#pragma once`.\n71: * All code should be inside a top-level Envoy namespace. There are some\n72:   exceptions such as `main()` functions. When code cannot be placed inside the\n73:   Envoy namespace there should be a comment of the form `// NOLINT(namespace-envoy)` at\n74:   the top of the file.\n75: * If a method that must be defined outside the `test` directory is intended to be called only\n76:   from test code then it should have a name that ends in `ForTest()` such as `aMethodForTest()`.\n77:   In most cases tests can and should be structured so this is not necessary.\n78: * Tests default to StrictMock so will fail if hitting unexpected warnings. Feel free to use\n79:   NiceMock for mocks whose behavior is not the focus of a test.\n80: * [Thread\n81:   annotations](https://github.com/abseil/abseil-cpp/blob/master/absl/base/thread_annotations.h),\n82:   such as `ABSL_GUARDED_BY`, should be used for shared state guarded by\n83:   locks/mutexes.\n84: * Functions intended to be local to a cc file should be declared in an anonymous namespace,\n85:   rather than using the 'static' keyword. Note that the\n86:   [Google C++ style guide](https://google.github.io/styleguide/cppguide.html#Unnamed_Namespaces_and_Static_Variables)\n87:    allows either, but in Envoy we prefer anonymous namespaces.\n88: * Braces are required for all control statements include single line if, while, etc. statements.\n89: * Don't use [mangled Protobuf enum\n90:   names](https://developers.google.com/protocol-buffers/docs/reference/cpp-generated#enum).\n91: \n92: # Error handling\n93: \n94: A few general notes on our error handling philosophy:\n95: \n96: * All error code returns should be checked.\n97: * At a very high level, our philosophy is that errors should be handled gracefully when caused by:\n98:   - Untrusted network traffic (from downstream, upstream, or extensions like filters)\n99:   - Raised by the Envoy process environment and are *likely* to happen\n100:   - Third party dependency return codes\n101: * Examples of likely environnmental errors include any type of network error, disk IO error, bad\n102:   data returned by an API call, bad data read from runtime files, etc. This includes loading\n103:   configuration at runtime.\n104: * Third party dependency return codes should be checked and gracefully handled. Examples include\n105:   HTTP/2 or JSON parsers. Some return codes may be handled by continuing, for example, in case of an\n106:   out of process RPC failure.\n107: * Testing should cover any serious cases that may result in infinite loops, crashes, or serious\n108:   errors. Non-trivial invariants are also encouraged to have testing. Internal, localized invariants\n109:   may not need testing.\n110: * Errors in the Envoy environment that are *unlikely* to happen after process initialization, should\n111:   lead to process death, under the assumption that the additional burden of defensive coding and\n112:   testing is not an effective use of time for an error that should not happen given proper system\n113:   setup. Examples of these types of errors include not being able to open the shared memory region,\n114:   system calls that should not fail assuming correct parameters (which should be validated via\n115:   tests), etc. Examples of system calls that should not fail when passed valid parameters include\n116:   the kernel returning a valid `sockaddr` after a successful call to `accept()`, `pthread_create()`,\n117:   `pthread_join()`, etc. However, system calls that require permissions may cause likely errors in\n118:   some deployments and need graceful error handling.\n119: * OOM events (both memory and FDs) or ENOMEM errors are considered fatal crashing errors. An OOM\n120:   error should never silently be ignored and should crash the process either via the C++ allocation\n121:   error exception, an explicit `RELEASE_ASSERT` following a third party library call, or an obvious\n122:   crash on a subsequent line via null pointer dereference. This rule is again based on the\n123:   philosophy that the engineering costs of properly handling these cases are not worth it. Time is\n124:   better spent designing proper system controls that shed load if resource usage becomes too high,\n125:   etc.\n126: * The \"less is more\" error handling philosophy described in the previous points is primarily\n127:   based on the fact that restarts are designed to be fast, reliable and cheap.\n128: * Although we strongly recommend that any type of startup error leads to a fatal error, since this\n129:   is almost always a result of faulty configuration which should be caught during a canary process,\n130:   there may be cases in which we want some classes of startup errors to be non-fatal. For example,\n131:   if a misconfigured option is not necessary for server operation. Although this is discouraged, we\n132:   will discuss these on a case by case basis during code review (an example of this\n133:   is the `--admin-address-path` option). **If degraded mode error handling is implemented, we require\n134:   that there is complete test coverage for the degraded case.** Additionally, the user should be\n135:   aware of the degraded state minimally via an error log of level warn or greater and via the\n136:   increment of a stat.\n137: * If you do need to log a non-fatal warning or error, you can unit-test it with EXPECT_LOG_CONTAINS\n138:   or EXPECT_NO_LOGS from [logging.h](test/test_common/logging.h). It's generally bad practice to\n139:   test by depending on log messages unless the actual behavior being validated is logging.\n140:   It's preferable to export statistics to enable consumption by external monitoring for any\n141:   behavior that should be externally consumed or to introduce appropriate internal interfaces\n142:   such as mocks for internal behavior.\n143: * The error handling philosophy described herein is based on the assumption that Envoy is deployed\n144:   using industry best practices (primarily canary). Major and obvious errors should always be\n145:   caught in canary. If a low rate error leads to periodic crash cycling when deployed to\n146:   production, the error rate should allow for rollback without large customer impact.\n147: * Tip: If the thought of adding the extra test coverage, logging, and stats to handle an error and\n148:   continue seems ridiculous because *\"this should never happen\"*, it's a very good indication that\n149:   the appropriate behavior is to terminate the process and not handle the error. When in doubt,\n150:   please discuss.\n151: \n152: # Macro Usage\n153: \n154: * The following macros are available:\n155:   - `RELEASE_ASSERT`: fatal check.\n156:   - `ASSERT`: fatal check in debug-only builds. These should be used to document (and check in\n157:     debug-only builds) program invariants.\n158:   - `ENVOY_BUG`: logs and increments a stat in release mode, fatal check in debug builds. These\n159:     should be used where it may be useful to detect if an efficient condition is violated in\n160:     production (and fatal check in debug-only builds). This will also log a stack trace\n161:     of the previous calls leading up to `ENVOY_BUG`.\n162: \n163: * Sub-macros alias the macros above and can be used to annotate specific situations:\n164:   - `ENVOY_BUG_ALPHA` (alias `ENVOY_BUG`): Used for alpha or rapidly changing protocols that need\n165:   detectability on probable conditions or invariants.\n166: \n167: * Per above it's acceptable to turn failures into crash semantics via `RELEASE_ASSERT(condition)` or\n168:   `PANIC(message)` if there is no other sensible behavior, e.g. in OOM (memory/FD) scenarios.\n169: * Do not `ASSERT` on conditions imposed by the external environment. Either add error handling\n170:   (potentially with an `ENVOY_BUG` for detectability) or `RELEASE_ASSERT` if the condition indicates\n171:   that the process is unrecoverable.\n172: * Use `ASSERT` and `ENVOY_BUG` liberally, but do not use them for things that will crash in an obvious\n173:   way in a subsequent line. E.g., do not do `ASSERT(foo != nullptr); foo->doSomething();`.\n174: * Use `ASSERT`s for true invariants and well-defined conditions that are useful for tests,\n175:   debug-only checks and documentation. They may be `ENVOY_BUG`s if performance allows, see point\n176:   below.\n177: * `ENVOY_BUG`s provide detectability and more confidence than an `ASSERT`. They are useful for\n178:   non-trivial conditions, those with complex control flow, and rapidly changing protocols. Testing\n179:   should be added to ensure that Envoy can continue to operate even if an `ENVOY_BUG` condition is\n180:   violated.\n181: * Annotate conditions with comments on belief or reasoning, for example `Condition is guaranteed by\n182:   caller foo` or `Condition is likely to hold after processing through external library foo`.\n183: * Macro usage should be understandable to a reader. Add comments if not. They should be robust to\n184:   future changes.\n185: * Note that there is a gray line between external environment failures and program invariant\n186:   violations. For example, memory corruption due to a security issue (a bug, deliberate buffer\n187:   overflow etc.) might manifest as a violation of program invariants or as a detectable condition in\n188:   the external environment (e.g. some library returning a highly unexpected error code or buffer\n189:   contents). Unfortunately no rule can cleanly cover when to use `RELEASE_ASSERT` vs. `ASSERT`. In\n190:   general we view `ASSERT` as the common case and `RELEASE_ASSERT` as the uncommon case, but\n191:   experience and judgment may dictate a particular approach depending on the situation. The risk of\n192:   process death from `RELEASE_ASSERT` should be justified with the severity and possibility of the\n193:   condition to avoid unintentional crashes. You may use the following guide:\n194:     * If a violation is high risk (will cause a crash in subsequent data processing or indicates a\n195:       failure state beyond recovery), use `RELEASE_ASSERT`.\n196:     * If a violation is medium or low risk (Envoy can continue safely) and is not expensive,\n197:       consider `ENVOY_BUG`.\n198:     * Otherwise (if a condition is expensive or test-only), use `ASSERT`.\n199: \n200: Below is a guideline for macro usage. The left side of the table has invariants and the right side\n201: has error conditions that can be triggered and should be gracefully handled. `ENVOY_BUG` represents\n202: a middle ground that can be used for uncertain conditions that need detectability. `ENVOY_BUG`s can\n203: also be added for errors if they warrant detection.\n204: \n205: | `ASSERT`/`RELEASE_ASSERT` | `ENVOY_BUG` | Error handling and Testing |\n206: | --- | --- | --- |\n207: | Low level invariants in data structures | | |\n208: | Simple, provable internal class invariants | Complex, uncertain internal class invariants (e.g. need detectability if violated) | |\n209: | Provable (pre/post)-conditions | Complicated but likely (pre-/post-) conditions that are low-risk (Envoy can continue safely) | Triggerable or uncertain conditions, may be based on untrusted data plane traffic or an extensions’ contract. |\n210: |                                                                                     | Conditions in alpha or changing extensions that need detectability. (`ENVOY_BUG_ALPHA`) | |\n211: | Unlikely environment errors after process initialization that would otherwise crash | | Likely environment errors, e.g. return codes from untrusted extensions, dependencies or system calls, network error, bad data read, permission based errors, etc. |\n212: | Fatal crashing events. e.g. OOMs, deadlocks, no process recovery possible | | |\n213: \n214: # Hermetic and deterministic tests\n215: \n216: Tests should be hermetic, i.e. have all dependencies explicitly captured and not depend on the local\n217: environment. In general, there should be no non-local network access. In addition:\n218: \n219: * Port numbers should not be hardcoded. Tests should bind to port zero and then discover the bound\n220:   port when needed. This avoids flakes due to conflicting ports and allows tests to be executed\n221:   concurrently by Bazel. See\n222:   [`test/integration/integration_test.h`](test/integration/integration_test.h) and\n223:   [`test/common/network/listener_impl_test.cc`](test/common/network/listener_impl_test.cc)\n224:   for examples of tests that do this.\n225: \n226: * Paths should be constructed using:\n227:   * The methods in [`TestEnvironment`](test/test_common/environment.h) for C++ tests.\n228:   * With `${TEST_TMPDIR}` (for writable temporary space) or `${TEST_SRCDIR}` for read-only access to\n229:     test inputs in shell tests.\n230:   * With `{{ test_tmpdir }}`, `{{ test_rundir }}` and `{{ test_udsdir }}` respectively for JSON templates.\n231:     `{{ test_udsdir }}` is provided for pathname based Unix Domain Sockets, which must fit within a\n232:     108 character limit on Linux, a property that might not hold for `{{ test_tmpdir }}`.\n233: \n234: Tests should be deterministic. They should not rely on randomness or details\n235: such as the current time. Instead, mocks such as\n236: [`MockRandomGenerator`](test/mocks/common.h) and\n237: [`SimulatedTimeSystem`](test/test_common/simulated_time_system.h) should be used.\n238: \n239: # Google style guides for other languages\n240: \n241: * [Python](https://google.github.io/styleguide/pyguide.html)\n242: * [Bash](https://google.github.io/styleguide/shell.xml)\n243: * [Bazel](https://bazel.build/versions/master/docs/skylark/build-style.html)\n244: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/envoy--v1.32.1@b35dd17bea856e19fc4e65fb05e68170841d3726/-/blob/STYLE.md"}}}

{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01XmPEeULMd2Sb1NbkDd7y1K","type":"tool_result","content":"{\"content\":\"1: # Repository layout overview\\n2: \\n3: This is a high level overview of how the repository is laid out to both aid in code investigation,\\n4: as well as to clearly specify how extensions are added to the repository. The top level directories\\n5: are:\\n6: \\n7: * [.azure-pipelines/](.azure-pipelines/): Configuration for\\n8: [Azure Pipelines](https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/services/devops/pipelines/).\\n9: * [api/](api/): Envoy data plane API.\\n10: * [bazel/](bazel/): Configuration for Envoy's use of [Bazel](https://bazel.build/).\\n11: * [ci/](ci/): Scripts used both during CI as well as to build Docker containers.\\n12: * [configs/](configs/): Example Envoy configurations.\\n13: * [docs/](docs/): End user facing Envoy proxy and data plane API documentation as well as scripts\\n14:   for publishing final docs during releases.\\n15: * [examples/](examples/): Larger Envoy examples using Docker and Docker Compose.\\n16: * [envoy/](envoy/): \\\"Public\\\" interface headers for \\\"core\\\" Envoy. In general,\\n17:   these are almost entirely 100% abstract classes. There are a few cases of not-abstract classes in\\n18:   the \\\"public\\\" headers, typically for performance reasons. Note that \\\"core\\\" includes some\\n19:   \\\"extensions\\\" such as the HTTP connection manager filter and associated functionality which are\\n20:   so fundamental to Envoy that they will likely never be optional from a compilation perspective.\\n21: * [restarter/](restarter/): Envoy's hot restart wrapper Python script.\\n22: * [security/](security/): Some templates for reporting security issues of Envoy. Historical security issues can also be found here.\\n23: * [source/](source/): Source code for core Envoy as well as extensions. The layout of this directory\\n24:   is discussed in further detail below.\\n25: * [support/](support/): Development support scripts (pre-commit Git hooks, etc.)\\n26: * [test/](test/): Test code for core Envoy as well as extensions. The layout of this directory is\\n27:   discussed in further detail below.\\n28: * [tools/](tools/): Miscellaneous tools that have not found a home somewhere else.\\n29: \\n30: ## [source/](source/)\\n31: \\n32: * [common/](source/common/): Core Envoy code (not specific to extensions) that is also not\\n33:   specific to a standalone server implementation. I.e., this is the code that could be used if Envoy\\n34:   were eventually embedded as a library.\\n35: * [docs/](source/docs/): Miscellaneous developer/design documentation that is not relevant for\\n36:   the public user documentation.\\n37: * [exe/](source/exe/): Code specific to building the final production Envoy server binary. This is\\n38:   the only code that is not shared by integration and unit tests.\\n39: * [extensions/](source/extensions/): Extensions to the core Envoy code. The layout of this\\n40:   directory is discussed in further detail below.\\n41: * [server/](source/server/): Code specific to running Envoy as a standalone server. E.g,\\n42:   configuration, server startup, workers, etc. Over time, the line between `common/` and `server/`\\n43:   has become somewhat blurred. Use best judgment as to where to place something.\\n44: \\n45: ## [test/](test/)\\n46: \\n47: Not every directory within test is described below, but a few highlights:\\n48: \\n49: * Unit tests are found in directories matching their [source/](source/) equivalents. E.g.,\\n50:   [common/](test/common/), [exe/](test/exe/), and [server/](test/server/).\\n51: * Extension unit tests also match their source equivalents in [extensions/](test/extensions/).\\n52: * [integration/](test/integration/) holds end-to-end integration tests using roughly the real\\n53:   Envoy server code, fake downstream clients, and fake upstream servers. Integration tests also\\n54:   test some of the extensions found in the repository. Note that in the future, we would like to\\n55:   allow integration tests that are specific to extensions and are not required for covering\\n56:   \\\"core\\\" Envoy functionality. Those integration tests will likely end up in the\\n57:   [extensions/](test/extensions/) directory but further work and thinking is required before\\n58:   we get to that point.\\n59: * [mocks/](test/mocks/) contains mock implementations of all of the core Envoy interfaces found in\\n60:   [include/](include/).\\n61: * Other directories include tooling used for configuration testing, coverage testing, fuzz testing,\\n62:   common test code, etc.\\n63: \\n64: ## [source/extensions](source/extensions/) layout\\n65: \\n66: We maintain a very specific code and namespace layout for extensions. This aids in discovering\\n67: code/extensions, and allows us specify extension owners in [CODEOWNERS](CODEOWNERS).\\n68: \\n69: * All extensions are either registered in [all_extensions.bzl](source/extensions/all_extensions.bzl)\\n70:   or [extensions_build_config.bzl](source/extensions/extensions_build_config.bzl). The former is\\n71:   for extensions that cannot be removed from the primary Envoy build. The latter is for extensions\\n72:   that can be removed on a site specific basis. See [bazel/README.md](bazel/README.md) for how to\\n73:   compile out extensions on a site specific basis. Note that by default extensions should be\\n74:   removable from the build unless there is a very good reason.\\n75: * These are the top level extension directories and associated namespaces:\\n76:   * [access_loggers/](/source/extensions/access_loggers): Access log implementations which use\\n77:     the `Envoy::Extensions::AccessLoggers` namespace.\\n78:   * [bootstrap/](/source/extensions/bootstrap): Bootstrap extensions which use\\n79:     the `Envoy::Extensions::Bootstrap` namespace.\\n80:   * [clusters/](/source/extensions/clusters): Cluster extensions which use the\\n81:     `Envoy::Extensions::Clusters` namespace.\\n82:   * [compression/](/source/extensions/compression): Compression extensions\\n83:     which use `Envoy::Extensions::Compression` namespace.\\n84:   * [fatal_actions/](/source/extensions/fatal_actions): Fatal Action extensions\\n85:     which use the `Envoy::Extensions::FatalActions` namespace.\\n86:   * [filters/http/](/source/extensions/filters/http): HTTP L7 filters which use the\\n87:     `Envoy::Extensions::HttpFilters` namespace.\\n88:   * [filters/listener/](/source/extensions/filters/listener): Listener filters which use the\\n89:     `Envoy::Extensions::ListenerFilters` namespace.\\n90:   * [filters/network/](/source/extensions/filters/network): L4 network filters which use the\\n91:     `Envoy::Extensions::NetworkFilters` namespace.\\n92:   * [formatters/](/source/extensions/formatters): Access log formatters which use the\\n93:     `Envoy::Extensions::Formatters` namespace.\\n94:   * [grpc_credentials/](/source/extensions/grpc_credentials): Custom gRPC credentials which use the\\n95:     `Envoy::Extensions::GrpcCredentials` namespace.\\n96:   * [health_checker/](/source/extensions/health_checker): Custom health checkers which use the\\n97:     `Envoy::Extensions::HealthCheckers` namespace.\\n98:   * [internal_redirect/](/source/extensions/internal_redirect): Internal Redirect\\n99:     extensions which use the `Envoy::Extensions::InternalRedirect` namespace.\\n100:   * [quic_listeners/](/source/extensions/quic_listeners): QUIC extensions which\\n101:     use the `Envoy::Quic` namespace.\\n102:   * [resource_monitors/](/source/extensions/resource_monitors): Resource monitor\\n103:     extensions which use the `Envoy::Extensions::ResourceMonitors` namespace.\\n104:   * [retry/](/source/extensions/retry): Retry extensions which use the\\n105:     `Envoy::Extensions::Retry` namespace.\\n106:   * [stat_sinks/](/source/extensions/stat_sinks): Stat sink implementations which use the\\n107:     `Envoy::Extensions::StatSinks` namespace.\\n108:   * [tracers/](/source/extensions/tracers): Tracers which use the\\n109:     `Envoy::Extensions::Tracers` namespace.\\n110:   * [transport_sockets/](/source/extensions/transport_sockets): Transport socket implementations\\n111:     which use the `Envoy::Extensions::TransportSockets` namespace.\\n112:   * [upstreams/](/source/extensions/upstreams): Upstream extensions use the\\n113:     `Envoy::Extensions::Upstreams` namespace.\\n114:   * [watchdog/](/source/extensions/watchdog): Watchdog extensions use the\\n115:     `Envoy::Extensions::Watchdog` namespace.\\n116:   * [rate_limit_descriptors/](/source/extensions/rate_limit_descriptors): Rate limit\\n117:     descriptor extensions use the `Envoy::Extensions::RateLimitDescriptors`\\n118:     namespace.\\n119: * Each extension is contained wholly in its own namespace. E.g.,\\n120:   `Envoy::Extensions::NetworkFilters::Echo`.\\n121: * Common code that is used by multiple extensions should be in a `common/` directory as close to\\n122:   the extensions as possible. E.g., [filters/common/](/source/extensions/filters/common) for common\\n123:   code that is used by both HTTP and network filters. Common code used only by two HTTP filters\\n124:   would be found in `filters/http/common/`. Common code should be placed in a common namespace.\\n125:   E.g., `Envoy::Extensions::Filters::Common`.\\n126: \\n127: ## [contrib](contrib/) layout\\n128: \\n129: This directory contains contrib extensions. {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01MRBUiDyCA7pWfL5tENABAu","type":"tool_result","content":"{\"content\":\"1: # Writing new tests\\n2: \\n3: The Envoy integration test framework is designed to make it simple to test downstream-Envoy-upstream\\n4: communication. In the common case, one\\n5: \\n6: - Sends a request from downstream through Envoy\\n7: - Verifies the request is received upstream, and possibly inspects elements of the headers or body\\n8: - Sends a response from upstream through Envoy\\n9: - Verifies the request is received downstream, again possibly inspecting headers and body\\n10: \\n11: For the simplest variant of this, one could do the following.\\n12: \\n13: ```c++\\n14: // start Envoy, set up the fake upstreams.\\n15: initialize();\\n16: \\n17: // Create a client aimed at Envoy’s default HTTP port.\\n18: codec_client_ = makeHttpConnection(makeClientConnection((lookupPort(\\\"http\\\"))));\\n19: \\n20: // Create some request headers.\\n21: Http::TestRequestHeaderMapImpl request_headers{{\\\":method\\\", \\\"GET\\\"},\\n22:                                                {\\\":path\\\", \\\"/test/long/url\\\"},\\n23:                                                {\\\":scheme\\\", \\\"http\\\"},\\n24:                                                {\\\":authority\\\", \\\"host\\\"}};\\n25: \\n26: // Send the request headers from the client, wait until they are received upstream. When they\\n27: // are received, send the default response headers from upstream and wait until they are\\n28: // received at by client\\n29: auto response = sendRequestAndWaitForResponse(request_headers, 0, default_response_headers_, 0);\\n30: \\n31: // Verify the proxied request was received upstream, as expected.\\n32: EXPECT_TRUE(upstream_request_->complete());\\n33: EXPECT_EQ(0U, upstream_request_->bodyLength());\\n34: // Verify the proxied response was received downstream, as expected.\\n35: EXPECT_TRUE(response->complete());\\n36: EXPECT_STREQ(\\\"200\\\", response->headers().Status()->value().c_str());\\n37: EXPECT_EQ(0U, response_->body().size());\\n38: ```\\n39: \\n40: Once you have the basic end-to-end test, it is fairly straight forward to modify it to test more\\n41: interesting corner cases. There are existing tests which send requests with bodies, have\\n42: downstream or upstream disconnect or time out, send multiple simultaneous requests on the same\\n43: connection, etc. Given that many of the disconnect/timeout cases are covered, a common case for\\n44: testing is covering a newly added configuration option.\\n45: \\n46: Most of Envoy's tests have been migrated from using [`json flatfiles`](../config/integration/) to\\n47: using a basic configuration defined as `basic_config` in [`config/utility.cc`](../config/utility.cc).\\n48: This configuration may be modified before the call to `initialize()`.\\n49: The [`ConfigHelper`](../config/utility.h) has utilities for common alterations such as:\\n50: \\n51: ```c++\\n52: // Set the default protocol to HTTP2\\n53: setDownstreamProtocol(Http::CodecType::HTTP2);\\n54: ```\\n55: \\n56: or\\n57: \\n58: ```c++\\n59: // Add a buffering filter on the request path\\n60: config_helper_.prependFilter(ConfigHelper::DEFAULT_BUFFER_FILTER);\\n61: ```\\n62: \\n63: For other edits which are less likely reusable, one can add config modifiers. Config modifiers\\n64: allow arbitrary modification of Envoy’s configuration just before Envoy is brought up. One can add\\n65: a config modifier to alter the bootstrap proto, one which affects the first `HttpConnectionManager`\\n66: object in the config, or mix and match. Config modifiers are operated on in the order they are\\n67: added, so one could, for example, modify the default `HttpConnectionManager`, duplicate the listening\\n68: config, and then change the first `HttpConnectionManager` to be different from the second.\\n69: \\n70: An example of modifying the bootstrap proto to overwrite runtime defaults:\\n71: \\n72: ```c++\\n73: config_helper_.addRuntimeOverride(\\\"Foo\\\", \\\"bar\\\");\\n74: });\\n75: ```\\n76: \\n77: An example of modifying `HttpConnectionManager` to change Envoy’s HTTP/1.1 processing:\\n78: \\n79: ```c++\\n80: config_helper_.addConfigModifier([&](envoy::extensions::filters::network::http_connection_manager::v3::HttpConnectionManager& hcm) -> void {\\n81:   nvoy::config::core::v3::Http1ProtocolOptions options;\\n82:   options.mutable_allow_absolute_url()->set_value(true);\\n83:   hcm.mutable_http_protocol_options()->CopyFrom(options);\\n84: };);\\n85: ```\\n86: \\n87: An example of modifying `HttpConnectionManager` to add an additional upstream\\n88: cluster:\\n89: \\n90: ```c++\\n91:    config_helper_.addConfigModifier([](envoy::config::bootstrap::v3::Bootstrap& bootstrap) {\\n92:       bootstrap.mutable_rate_limit_service()->set_cluster_name(\\\"ratelimit\\\");\\n93:       auto* ratelimit_cluster = bootstrap.mutable_static_resources()->add_clusters();\\n94:       ratelimit_cluster->MergeFrom(bootstrap.static_resources().clusters()[0]);\\n95:       ratelimit_cluster->set_name(\\\"ratelimit\\\");\\n96:       ConfigHelper::setHttp2(*ratelimit_cluster);\\n97:     });\\n98: ```\\n99: \\n100: In addition to the existing test framework, which allows for carefully timed interaction and ordering of events between downstream, Envoy, and Upstream, there is now an “autonomous” framework which simplifies the common case where the timing is not essential (or bidirectional streaming is desired). When AutonomousUpstream is used, by setting `autonomous_upstream_ = true` before `initialize()`, upstream will by default create AutonomousHttpConnections for each incoming connection and AutonomousStreams for each incoming stream. By default, the streams will respond to each complete request with “200 OK” and 10 bytes of payload, but this behavior can be altered by setting various request headers, as documented in [`autonomous_upstream.h`](autonomous_upstream.h)\\n101: \\n102: ## Common Problems\\n103: - If a response body length does not match the `content-length` header, any mock calls to wait for the response completion such as `sendRequestAndWaitForResponse` or `response_->waitForEndStream` could time out. Also, any asserts that the response was completed such as `EXPECT_TRUE(response_->complete())` could fail. Make sure that the response body length matches the `content-length` header.\\n104: \\n105: # Extending the test framework\\n106: \\n107: The Envoy integration test framework is most definitely a work in progress.\\n108: When encountering features which do not exist (actions for the autonomous\\n109: backend, testing new sections of configuration) please use your best judgement\\n110: if the changes will be needed by one specific test file, or will be likely\\n111: reused in other integration tests. If it's likely be reused, please add the\\n112: appropriate functions to existing utilities or add new test utilities. If it's\\n113: likely a one-off change, it can be scoped to the existing test file.\\n114: \\n115: # Debugging integration tests\\n116: \\n117: The Envoy integration test framework is generally designed to fast-fail when\\n118: things go wrong, with an explanatory message such as\\n119: \\\"Timed out waiting for new connection.\\\"\\n120: but it's not always clear what the underlying cause is. Because there are many\\n121: Envoy components under test, often the best tool for debugging is to try to get\\n122: a run of the test with `--test_arg=\\\"-l debug\\\"`, or `--test_arg=\\\"-l trace\\\"` ideally\\n123: with a clean run (if it's a code change which caused test breakage) or a comparable\\n124: test (if it's a new test failing). Looking at the conn_manager_impl.cc\\n125: logs, router.cc logs, and fake_upstream.cc logs, can often give you a feel for\\n126: what unexpected event is occurring. If that doesn't help, following the GDB\\n127: instructions to run the test in a debugger or sprinkling cerrs around are both often helpful.\\n128: \\n129: # Deflaking tests\\n130: \\n131: The instructions below assume the developer is running tests natively with bazel\\n132: rather than in docker. For developers using docker the best workaround today is\\n133: to replace `//test/...` on the relevant `ci/do_ci.sh`with the command lines\\n134: referenced below and remember to back those changes out before sending the fix\\n135: upstream!\\n136: \\n137: ## Reproducing test flakes\\n138: \\n139: The first step of fixing test flakes is reproducing the test flake. In general\\n140: if you have written a test which flakes, you can start by running\\n141: \\n142: ``\\n143: bazel test [test_name] --runs_per_test=1000\\n144: ``\\n145: \\n146: Which runs the full test many times. If this works, great!  If not, it's worth\\n147: trying to stress your system more by running more tests in parallel, by setting\\n148: `--jobs` and `--local_resources.`\\n149: \\n150: Once you've managed to reproduce a failure it may be beneficial to limit your\\n151: test run to the specific failing test(s) with `--gtest_filter`. This may cause\\n152: the test to flake less often (i.e. if two tests are interfering with each other,\\n153: scoping to your specific test name may harm rather than help reproducibility.)\\n154: but if it works it lets you iterate faster.\\n155: \\n156: Another helpful tip for debugging is turn turn up Envoy trace logs with\\n157: `--test_arg=\\\"-l trace\\\"`. Again if the test failure is due to a race, this may make\\n158: it harder to reproduce, and it may also hide any custom logging you add, but it's a\\n159: handy thing to know of to follow the general flow.\\n160: \\n161: The full command might look something like\\n162: \\n163: ```\\n164: bazel test //test/integration:http2_upstream_integration_test \\\\\\n165: --test_arg=--gtest_filter=\\\"IpVersions/Http2UpstreamIntegrationTest.RouterRequestAndResponseWithBodyNoBuffer/IPv6\\\" \\\\\\n166: --jobs 60 --local_test_jobs=60 --runs_per_test=1000 --test_arg=\\\"-l trace\\\"\\n167: ```\\n168: \\n169: For hard to reproduce flakes, a sometimes useful tool is `stress`, available via\\n170: `apt install stress`. Running stress alongsize `bazel test` (in another window,\\n171: starting it after the build completes) can be a great help in reproducing issues,\\n172: especially where tests are blocked on different things. For example, if a test\\n173: spends some time blocked on network traffic and has a cpu race, running many\\n174: instances of the test doesn't much help repro because the other instances aren't\\n175: using cpu at the critical moment. For this case, `stress -c [number of cores]`\\n176: can frequently make a 1/1000 flake into a 1/2 flake. Less commonly, for example,\\n177: unusually slow disk access can flake a test, in which case `stress --hdd 8`\\n178: helps boost the failure rate.\\n179: \\n180: ## Debugging test flakes\\n181: \\n182: Once you've managed to reproduce your test flake, you get to figure out what's\\n183: going on. If your failure mode isn't documented below, ideally some combination\\n184: of cerr << logging and trace logs will help you sort out what is going on (and\\n185: please add to this document as you figure it out!)\\n186: \\n187: \\n188: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/envoy--v1.32.1@b35dd17bea856e19fc4e65fb05e68170841d3726/-/blob/test/integration/README.md\"}"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"e91147b7-778e-4396-9da9-831fcb6d3019","uuid":"fe17a8c7-9432-4fec-9b30-ac01761946ec","tool_use_result":{"content":"{\"content\":\"1: # Writing new tests\\n2: \\n3: The Envoy integration test framework is designed to make it simple to test downstream-Envoy-upstream\\n4: communication. Config modifiers are operated on in the order they are\n67: added, so one could, for example, modify the default `HttpConnectionManager`, duplicate the listening\n68: config, and then change the first `HttpConnectionManager` to be different from the second.\n69: \n70: An example of modifying the bootstrap proto to overwrite runtime defaults:\n71: \n72: ```c++\n73: config_helper_.addRuntimeOverride(\"Foo\", \"bar\");\n74: });\n75: ```\n76: \n77: An example of modifying `HttpConnectionManager` to change Envoy’s HTTP/1.1 processing:\n78: \n79: ```c++\n80: config_helper_.addConfigModifier([&](envoy::extensions::filters::network::http_connection_manager::v3::HttpConnectionManager& hcm) -> void {\n81:   nvoy::config::core::v3::Http1ProtocolOptions options;\n82:   options.mutable_allow_absolute_url()->set_value(true);\n83:   hcm.mutable_http_protocol_options()->CopyFrom(options);\n84: };);\n85: ```\n86: \n87: An example of modifying `HttpConnectionManager` to add an additional upstream\n88: cluster:\n89: \n90: ```c++\n91:    config_helper_.addConfigModifier([](envoy::config::bootstrap::v3::Bootstrap& bootstrap) {\n92:       bootstrap.mutable_rate_limit_service()->set_cluster_name(\"ratelimit\");\n93:       auto* ratelimit_cluster = bootstrap.mutable_static_resources()->add_clusters();\n94:       ratelimit_cluster->MergeFrom(bootstrap.static_resources().clusters()[0]);\n95:       ratelimit_cluster->set_name(\"ratelimit\");\n96:       ConfigHelper::setHttp2(*ratelimit_cluster);\n97:     });\n98: ```\n99: \n100: In addition to the existing test framework, which allows for carefully timed interaction and ordering of events between downstream, Envoy, and Upstream, there is now an “autonomous” framework which simplifies the common case where the timing is not essential (or bidirectional streaming is desired). When AutonomousUpstream is used, by setting `autonomous_upstream_ = true` before `initialize()`, upstream will by default create AutonomousHttpConnections for each incoming connection and AutonomousStreams for each incoming stream. By default, the streams will respond to each complete request with “200 OK” and 10 bytes of payload, but this behavior can be altered by setting various request headers, as documented in [`autonomous_upstream.h`](autonomous_upstream.h)\n101: \n102: ## Common Problems\n103: - If a response body length does not match the `content-length` header, any mock calls to wait for the response completion such as `sendRequestAndWaitForResponse` or `response_->waitForEndStream` could time out. Also, any asserts that the response was completed such as `EXPECT_TRUE(response_->complete())` could fail. Make sure that the response body length matches the `content-length` header.\n104: \n105: # Extending the test framework\n106: \n107: The Envoy integration test framework is most definitely a work in progress.\n108: When encountering features which do not exist (actions for the autonomous\n109: backend, testing new sections of configuration) please use your best judgement\n110: if the changes will be needed by one specific test file, or will be likely\n111: reused in other integration tests. If it's likely be reused, please add the\n112: appropriate functions to existing utilities or add new test utilities. If it's\n113: likely a one-off change, it can be scoped to the existing test file.\n114: \n115: # Debugging integration tests\n116: \n117: The Envoy integration test framework is generally designed to fast-fail when\n118: things go wrong, with an explanatory message such as\n119: \"Timed out waiting for new connection.\"\n120: but it's not always clear what the underlying cause is. Because there are many\n121: Envoy components under test, often the best tool for debugging is to try to get\n122: a run of the test with `--test_arg=\"-l debug\"`, or `--test_arg=\"-l trace\"` ideally\n123: with a clean run (if it's a code change which caused test breakage) or a comparable\n124: test (if it's a new test failing). Looking at the conn_manager_impl.cc\n125: logs, router.cc logs, and fake_upstream.cc logs, can often give you a feel for\n126: what unexpected event is occurring. If that doesn't help, following the GDB\n127: instructions to run the test in a debugger or sprinkling cerrs around are both often helpful.\n128: \n129: # Deflaking tests\n130: \n131: The instructions below assume the developer is running tests natively with bazel\n132: rather than in docker. For developers using docker the best workaround today is\n133: to replace `//test/...` on the relevant `ci/do_ci.sh`with the command lines\n134: referenced below and remember to back those changes out before sending the fix\n135: upstream!\n136: \n137: ## Reproducing test flakes\n138: \n139: The first step of fixing test flakes is reproducing the test flake. In general\n140: if you have written a test which flakes, you can start by running\n141: \n142: ``\n143: bazel test [test_name] --runs_per_test=1000\n144: ``\n145: \n146: Which runs the full test many times. If this works, great!  If not, it's worth\n147: trying to stress your system more by running more tests in parallel, by setting\n148: `--jobs` and `--local_resources.`\n149: \n150: Once you've managed to reproduce a failure it may be beneficial to limit your\n151: test run to the specific failing test(s) with `--gtest_filter`. This may cause\n152: the test to flake less often (i.e. if two tests are interfering with each other,\n153: scoping to your specific test name may harm rather than help reproducibility.)\n154: but if it works it lets you iterate faster.\n155: \n156: Another helpful tip for debugging is turn turn up Envoy trace logs with\n157: `--test_arg=\"-l trace\"`. Again if the test failure is due to a race, this may make\n158: it harder to reproduce, and it may also hide any custom logging you add, but it's a\n159: handy thing to know of to follow the general flow.\n160: \n161: The full command might look something like\n162: \n163: ```\n164: bazel test //test/integration:http2_upstream_integration_test \\\n165: --test_arg=--gtest_filter=\"IpVersions/Http2UpstreamIntegrationTest.RouterRequestAndResponseWithBodyNoBuffer/IPv6\" \\\n166: --jobs 60 --local_test_jobs=60 --runs_per_test=1000 --test_arg=\"-l trace\"\n167: ```\n168: \n169: For hard to reproduce flakes, a sometimes useful tool is `stress`, available via\n170: `apt install stress`. Running stress alongsize `bazel test` (in another window,\n171: starting it after the build completes) can be a great help in reproducing issues,\n172: especially where tests are blocked on different things. For example, if a test\n173: spends some time blocked on network traffic and has a cpu race, running many\n174: instances of the test doesn't much help repro because the other instances aren't\n175: using cpu at the critical moment. For this case, `stress -c [number of cores]`\n176: can frequently make a 1/1000 flake into a 1/2 flake. Less commonly, for example,\n177: unusually slow disk access can flake a test, in which case `stress --hdd 8`\n178: helps boost the failure rate.\n179: \n180: ## Debugging test flakes\n181: \n182: Once you've managed to reproduce your test flake, you get to figure out what's\n183: going on. If your failure mode isn't documented below, ideally some combination\n184: of cerr << logging and trace logs will help you sort out what is going on (and\n185: please add to this document as you figure it out!)\n186: \n187: \n188: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/envoy--v1.32.1@b35dd17bea856e19fc4e65fb05e68170841d3726/-/blob/test/integration/README.md"}}}

Build Prerequisites\n\nEnvoy requires the following tools and dependencies before building:\n\n### Core Tools\n- **Bazel/Bazelisk**: The Envoy project uses Bazel as its build system. It's recommended to use [Bazelisk](https://github.com/bazelbuild/bazelisk) which automatically manages Bazel versions.\n  - **Linux**: Install via `sudo wget -O /usr/local/bin/bazel https://github.com/bazelbuild/bazelisk/releases/latest/download/bazelisk-linux-$([ $(uname -m) = \"aarch64\" ] && echo \"arm64\" || echo \"amd64\")` and `sudo chmod +x /usr/local/bin/bazel`\n  - **macOS**: Install via `brew install bazelisk`\n  - **Windows**: Download from [Bazelisk releases](https://github.com/bazelbuild/bazelisk/releases) and add to PATH\n\n### Build Dependencies\nThe following are required for building Envoy in production environments. For development, Docker containers are recommended (see section on CI Docker images).\n\n- C++ compiler (Clang 14 or GCC 9+)\n- Python 3.6+\n- Git\n\n### Development Docker Images\nFor a self-contained development environment, use the official Envoy build Docker images:\n- **Linux**: `envoyproxy/envoy-build-ubuntu` (based on Ubuntu 20.04)\n- **CentOS**: `envoyproxy/envoy-build-centos` (experimental, based on CentOS 7)\n- **Windows**: `envoyproxy/envoy-build-windows2019` (official Windows support ended August 2023)\n\nRetrieve the specific image SHA from `ci/envoy_build_sha.sh`.\n\n### Setup Development Support Toolchain\nBefore contributing, install the development support toolchain for automatic DCO signoff and pre-commit format checking:\n\n```bash\n./support/bootstrap\n```\n\nThis installs Git hooks from `support/hooks/` that:\n- Automatically append DCO signoff to commits\n- Run format and lint checks before push\n\nDocumentation: See `support/README.md`\n\n---\n\n## 2. Build System\n\nEnvoy uses **Bazel** as its build system. All build configuration is defined in `BUILD` files and `.bazelrc` configuration files.\n\n### Key Build Concepts\n- **BUILD files**: Located throughout the codebase, define build targets using Bazel rules\n- **.bazelrc**: Main configuration file in the repository root\n- **Bazel rules**: Custom Envoy-specific rules defined in `bazel/` directory (e.g., `envoy_cc_library`, `envoy_cc_extension`, etc.)\n\n### Building for Development\n\n#### Using Docker (Recommended)\nThe easiest way to build for development is using the provided Docker script:\n\n```bash\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh dev'\n```\n\nThis builds Envoy with fastbuild configuration inside a standardized container. Output binary: `/tmp/envoy-docker-build/envoy/source/exe/envoy-fastbuild`\n\nControl output directory with environment variable:\n```bash\nENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR=~/build ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh dev'\n```\n\n#### Direct Bazel Commands (Linux/macOS)\nIf you have build dependencies installed locally:\n\n```bash\n# Development build (fastbuild, fastest)\nbazel build -c fastbuild //source/exe:envoy-static\n\n# Release build (optimized)\nbazel build -c opt //source/exe:envoy-static\n\n# Debug build (with symbols)\nbazel build -c dbg //source/exe:envoy-static\n\n# Build a specific test\nbazel build //test/common/network:connection_test\n```\n\n### Build Configurations Available\n\n#### Via `./ci/do_ci.sh <TARGET>` in Docker:\n- **dev** — fastbuild with tests\n- **dev <test>** — fastbuild for specific test\n- **debug** — dbg configuration with tests\n- **debug <test>** — dbg for specific test\n- **release** — opt configuration with tests\n- **release <test>** — opt for specific test\n- **release.server_only** — opt configuration, binary only\n- **debug.server_only** — dbg configuration, binary only\n- **asan** — ASAN sanitizer build with tests\n- **msan** — MSAN sanitizer build with tests\n- **tsan** — TSAN sanitizer build with tests\n- **coverage** — coverage build with gcc\n- **compile_time_options** — test various compile flags\n- **format** — run formatting and linting\n- **clang_tidy** — run clang-tidy analysis\n\n### Building Extensions and Specific Components\n\nTo build only specific packages (not the entire repo):\n\n```bash\n# Build HTTP connection manager filter\nbazel build //source/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager:config_lib\n\n# Build and test HTTP filters\nbazel test //source/extensions/filters/http/...\n```\n\n### Build File Structure\n\nCore Bazel rules used in Envoy:\n- `envoy_cc_library` — C++ library\n- `envoy_cc_binary` — C++ binary\n- `envoy_cc_test` — C++ unit test\n- `envoy_cc_extension` — Extension (filter, etc.)\n- `envoy_integration_test` — Integration test\n- `envoy_benchmark_test` — Benchmark test\n\nLocation: `bazel/envoy_build_system.bzl` and `bazel/DEVELOPER.md`\n\n---\n\n## 3. Running Tests\n\nEnvoy uses **Google Test** framework for unit tests and a custom integration test framework for end-to-end testing.\n\n### Test Frameworks\n\n1. **Google Test (gtest)**: Unit tests using Google Test macros (EXPECT_*, ASSERT_*)\n2. **Google Mock (gmock)**: Mocking and matchers for unit tests\n3. **Integration Test Framework**: Custom framework in `test/integration/` for downstream-Envoy-upstream testing\n4. **Benchmark Tests**: Performance testing via Google Benchmark\n\n### Running All Tests\n\n#### Using Docker (Recommended):\n```bash\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh dev'\n```\n\n#### Direct Bazel:\n```bash\n# Run all tests in fastbuild\nbazel test -c fastbuild //test/...\n\n# Run with test args (e.g., verbose output)\nbazel test -c fastbuild //test/... --test_arg=\"-l trace\"\n\n# Run with multiple jobs for parallelization\nbazel test -c fastbuild //test/... --jobs 60\n```\n\n### Running Specific Tests\n\n```bash\n# Run all tests in a directory\nbazel test //test/common/network:*\n\n# Run a specific test file\nbazel test //test/common/network:connection_test\n\n# Run a specific test case\nbazel test //test/common/network:connection_test --test_filter=\"ConnectionTest.Accepted\"\n\n# Run integration tests\nbazel test //test/integration:http_integration_test\n```\n\n### Integration Tests\n\nIntegration tests validate end-to-end downstream-Envoy-upstream communication. They're located in `test/integration/`:\n\n```bash\nbazel test //test/integration:http_integration_test\nbazel test //test/integration:http2_upstream_integration_test\n```\n\nIntegration tests can be parameterized to run with different configurations (IPv4/IPv6, HTTP/1.1, HTTP/2, etc.).\n\n### Test Coverage\n\nEnvoy requires **100% test coverage for added code**. Generate coverage reports:\n\n```bash\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh coverage'\n```\n\nCoverage output: `$ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR/envoy/generated/coverage/coverage.html`\n\nOr for a specific test:\n```bash\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh coverage //test/common/network:connection_test'\n```\n\n### Test Utilities and Helpers\n\nKey test utilities located in `test/`:\n- `test/test_common/` — Common test utilities\n- `test/mocks/` — Mock implementations of core interfaces\n- `test/integration/` — Integration test framework\n- `test/config/` — Configuration utilities for tests\n\nImportant test macros and patterns (from `test/README.md`):\n- `EXPECT_THAT()` with `HeaderValueOf()`, `HttpStatusIs()`, etc. for HTTP testing\n- `SimulatedTimeSystem` for deterministic time-based tests\n- `Event::TestTimeSystem` for controlling time in tests\n\n---\n\n## 4. CI Pipeline\n\nEnvoy uses **Azure Pipelines** as the primary CI system, with additional tooling for distributed testing.\n\n### CI Platform: Azure Pipelines\n\nAzure Pipelines automatically runs on all pull requests to `envoyproxy/envoy`. Access it at:\nhttps://dev.azure.com/cncf/envoy/_build\n\n### CI Configuration Files\n\n- **`.azure-pipelines/`** — Main CI configuration directory (not present in this version but referenced in README.md)\n- **`ci/do_ci.sh`** — Main CI script that orchestrates builds and tests\n- **`ci/run_envoy_docker.sh`** — Docker runner for local CI reproduction\n- **`ci/mac_ci_steps.sh`** — macOS-specific build and test steps\n- **`ci/mac_ci_setup.sh`** — macOS dependency installation via Homebrew\n- **`ci/windows_ci_steps.sh`** — Windows build and test steps (deprecated)\n\n### CI Checks Run on Pull Requests\n\n1. **Compilation**: Build Envoy with multiple configurations (fastbuild, opt, dbg)\n2. **Testing**: Run full unit and integration test suite\n3. **Sanitizers**: ASAN, MSAN, TSAN builds and tests\n4. **Format Checking**: Code formatting, clang-tidy, proto format validation\n5. **Coverage**: Coverage build and analysis\n6. **Platform-Specific**: macOS builds via Azure Pipelines\n\n### CI Targets\n\nAll CI targets can be run locally via:\n```bash\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh <TARGET>'\n```\n\nWhere `<TARGET>` is one of: `api`, `asan`, `debug`, `dev`, `dev.contrib`, `release`, `sizeopt`, `coverage`, `msan`, `tsan`, `fuzz`, `compile_time_options`, `clang_tidy`, `format`, `check_proto_format`, `docs`.\n\n### CI Timing\n\n- Typical full CI run: **30-45 minutes**\n- Can be parallelized across multiple machines/jobs\n- PRs are checked against main branch\n\n### Triggering CI Reruns\n\nTo rerun CI without making code changes:\n\n1. **Retest failed tasks**: Add comment `/retest` to PR\n2. **Full rerun**: Push empty commit: `git commit -s --allow-empty -m 'Kick CI' && git push` (or use alias from `.gitconfig`)\n\n### Distributed Testing Infrastructure\n\n- **Remote Build Cache**: Optional for faster rebuilds\n- **RBE (Remote Build Execution)**: Can be configured for distributed test execution\n- **Bazel CI Integration**: `.bazelci/` directory contains Bazel-specific CI configs\n\n---\n\n## 5. Code Review Process\n\n### Contribution Workflow\n\n1. **Discuss major features**: Before starting work on features >100 LOC or behavior changes, open a GitHub issue to discuss with maintainers\n2. **Small patches**: Bug fixes and small patches don't require prior discussion\n3. **Fork and branch**: Fork the repository and create a feature branch\n4. **Local hooks**: Run `./support/bootstrap` to install pre-commit hooks\n5. **Code and test**: Write code and tests (100% coverage required)\n6. **Documentation**: Update docs and release notes for user-facing changes\n7. **Commit message**: Follow format: `subsystem: description`\n8. **Create PR**: Push to your fork and create PR against `main` branch\n\n### Pull Request Requirements\n\n**Before submitting:**\n- All tests pass locally\n- 100% test coverage for new code\n- Code follows `STYLE.md` guidelines\n- Commit has DCO signoff (automatic via `./support/bootstrap`)\n- Release notes added to `changelogs/current.yaml` if user-facing\n- Documentation updated in `docs/` if applicable\n\n**PR Title Format:**\n- Lowercase component/subsystem name followed by colon\n- Examples:\n  - `docs: fix grammar error`\n  - `http conn man: add new feature`\n  - `router: add x-envoy-overloaded header`\n\n**PR Description Fields** (see `PULL_REQUEST_TEMPLATE.md`):\n- **Commit Message**: What the PR does, behavior changes, bug fixes\n- **Additional Description**: Extra context for reviewers\n- **Risk Level**: Low, Medium, or High\n- **Testing**: What testing was performed\n- **Documentation**: Documentation changes\n- **Release Notes**: User-facing impact\n- **Issues**: Link with `Fixes #XXX` to auto-close issues\n\n### Code Style\n\n**File:** `STYLE.md`\n\nKey requirements:\n- **Formatting**: clang-format (checked automatically)\n- **Line length**: Max 100 columns\n- **Naming**: camelCase for functions (lowercase start), PascalCase for enums, `foo_` for member variables\n- **Language**: Google C++ style guide with Envoy deviations\n- **Tests**: Default to StrictMock for Google Mock\n- **Comments**: Use GitHub username in TODOs, e.g., `TODO(username): description`\n- **Inclusive Language**: No whitelist/blacklist/master/slave terminology\n\n### Code Review and Merging\n\n**Review Process:**\n- PR assigned to maintainer automatically\n- Expected turnaround: within one business day\n- Typically requires one senior maintainer review + domain expert\n- For new extensions: at least one approval from different organization than author\n- Anyone can review, but maintainers must approve\n\n**Before Merging:**\n- All tests pass in CI\n- All comments resolved\n- **Don't rebase after review starts** — use merge instead (CI will squash on merge)\n- PR title and description cleaned up by maintainer\n- Original PR author's DCO signoff preserved\n\n### DCO Sign-off (Developer Certificate of Origin)\n\nAll commits must be signed off with DCO. This is automatic if you run `./support/bootstrap`.\n\n**Manual sign-off:**\n```bash\ngit commit -s -m \"message\"\n# Or set up aliases\ngit config --add alias.c \"commit -s\"\ngit config --add alias.amend \"commit -s --amend\"\n```\n\n**If DCO check fails**, squash commits and add signoff:\n```bash\ngit rebase -i HEAD^^\n# Then fix signoff and force push (only for DCO fixes)\ngit push origin -f\n```\n\n### Breaking Changes and Deprecation\n\n- **API deprecation**: Must implement conversion and add tests with `DEPRECATED_FEATURE_TEST()` macro\n- **Configuration deprecation**: Must document in `changelogs/current.yaml`\n- **Breaking changes**: Clear deprecation path (warn, then fail) with runtime override option\n- **Runtime guarding**: High-risk changes should be guarded with `Runtime::runtimeFeatureEnabled(\"envoy.reloadable_features.feature_name\")`\n\nFor details, see `CONTRIBUTING.md` Breaking Change Policy section.\n\n### Getting Help\n\n- **Mailing Lists**:\n  - `envoy-dev@groups.google.com` — Developer discussion\n  - `envoy-announce@groups.google.com` — Announcements\n  - `envoy-users@groups.google.com` — User discussion\n  - `envoy-maintainers@groups.google.com` — Reach all maintainers\n\n- **Slack**: https://envoyproxy.slack.com/ (get invite at https://communityinviter.com/apps/envoyproxy/envoy)\n- **Issues**: Use GitHub Issues for bugs and feature discussions\n- **CODEOWNERS**: See `CODEOWNERS` file to find domain experts\n\n---\n\n## 6. Developer Workflow Example\n\n### Concrete Example: Fix HTTP Connection Manager Bug\n\nThis example walks through fixing a bug in the HTTP connection manager filter from cloning to PR merge.\n\n#### Step 1: Setup\n\n```bash\n# Clone the repository\ngit clone https://github.com/YOUR-USERNAME/envoy.git\ncd envoy\n\n# Install development toolchain\n./support/bootstrap\n\n# Create feature branch\ngit checkout -b bugfix/http-connman-fix\n\n# Make sure you're on the latest main\ngit checkout main\ngit pull origin main\ngit checkout bugfix/http-connman-fix\ngit merge main\n```\n\n#### Step 2: Locate the Code\n\nThe HTTP connection manager filter is in:\n- **Source**: `source/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/`\n- **Headers**: `envoy/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/http_connection_manager.h`\n- **Tests**: `test/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/`\n- **Config proto**: `api/envoy/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/v3/`\n\nStart by exploring the test files to understand existing behavior:\n```bash\n# Run existing tests\nbazel test //test/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager:*\n```\n\n#### Step 3: Write Tests First\n\nCreate or modify test in `test/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/conn_manager_test.cc`:\n\n```cpp\n#include \"test/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/config_test_base.h\"\n#include \"test/mocks/http/mocks.h\"\n\n// Add test for the bug\nTEST(HttpConnectionManagerTest, FixedBugBehavior) {\n  // Arrange: Set up test fixtures\n  // Act: Trigger the bug scenario\n  // Assert: Verify expected behavior after fix\n}\n```\n\nRun the test to confirm it fails:\n```bash\nbazel test //test/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager:conn_manager_test --test_filter=\"HttpConnectionManagerTest.FixedBugBehavior\"\n```\n\n#### Step 4: Implement the Fix\n\nEdit the source code:\n```bash\n# Main source files\nvi source/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/conn_manager_impl.cc\nvi source/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/conn_manager_impl.h\n```\n\nRun tests to verify fix:\n```bash\nbazel test //test/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager:conn_manager_test --test_filter=\"HttpConnectionManagerTest.FixedBugBehavior\"\n```\n\n#### Step 5: Verify Full Test Coverage\n\nEnsure 100% coverage for modified code:\n```bash\n# Run all HTTP connection manager tests\nbazel test //test/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager:*\n\n# Run broader test suite\nbazel test //test/extensions/filters/network/...\n```\n\n#### Step 6: Format Code\n\nAuto-format and check for issues:\n```bash\n# Using support toolchain hooks (automatic on commit)\n# Or manually:\nbazel run //tools/code_format:check_format -- fix\n\n# Check clang-tidy\nbazel run //tools/code:check -- fix -s main -v warn\n```\n\nOr in Docker:\n```bash\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh format'\n```\n\n#### Step 7: Documentation and Release Notes\n\nIf this is a user-facing fix:\n\n1. **Update release notes** in `changelogs/current.yaml`:\n```yaml\n- area: http\n  change: |\n    Fixed HTTP connection manager bug where [description]. This can be reverted with runtime guard\n    `envoy.reloadable_features.fixed_http_connman_bug` if needed.\n```\n\n2. **Update docs** if API changes:\n   - Proto inline docs in `api/envoy/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/v3/`\n   - User docs in `docs/root/configuration/listeners/`\n\n#### Step 8: Commit and Push\n\n```bash\n# Stage changes\ngit add source/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/\ngit add test/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/\ngit add changelogs/current.yaml\ngit add docs/\n\n# Commit with DCO sign-off (automatic via bootstrap hook)\ngit commit -m \"http conn man: fix bug with connection handling\n\nFixes a critical bug where [specific issue] was causing [impact].\n\nThe fix ensures that [how it's fixed].\n\nFixes #1234\"\n\n# Push to your fork\ngit push origin bugfix/http-connman-fix\n```\n\n#### Step 9: Create Pull Request\n\nOn GitHub:\n1. Go to your fork, create PR against `main` branch\n2. Fill in PR template:\n   - **Title**: `http conn man: fix connection handling bug`\n   - **Risk**: `Medium` (fixes existing code path)\n   - **Testing**: \"All unit and integration tests pass. Added test case `FixedBugBehavior` to verify fix.\"\n   - **Documentation**: Updated `changelogs/current.yaml` with release notes\n   - **Release Notes**: Added to changelogs/current.yaml\n\n#### Step 10: CI Verification\n\nGitHub automatically runs full CI suite:\n- Wait for all checks to pass (typically 30-45 minutes)\n- If failures occur, check error messages and iterate:\n  ```bash\n  git log --oneline -1\n  # Make fix\n  git commit -s --amend\n  git push origin bugfix/http-connman-fix --force-with-lease\n  ```\n\n  **Important**: Don't force push after a maintainer starts reviewing\n\n#### Step 11: Code Review\n\n1. Maintainer assigned automatically\n2. May request changes or clarifications\n3. Update code if needed without rebasing (add new commits instead)\n4. Maintainer cleans up title/message and merges\n\n#### Step 12: Post-Merge\n\n1. PR is squash-merged to `main`\n2. Your branch can be deleted\n3. Monitor for any issues in releases\n\n---\n\n## Additional Resources\n\n### Key Documentation Files\n\n- **DEVELOPER.md** — Developer setup and workflows\n- **CONTRIBUTING.md** — Full contribution
