Build Prerequisites\n\nEnvoy requires the following tools and dependencies before building:\n\n### Core Tools\n- **Bazel/Bazelisk**: The Envoy project uses Bazel as its build system. It's recommended to use [Bazelisk](https://github.com/bazelbuild/bazelisk) which automatically manages Bazel versions.\n  - **Linux**: Install via `sudo wget -O /usr/local/bin/bazel https://github.com/bazelbuild/bazelisk/releases/latest/download/bazelisk-linux-$([ $(uname -m) = \"aarch64\" ] && echo \"arm64\" || echo \"amd64\")` and `sudo chmod +x /usr/local/bin/bazel`\n  - **macOS**: Install via `brew install bazelisk`\n  - **Windows**: Download from [Bazelisk releases](https://github.com/bazelbuild/bazelisk/releases) and add to PATH\n\n### Build Dependencies\nThe following are required for building Envoy in production environments. For development, Docker containers are recommended (see section on CI Docker images).\n\n- C++ compiler (Clang 14 or GCC 9+)\n- Python 3.6+\n- Git\n\n### Development Docker Images\nFor a self-contained development environment, use the official Envoy build Docker images:\n- **Linux**: `envoyproxy/envoy-build-ubuntu` (based on Ubuntu 20.04)\n- **CentOS**: `envoyproxy/envoy-build-centos` (experimental, based on CentOS 7)\n- **Windows**: `envoyproxy/envoy-build-windows2019` (official Windows support ended August 2023)\n\nRetrieve the specific image SHA from `ci/envoy_build_sha.sh`.\n\n### Setup Development Support Toolchain\nBefore contributing, install the development support toolchain for automatic DCO signoff and pre-commit format checking:\n\n```bash\n./support/bootstrap\n```\n\nThis installs Git hooks from `support/hooks/` that:\n- Automatically append DCO signoff to commits\n- Run format and lint checks before push\n\nDocumentation: See `support/README.md`\n\n---\n\n## 2. Build System\n\nEnvoy uses **Bazel** as its build system. All build configuration is defined in `BUILD` files and `.bazelrc` configuration files.\n\n### Key Build Concepts\n- **BUILD files**: Located throughout the codebase, define build targets using Bazel rules\n- **.bazelrc**: Main configuration file in the repository root\n- **Bazel rules**: Custom Envoy-specific rules defined in `bazel/` directory (e.g., `envoy_cc_library`, `envoy_cc_extension`, etc.)\n\n### Building for Development\n\n#### Using Docker (Recommended)\nThe easiest way to build for development is using the provided Docker script:\n\n```bash\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh dev'\n```\n\nThis builds Envoy with fastbuild configuration inside a standardized container. Output binary: `/tmp/envoy-docker-build/envoy/source/exe/envoy-fastbuild`\n\nControl output directory with environment variable:\n```bash\nENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR=~/build ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh dev'\n```\n\n#### Direct Bazel Commands (Linux/macOS)\nIf you have build dependencies installed locally:\n\n```bash\n# Development build (fastbuild, fastest)\nbazel build -c fastbuild //source/exe:envoy-static\n\n# Release build (optimized)\nbazel build -c opt //source/exe:envoy-static\n\n# Debug build (with symbols)\nbazel build -c dbg //source/exe:envoy-static\n\n# Build a specific test\nbazel build //test/common/network:connection_test\n```\n\n### Build Configurations Available\n\n#### Via `./ci/do_ci.sh <TARGET>` in Docker:\n- **dev** — fastbuild with tests\n- **dev <test>** — fastbuild for specific test\n- **debug** — dbg configuration with tests\n- **debug <test>** — dbg for specific test\n- **release** — opt configuration with tests\n- **release <test>** — opt for specific test\n- **release.server_only** — opt configuration, binary only\n- **debug.server_only** — dbg configuration, binary only\n- **asan** — ASAN sanitizer build with tests\n- **msan** — MSAN sanitizer build with tests\n- **tsan** — TSAN sanitizer build with tests\n- **coverage** — coverage build with gcc\n- **compile_time_options** — test various compile flags\n- **format** — run formatting and linting\n- **clang_tidy** — run clang-tidy analysis\n\n### Building Extensions and Specific Components\n\nTo build only specific packages (not the entire repo):\n\n```bash\n# Build HTTP connection manager filter\nbazel build //source/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager:config_lib\n\n# Build and test HTTP filters\nbazel test //source/extensions/filters/http/...\n```\n\n### Build File Structure\n\nCore Bazel rules used in Envoy:\n- `envoy_cc_library` — C++ library\n- `envoy_cc_binary` — C++ binary\n- `envoy_cc_test` — C++ unit test\n- `envoy_cc_extension` — Extension (filter, etc.)\n- `envoy_integration_test` — Integration test\n- `envoy_benchmark_test` — Benchmark test\n\nLocation: `bazel/envoy_build_system.bzl` and `bazel/DEVELOPER.md`\n\n---\n\n## 3. Running Tests\n\nEnvoy uses **Google Test** framework for unit tests and a custom integration test framework for end-to-end testing.\n\n### Test Frameworks\n\n1. **Google Test (gtest)**: Unit tests using Google Test macros (EXPECT_*, ASSERT_*)\n2. **Google Mock (gmock)**: Mocking and matchers for unit tests\n3. **Integration Test Framework**: Custom framework in `test/integration/` for downstream-Envoy-upstream testing\n4. **Benchmark Tests**: Performance testing via Google Benchmark\n\n### Running All Tests\n\n#### Using Docker (Recommended):\n```bash\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh dev'\n```\n\n#### Direct Bazel:\n```bash\n# Run all tests in fastbuild\nbazel test -c fastbuild //test/...\n\n# Run with test args (e.g., verbose output)\nbazel test -c fastbuild //test/... --test_arg=\"-l trace\"\n\n# Run with multiple jobs for parallelization\nbazel test -c fastbuild //test/... --jobs 60\n```\n\n### Running Specific Tests\n\n```bash\n# Run all tests in a directory\nbazel test //test/common/network:*\n\n# Run a specific test file\nbazel test //test/common/network:connection_test\n\n# Run a specific test case\nbazel test //test/common/network:connection_test --test_filter=\"ConnectionTest.Accepted\"\n\n# Run integration tests\nbazel test //test/integration:http_integration_test\n```\n\n### Integration Tests\n\nIntegration tests validate end-to-end downstream-Envoy-upstream communication. They're located in `test/integration/`:\n\n```bash\nbazel test //test/integration:http_integration_test\nbazel test //test/integration:http2_upstream_integration_test\n```\n\nIntegration tests can be parameterized to run with different configurations (IPv4/IPv6, HTTP/1.1, HTTP/2, etc.).\n\n### Test Coverage\n\nEnvoy requires **100% test coverage for added code**. Generate coverage reports:\n\n```bash\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh coverage'\n```\n\nCoverage output: `$ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR/envoy/generated/coverage/coverage.html`\n\nOr for a specific test:\n```bash\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh coverage //test/common/network:connection_test'\n```\n\n### Test Utilities and Helpers\n\nKey test utilities located in `test/`:\n- `test/test_common/` — Common test utilities\n- `test/mocks/` — Mock implementations of core interfaces\n- `test/integration/` — Integration test framework\n- `test/config/` — Configuration utilities for tests\n\nImportant test macros and patterns (from `test/README.md`):\n- `EXPECT_THAT()` with `HeaderValueOf()`, `HttpStatusIs()`, etc. for HTTP testing\n- `SimulatedTimeSystem` for deterministic time-based tests\n- `Event::TestTimeSystem` for controlling time in tests\n\n---\n\n## 4. CI Pipeline\n\nEnvoy uses **Azure Pipelines** as the primary CI system, with additional tooling for distributed testing.\n\n### CI Platform: Azure Pipelines\n\nAzure Pipelines automatically runs on all pull requests to `envoyproxy/envoy`. Access it at:\nhttps://dev.azure.com/cncf/envoy/_build\n\n### CI Configuration Files\n\n- **`.azure-pipelines/`** — Main CI configuration directory (not present in this version but referenced in README.md)\n- **`ci/do_ci.sh`** — Main CI script that orchestrates builds and tests\n- **`ci/run_envoy_docker.sh`** — Docker runner for local CI reproduction\n- **`ci/mac_ci_steps.sh`** — macOS-specific build and test steps\n- **`ci/mac_ci_setup.sh`** — macOS dependency installation via Homebrew\n- **`ci/windows_ci_steps.sh`** — Windows build and test steps (deprecated)\n\n### CI Checks Run on Pull Requests\n\n1. **Compilation**: Build Envoy with multiple configurations (fastbuild, opt, dbg)\n2. **Testing**: Run full unit and integration test suite\n3. **Sanitizers**: ASAN, MSAN, TSAN builds and tests\n4. **Format Checking**: Code formatting, clang-tidy, proto format validation\n5. **Coverage**: Coverage build and analysis\n6. **Platform-Specific**: macOS builds via Azure Pipelines\n\n### CI Targets\n\nAll CI targets can be run locally via:\n```bash\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh <TARGET>'\n```\n\nWhere `<TARGET>` is one of: `api`, `asan`, `debug`, `dev`, `dev.contrib`, `release`, `sizeopt`, `coverage`, `msan`, `tsan`, `fuzz`, `compile_time_options`, `clang_tidy`, `format`, `check_proto_format`, `docs`.\n\n### CI Timing\n\n- Typical full CI run: **30-45 minutes**\n- Can be parallelized across multiple machines/jobs\n- PRs are checked against main branch\n\n### Triggering CI Reruns\n\nTo rerun CI without making code changes:\n\n1. **Retest failed tasks**: Add comment `/retest` to PR\n2. **Full rerun**: Push empty commit: `git commit -s --allow-empty -m 'Kick CI' && git push` (or use alias from `.gitconfig`)\n\n### Distributed Testing Infrastructure\n\n- **Remote Build Cache**: Optional for faster rebuilds\n- **RBE (Remote Build Execution)**: Can be configured for distributed test execution\n- **Bazel CI Integration**: `.bazelci/` directory contains Bazel-specific CI configs\n\n---\n\n## 5. Code Review Process\n\n### Contribution Workflow\n\n1. **Discuss major features**: Before starting work on features >100 LOC or behavior changes, open a GitHub issue to discuss with maintainers\n2. **Small patches**: Bug fixes and small patches don't require prior discussion\n3. **Fork and branch**: Fork the repository and create a feature branch\n4. **Local hooks**: Run `./support/bootstrap` to install pre-commit hooks\n5. **Code and test**: Write code and tests (100% coverage required)\n6. **Documentation**: Update docs and release notes for user-facing changes\n7. **Commit message**: Follow format: `subsystem: description`\n8. **Create PR**: Push to your fork and create PR against `main` branch\n\n### Pull Request Requirements\n\n**Before submitting:**\n- All tests pass locally\n- 100% test coverage for new code\n- Code follows `STYLE.md` guidelines\n- Commit has DCO signoff (automatic via `./support/bootstrap`)\n- Release notes added to `changelogs/current.yaml` if user-facing\n- Documentation updated in `docs/` if applicable\n\n**PR Title Format:**\n- Lowercase component/subsystem name followed by colon\n- Examples:\n  - `docs: fix grammar error`\n  - `http conn man: add new feature`\n  - `router: add x-envoy-overloaded header`\n\n**PR Description Fields** (see `PULL_REQUEST_TEMPLATE.md`):\n- **Commit Message**: What the PR does, behavior changes, bug fixes\n- **Additional Description**: Extra context for reviewers\n- **Risk Level**: Low, Medium, or High\n- **Testing**: What testing was performed\n- **Documentation**: Documentation changes\n- **Release Notes**: User-facing impact\n- **Issues**: Link with `Fixes #XXX` to auto-close issues\n\n### Code Style\n\n**File:** `STYLE.md`\n\nKey requirements:\n- **Formatting**: clang-format (checked automatically)\n- **Line length**: Max 100 columns\n- **Naming**: camelCase for functions (lowercase start), PascalCase for enums, `foo_` for member variables\n- **Language**: Google C++ style guide with Envoy deviations\n- **Tests**: Default to StrictMock for Google Mock\n- **Comments**: Use GitHub username in TODOs, e.g., `TODO(username): description`\n- **Inclusive Language**: No whitelist/blacklist/master/slave terminology\n\n### Code Review and Merging\n\n**Review Process:**\n- PR assigned to maintainer automatically\n- Expected turnaround: within one business day\n- Typically requires one senior maintainer review + domain expert\n- For new extensions: at least one approval from different organization than author\n- Anyone can review, but maintainers must approve\n\n**Before Merging:**\n- All tests pass in CI\n- All comments resolved\n- **Don't rebase after review starts** — use merge instead (CI will squash on merge)\n- PR title and description cleaned up by maintainer\n- Original PR author's DCO signoff preserved\n\n### DCO Sign-off (Developer Certificate of Origin)\n\nAll commits must be signed off with DCO. This is automatic if you run `./support/bootstrap`.\n\n**Manual sign-off:**\n```bash\ngit commit -s -m \"message\"\n# Or set up aliases\ngit config --add alias.c \"commit -s\"\ngit config --add alias.amend \"commit -s --amend\"\n```\n\n**If DCO check fails**, squash commits and add signoff:\n```bash\ngit rebase -i HEAD^^\n# Then fix signoff and force push (only for DCO fixes)\ngit push origin -f\n```\n\n### Breaking Changes and Deprecation\n\n- **API deprecation**: Must implement conversion and add tests with `DEPRECATED_FEATURE_TEST()` macro\n- **Configuration deprecation**: Must document in `changelogs/current.yaml`\n- **Breaking changes**: Clear deprecation path (warn, then fail) with runtime override option\n- **Runtime guarding**: High-risk changes should be guarded with `Runtime::runtimeFeatureEnabled(\"envoy.reloadable_features.feature_name\")`\n\nFor details, see `CONTRIBUTING.md` Breaking Change Policy section.\n\n### Getting Help\n\n- **Mailing Lists**:\n  - `envoy-dev@groups.google.com` — Developer discussion\n  - `envoy-announce@groups.google.com` — Announcements\n  - `envoy-users@groups.google.com` — User discussion\n  - `envoy-maintainers@groups.google.com` — Reach all maintainers\n\n- **Slack**: https://envoyproxy.slack.com/ (get invite at https://communityinviter.com/apps/envoyproxy/envoy)\n- **Issues**: Use GitHub Issues for bugs and feature discussions\n- **CODEOWNERS**: See `CODEOWNERS` file to find domain experts\n\n---\n\n## 6. Developer Workflow Example\n\n### Concrete Example: Fix HTTP Connection Manager Bug\n\nThis example walks through fixing a bug in the HTTP connection manager filter from cloning to PR merge.\n\n#### Step 1: Setup\n\n```bash\n# Clone the repository\ngit clone https://github.com/YOUR-USERNAME/envoy.git\ncd envoy\n\n# Install development toolchain\n./support/bootstrap\n\n# Create feature branch\ngit checkout -b bugfix/http-connman-fix\n\n# Make sure you're on the latest main\ngit checkout main\ngit pull origin main\ngit checkout bugfix/http-connman-fix\ngit merge main\n```\n\n#### Step 2: Locate the Code\n\nThe HTTP connection manager filter is in:\n- **Source**: `source/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/`\n- **Headers**: `envoy/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/http_connection_manager.h`\n- **Tests**: `test/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/`\n- **Config proto**: `api/envoy/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/v3/`\n\nStart by exploring the test files to understand existing behavior:\n```bash\n# Run existing tests\nbazel test //test/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager:*\n```\n\n#### Step 3: Write Tests First\n\nCreate or modify test in `test/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/conn_manager_test.cc`:\n\n```cpp\n#include \"test/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/config_test_base.h\"\n#include \"test/mocks/http/mocks.h\"\n\n// Add test for the bug\nTEST(HttpConnectionManagerTest, FixedBugBehavior) {\n  // Arrange: Set up test fixtures\n  // Act: Trigger the bug scenario\n  // Assert: Verify expected behavior after fix\n}\n```\n\nRun the test to confirm it fails:\n```bash\nbazel test //test/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager:conn_manager_test --test_filter=\"HttpConnectionManagerTest.FixedBugBehavior\"\n```\n\n#### Step 4: Implement the Fix\n\nEdit the source code:\n```bash\n# Main source files\nvi source/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/conn_manager_impl.cc\nvi source/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/conn_manager_impl.h\n```\n\nRun tests to verify fix:\n```bash\nbazel test //test/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager:conn_manager_test --test_filter=\"HttpConnectionManagerTest.FixedBugBehavior\"\n```\n\n#### Step 5: Verify Full Test Coverage\n\nEnsure 100% coverage for modified code:\n```bash\n# Run all HTTP connection manager tests\nbazel test //test/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager:*\n\n# Run broader test suite\nbazel test //test/extensions/filters/network/...\n```\n\n#### Step 6: Format Code\n\nAuto-format and check for issues:\n```bash\n# Using support toolchain hooks (automatic on commit)\n# Or manually:\nbazel run //tools/code_format:check_format -- fix\n\n# Check clang-tidy\nbazel run //tools/code:check -- fix -s main -v warn\n```\n\nOr in Docker:\n```bash\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh format'\n```\n\n#### Step 7: Documentation and Release Notes\n\nIf this is a user-facing fix:\n\n1. **Update release notes** in `changelogs/current.yaml`:\n```yaml\n- area: http\n  change: |\n    Fixed HTTP connection manager bug where [description]. This can be reverted with runtime guard\n    `envoy.reloadable_features.fixed_http_connman_bug` if needed.\n```\n\n2. **Update docs** if API changes:\n   - Proto inline docs in `api/envoy/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/v3/`\n   - User docs in `docs/root/configuration/listeners/`\n\n#### Step 8: Commit and Push\n\n```bash\n# Stage changes\ngit add source/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/\ngit add test/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/\ngit add changelogs/current.yaml\ngit add docs/\n\n# Commit with DCO sign-off (automatic via bootstrap hook)\ngit commit -m \"http conn man: fix bug with connection handling\n\nFixes a critical bug where [specific issue] was causing [impact].\n\nThe fix ensures that [how it's fixed].\n\nFixes #1234\"\n\n# Push to your fork\ngit push origin bugfix/http-connman-fix\n```\n\n#### Step 9: Create Pull Request\n\nOn GitHub:\n1. Go to your fork, create PR against `main` branch\n2. Fill in PR template:\n   - **Title**: `http conn man: fix connection handling bug`\n   - **Risk**: `Medium` (fixes existing code path)\n   - **Testing**: \"All unit and integration tests pass. Added test case `FixedBugBehavior` to verify fix.\"\n   - **Documentation**: Updated `changelogs/current.yaml` with release notes\n   - **Release Notes**: Added to changelogs/current.yaml\n\n#### Step 10: CI Verification\n\nGitHub automatically runs full CI suite:\n- Wait for all checks to pass (typically 30-45 minutes)\n- If failures occur, check error messages and iterate:\n  ```bash\n  git log --oneline -1\n  # Make fix\n  git commit -s --amend\n  git push origin bugfix/http-connman-fix --force-with-lease\n  ```\n\n  **Important**: Don't force push after a maintainer starts reviewing\n\n#### Step 11: Code Review\n\n1. Maintainer assigned automatically\n2. May request changes or clarifications\n3. Update code if needed without rebasing (add new commits instead)\n4. Maintainer cleans up title/message and merges\n\n#### Step 12: Post-Merge\n\n1. PR is squash-merged to `main`\n2. Your branch can be deleted\n3. Monitor for any issues in releases\n\n---\n\n## Additional Resources\n\n### Key Documentation Files\n\n- **DEVELOPER.md** — Developer setup and workflows\n- **CONTRIBUTING.md** — Full contribution guidelines\n- **STYLE.md** — Code style and best practices\n- **REPO_LAYOUT.md** — Repository structure\n- **bazel/README.md** — Bazel build system documentation\n- **test/README.md** — Testing frameworks and utilities\n- **test/integration/README.md** — Integration testing guide\n- **support/README.md** — Development support toolchain\n- **ci/README.md** — CI system details and Docker usage\n- **PULL_REQUESTS.md** — PR template field explanations\n\n### Extension Development\n\nFor developers adding new extensions:\n- See `CONTRIBUTING.md` \"Adding new extensions\" section\n- Use existing extensions as templates\n- API files in `api/envoy/extensions/`\n- Source in `source/extensions/`\n- Configuration in BUILD files with `envoy_cc_extension` rule\n- For contrib extensions, see `EXTENSION_POLICY.md`\n\n### Performance and Advanced Topics\n\n- **Remote build caching**: Configure in `.bazelrc` with `--remote_cache`\n- **Distributed testing**: RBE configuration in `.bazelci/`\n- **Profiling**: See `bazel/PPROF.md` for tcmalloc/pprof profiling\n- **Code generation**: `bazel/EXTERNAL_DEPS.md` for managing dependencies\n\n### Community\n\n- **Bi-weekly community meeting**: Check [public calendar](https://goo.gl/PkDijT) and [meeting minutes](https://goo.gl/5Cergb)\n- **Code owners**: Check `CODEOWNERS` file for maintainers by subsystem\n- **OWNERS**: See `OWNERS.md` for list of committers\n\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}

Build Prerequisites\n     4→\n     5→Envoy requires the following tools and dependencies before building:\n     6→\n     7→### Core Tools\n     8→- **Bazel/Bazelisk**: The Envoy project uses Bazel as its build system. It's recommended to use [Bazelisk](https://github.com/bazelbuild/bazelisk) which automatically manages Bazel versions.\n     9→  - **Linux**: Install via `sudo wget -O /usr/local/bin/bazel https://github.com/bazelbuild/bazelisk/releases/latest/download/bazelisk-linux-$([ $(uname -m) = \"aarch64\" ] && echo \"arm64\" || echo \"amd64\")` and `sudo chmod +x /usr/local/bin/bazel`\n    10→  - **macOS**: Install via `brew install bazelisk`\n    11→  - **Windows**: Download from [Bazelisk releases](https://github.com/bazelbuild/bazelisk/releases) and add to PATH\n    12→\n    13→### Build Dependencies\n    14→The following are required for building Envoy in production environments. For development, Docker containers are recommended (see section on CI Docker images).\n    15→\n    16→- C++ compiler (Clang 14 or GCC 9+)\n    17→- Python 3.6+\n    18→- Git\n    19→\n    20→### Development Docker Images\n    21→For a self-contained development environment, use the official Envoy build Docker images:\n    22→- **Linux**: `envoyproxy/envoy-build-ubuntu` (based on Ubuntu 20.04)\n    23→- **CentOS**: `envoyproxy/envoy-build-centos` (experimental, based on CentOS 7)\n    24→- **Windows**: `envoyproxy/envoy-build-windows2019` (official Windows support ended August 2023)\n    25→\n    26→Retrieve the specific image SHA from `ci/envoy_build_sha.sh`.\n    27→\n    28→### Setup Development Support Toolchain\n    29→Before contributing, install the development support toolchain for automatic DCO signoff and pre-commit format checking:\n    30→\n    31→```bash\n    32→./support/bootstrap\n    33→```\n    34→\n    35→This installs Git hooks from `support/hooks/` that:\n    36→- Automatically append DCO signoff to commits\n    37→- Run format and lint checks before push\n    38→\n    39→Documentation: See `support/README.md`\n    40→\n    41→---\n    42→\n    43→## 2. Build System\n    44→\n    45→Envoy uses **Bazel** as its build system. All build configuration is defined in `BUILD` files and `.bazelrc` configuration files.\n    46→\n    47→### Key Build Concepts\n    48→- **BUILD files**: Located throughout the codebase, define build targets using Bazel rules\n    49→- **.bazelrc**: Main configuration file in the repository root\n    50→- **Bazel rules**: Custom Envoy-specific rules defined in `bazel/` directory (e.g., `envoy_cc_library`, `envoy_cc_extension`, etc.)\n    51→\n    52→### Building for Development\n    53→\n    54→#### Using Docker (Recommended)\n    55→The easiest way to build for development is using the provided Docker script:\n    56→\n    57→```bash\n    58→./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh dev'\n    59→```\n    60→\n    61→This builds Envoy with fastbuild configuration inside a standardized container. Output binary: `/tmp/envoy-docker-build/envoy/source/exe/envoy-fastbuild`\n    62→\n    63→Control output directory with environment variable:\n    64→```bash\n    65→ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR=~/build ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh dev'\n    66→```\n    67→\n    68→#### Direct Bazel Commands (Linux/macOS)\n    69→If you have build dependencies installed locally:\n    70→\n    71→```bash\n    72→# Development build (fastbuild, fastest)\n    73→bazel build -c fastbuild //source/exe:envoy-static\n    74→\n    75→# Release build (optimized)\n    76→bazel build -c opt //source/exe:envoy-static\n    77→\n    78→# Debug build (with symbols)\n    79→bazel build -c dbg //source/exe:envoy-static\n    80→\n    81→# Build a specific test\n    82→bazel build //test/common/network:connection_test\n    83→```\n    84→\n    85→### Build Configurations Available\n    86→\n    87→#### Via `./ci/do_ci.sh <TARGET>` in Docker:\n    88→- **dev** — fastbuild with tests\n    89→- **dev <test>** — fastbuild for specific test\n    90→- **debug** — dbg configuration with tests\n    91→- **debug <test>** — dbg for specific test\n    92→- **release** — opt configuration with tests\n    93→- **release <test>** — opt for specific test\n    94→- **release.server_only** — opt configuration, binary only\n    95→- **debug.server_only** — dbg configuration, binary only\n    96→- **asan** — ASAN sanitizer build with tests\n    97→- **msan** — MSAN sanitizer build with tests\n    98→- **tsan** — TSAN sanitizer build with tests\n    99→- **coverage** — coverage build with gcc\n   100→- **compile_time_options** — test various compile flags\n   101→- **format** — run formatting and linting\n   102→- **clang_tidy** — run clang-tidy analysis\n   103→\n   104→### Building Extensions and Specific Components\n   105→\n   106→To build only specific packages (not the entire repo):\n   107→\n   108→```bash\n   109→# Build HTTP connection manager filter\n   110→bazel build //source/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager:config_lib\n   111→\n   112→# Build and test HTTP filters\n   113→bazel test //source/extensions/filters/http/...\n   114→```\n   115→\n   116→### Build File Structure\n   117→\n   118→Core Bazel rules used in Envoy:\n   119→- `envoy_cc_library` — C++ library\n   120→- `envoy_cc_binary` — C++ binary\n   121→- `envoy_cc_test` — C++ unit test\n   122→- `envoy_cc_extension` — Extension (filter, etc.)\n   123→- `envoy_integration_test` — Integration test\n   124→- `envoy_benchmark_test` — Benchmark test\n   125→\n   126→Location: `bazel/envoy_build_system.bzl` and `bazel/DEVELOPER.md`\n   127→\n   128→---\n   129→\n   130→## 3. Running Tests\n   131→\n   132→Envoy uses **Google Test** framework for unit tests and a custom integration test framework for end-to-end testing.\n   133→\n   134→### Test Frameworks\n   135→\n   136→1. **Google Test (gtest)**: Unit tests using Google Test macros (EXPECT_*, ASSERT_*)\n   137→2. **Google Mock (gmock)**: Mocking and matchers for unit tests\n   138→3. **Integration Test Framework**: Custom framework in `test/integration/` for downstream-Envoy-upstream testing\n   139→4. **Benchmark Tests**: Performance testing via Google Benchmark\n   140→\n   141→### Running All Tests\n   142→\n   143→#### Using Docker (Recommended):\n   144→```bash\n   145→./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh dev'\n   146→```\n   147→\n   148→#### Direct Bazel:\n   149→```bash\n   150→# Run all tests in fastbuild\n   151→bazel test -c fastbuild //test/...\n   152→\n   153→# Run with test args (e.g., verbose output)\n   154→bazel test -c fastbuild //test/... --test_arg=\"-l trace\"\n   155→\n   156→# Run with multiple jobs for parallelization\n   157→bazel test -c fastbuild //test/... --jobs 60\n   158→```\n   159→\n   160→### Running Specific Tests\n   161→\n   162→```bash\n   163→# Run all tests in a directory\n   164→bazel test //test/common/network:*\n   165→\n   166→# Run a specific test file\n   167→bazel test //test/common/network:connection_test\n   168→\n   169→# Run a specific test case\n   170→bazel test //test/common/network:connection_test --test_filter=\"ConnectionTest.Accepted\"\n   171→\n   172→# Run integration tests\n   173→bazel test //test/integration:http_integration_test\n   174→```\n   175→\n   176→### Integration Tests\n   177→\n   178→Integration tests validate end-to-end downstream-Envoy-upstream communication. They're located in `test/integration/`:\n   179→\n   180→```bash\n   181→bazel test //test/integration:http_integration_test\n   182→bazel test //test/integration:http2_upstream_integration_test\n   183→```\n   184→\n   185→Integration tests can be parameterized to run with different configurations (IPv4/IPv6, HTTP/1.1, HTTP/2, etc.).\n   186→\n   187→### Test Coverage\n   188→\n   189→Envoy requires **100% test coverage for added code**. Generate coverage reports:\n   190→\n   191→```bash\n   192→./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh coverage'\n   193→```\n   194→\n   195→Coverage output: `$ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR/envoy/generated/coverage/coverage.html`\n   196→\n   197→Or for a specific test:\n   198→```bash\n   199→./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh coverage //test/common/network:connection_test'\n   200→```\n   201→\n   202→### Test Utilities and Helpers\n   203→\n   204→Key test utilities located in `test/`:\n   205→- `test/test_common/` — Common test utilities\n   206→- `test/mocks/` — Mock implementations of core interfaces\n   207→- `test/integration/` — Integration test framework\n   208→- `test/config/` — Configuration utilities for tests\n   209→\n   210→Important test macros and patterns (from `test/README.md`):\n   211→- `EXPECT_THAT()` with `HeaderValueOf()`, `HttpStatusIs()`, etc. for HTTP testing\n   212→- `SimulatedTimeSystem` for deterministic time-based tests\n   213→- `Event::TestTimeSystem` for controlling time in tests\n   214→\n   215→---\n   216→\n   217→## 4. CI Pipeline\n   218→\n   219→Envoy uses **Azure Pipelines** as the primary CI system, with additional tooling for distributed testing.\n   220→\n   221→### CI Platform: Azure Pipelines\n   222→\n   223→Azure Pipelines automatically runs on all pull requests to `envoyproxy/envoy`. Access it at:\n   224→https://dev.azure.com/cncf/envoy/_build\n   225→\n   226→### CI Configuration Files\n   227→\n   228→- **`.azure-pipelines/`** — Main CI configuration directory (not present in this version but referenced in README.md)\n   229→- **`ci/do_ci.sh`** — Main CI script that orchestrates builds and tests\n   230→- **`ci/run_envoy_docker.sh`** — Docker runner for local CI reproduction\n   231→- **`ci/mac_ci_steps.sh`** — macOS-specific build and test steps\n   232→- **`ci/mac_ci_setup.sh`** — macOS dependency installation via Homebrew\n   233→- **`ci/windows_ci_steps.sh`** — Windows build and test steps (deprecated)\n   234→\n   235→### CI Checks Run on Pull Requests\n   236→\n   237→1. **Compilation**: Build Envoy with multiple configurations (fastbuild, opt, dbg)\n   238→2. **Testing**: Run full unit and integration test suite\n   239→3. **Sanitizers**: ASAN, MSAN, TSAN builds and tests\n   240→4. **Format Checking**: Code formatting, clang-tidy, proto format validation\n   241→5. **Coverage**: Coverage build and analysis\n   242→6. **Platform-Specific**: macOS builds via Azure Pipelines\n   243→\n   244→### CI Targets\n   245→\n   246→All CI targets can be run locally via:\n   247→```bash\n   248→./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh <TARGET>'\n   249→```\n   250→\n   251→Where `<TARGET>` is one of: `api`, `asan`, `debug`, `dev`, `dev.contrib`, `release`, `sizeopt`, `coverage`, `msan`, `tsan`, `fuzz`, `compile_time_options`, `clang_tidy`, `format`, `check_proto_format`, `docs`.\n   252→\n   253→### CI Timing\n   254→\n   255→- Typical full CI run: **30-45 minutes**\n   256→- Can be parallelized across multiple machines/jobs\n   257→- PRs are checked against main branch\n   258→\n   259→### Triggering CI Reruns\n   260→\n   261→To rerun CI without making code changes:\n   262→\n   263→1. **Retest failed tasks**: Add comment `/retest` to PR\n   264→2. **Full rerun**: Push empty commit: `git commit -s --allow-empty -m 'Kick CI' && git push` (or use alias from `.gitconfig`)\n   265→\n   266→### Distributed Testing Infrastructure\n   267→\n   268→- **Remote Build Cache**: Optional for faster rebuilds\n   269→- **RBE (Remote Build Execution)**: Can be configured for distributed test execution\n   270→- **Bazel CI Integration**: `.bazelci/` directory contains Bazel-specific CI configs\n   271→\n   272→---\n   273→\n   274→## 5. Code Review Process\n   275→\n   276→### Contribution Workflow\n   277→\n   278→1. **Discuss major features**: Before starting work on features >100 LOC or behavior changes, open a GitHub issue to discuss with maintainers\n   279→2. **Small patches**: Bug fixes and small patches don't require prior discussion\n   280→3. **Fork and branch**: Fork the repository and create a feature branch\n   281→4. **Local hooks**: Run `./support/bootstrap` to install pre-commit hooks\n   282→5. **Code and test**: Write code and tests (100% coverage required)\n   283→6. **Documentation**: Update docs and release notes for user-facing changes\n   284→7. **Commit message**: Follow format: `subsystem: description`\n   285→8. **Create PR**: Push to your fork and create PR against `main` branch\n   286→\n   287→### Pull Request Requirements\n   288→\n   289→**Before submitting:**\n   290→- All tests pass locally\n   291→- 100% test coverage for new code\n   292→- Code follows `STYLE.md` guidelines\n   293→- Commit has DCO signoff (automatic via `./support/bootstrap`)\n   294→- Release notes added to `changelogs/current.yaml` if user-facing\n   295→- Documentation updated in `docs/` if applicable\n   296→\n   297→**PR Title Format:**\n   298→- Lowercase component/subsystem name followed by colon\n   299→- Examples:\n   300→  - `docs: fix grammar error`\n   301→  - `http conn man: add new feature`\n   302→  - `router: add x-envoy-overloaded header`\n   303→\n   304→**PR Description Fields** (see `PULL_REQUEST_TEMPLATE.md`):\n   305→- **Commit Message**: What the PR does, behavior changes, bug fixes\n   306→- **Additional Description**: Extra context for reviewers\n   307→- **Risk Level**: Low, Medium, or High\n   308→- **Testing**: What testing was performed\n   309→- **Documentation**: Documentation changes\n   310→- **Release Notes**: User-facing impact\n   311→- **Issues**: Link with `Fixes #XXX` to auto-close issues\n   312→\n   313→### Code Style\n   314→\n   315→**File:** `STYLE.md`\n   316→\n   317→Key requirements:\n   318→- **Formatting**: clang-format (checked automatically)\n   319→- **Line length**: Max 100 columns\n   320→- **Naming**: camelCase for functions (lowercase start), PascalCase for enums, `foo_` for member variables\n   321→- **Language**: Google C++ style guide with Envoy deviations\n   322→- **Tests**: Default to StrictMock for Google Mock\n   323→- **Comments**: Use GitHub username in TODOs, e.g., `TODO(username): description`\n   324→- **Inclusive Language**: No whitelist/blacklist/master/slave terminology\n   325→\n   326→### Code Review and Merging\n   327→\n   328→**Review Process:**\n   329→- PR assigned to maintainer automatically\n   330→- Expected turnaround: within one business day\n   331→- Typically requires one senior maintainer review + domain expert\n   332→- For new extensions: at least one approval from different organization than author\n   333→- Anyone can review, but maintainers must approve\n   334→\n   335→**Before Merging:**\n   336→- All tests pass in CI\n   337→- All comments resolved\n   338→- **Don't rebase after review starts** — use merge instead (CI will squash on merge)\n   339→- PR title and description cleaned up by maintainer\n   340→- Original PR author's DCO signoff preserved\n   341→\n   342→### DCO Sign-off (Developer Certificate of Origin)\n   343→\n   344→All commits must be signed off with DCO. This is automatic if you run `./support/bootstrap`.\n   345→\n   346→**Manual sign-off:**\n   347→```bash\n   348→git commit -s -m \"message\"\n   349→# Or set up aliases\n   350→git config --add alias.c \"commit -s\"\n   351→git config --add alias.amend \"commit -s --amend\"\n   352→```\n   353→\n   354→**If DCO check fails**, squash commits and add signoff:\n   355→```bash\n   356→git rebase -i HEAD^^\n   357→# Then fix signoff and force push (only for DCO fixes)\n   358→git push origin -f\n   359→```\n   360→\n   361→### Breaking Changes and Deprecation\n   362→\n   363→- **API deprecation**: Must implement conversion and add tests with `DEPRECATED_FEATURE_TEST()` macro\n   364→- **Configuration deprecation**: Must document in `changelogs/current.yaml`\n   365→- **Breaking changes**: Clear deprecation path (warn, then fail) with runtime override option\n   366→- **Runtime guarding**: High-risk changes should be guarded with `Runtime::runtimeFeatureEnabled(\"envoy.reloadable_features.feature_name\")`\n   367→\n   368→For details, see `CONTRIBUTING.md` Breaking Change Policy section.\n   369→\n   370→### Getting Help\n   371→\n   372→- **Mailing Lists**:\n   373→  - `envoy-dev@groups.google.com` — Developer discussion\n   374→  - `envoy-announce@groups.google.com` — Announcements\n   375→  - `envoy-users@groups.google.com` — User discussion\n   376→  - `envoy-maintainers@groups.google.com` — Reach all maintainers\n   377→\n   378→- **Slack**: https://envoyproxy.slack.com/ (get invite at https://communityinviter.com/apps/envoyproxy/envoy)\n   379→- **Issues**: Use GitHub Issues for bugs and feature discussions\n   380→- **CODEOWNERS**: See `CODEOWNERS` file to find domain experts\n   381→\n   382→---\n   383→\n   384→## 6. Developer Workflow Example\n   385→\n   386→### Concrete Example: Fix HTTP Connection Manager Bug\n   387→\n   388→This example walks through fixing a bug in the HTTP connection manager filter from cloning to PR merge.\n   389→\n   390→#### Step 1: Setup\n   391→\n   392→```bash\n   393→# Clone the repository\n   394→git clone https://github.com/YOUR-USERNAME/envoy.git\n   395→cd envoy\n   396→\n   397→# Install development toolchain\n   398→./support/bootstrap\n   399→\n   400→# Create feature branch\n   401→git checkout -b bugfix/http-connman-fix\n   402→\n   403→# Make sure you're on the latest main\n   404→git checkout main\n   405→git pull origin main\n   406→git checkout bugfix/http-connman-fix\n   407→git merge main\n   408→```\n   409→\n   410→#### Step 2: Locate the Code\n   411→\n   412→The HTTP connection manager filter is in:\n   413→- **Source**: `source/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/`\n   414→- **Headers**: `envoy/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/http_connection_manager.h`\n   415→- **Tests**: `test/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/`\n   416→- **Config proto**: `api/envoy/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/v3/`\n   417→\n   418→Start by exploring the test files to understand existing behavior:\n   419→```bash\n   420→# Run existing tests\n   421→bazel test //test/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager:*\n   422→```\n   423→\n   424→#### Step 3: Write Tests First\n   425→\n   426→Create or modify test in `test/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/conn_manager_test.cc`:\n   427→\n   428→```cpp\n   429→#include \"test/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/config_test_base.h\"\n   430→#include \"test/mocks/http/mocks.h\"\n   431→\n   432→// Add test for the bug\n   433→TEST(HttpConnectionManagerTest, FixedBugBehavior) {\n   434→  // Arrange: Set up test fixtures\n   435→  // Act: Trigger the bug scenario\n   436→  // Assert: Verify expected behavior after fix\n   437→}\n   438→```\n   439→\n   440→Run the test to confirm it fails:\n   441→```bash\n   442→bazel test //test/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager:conn_manager_test --test_filter=\"HttpConnectionManagerTest.FixedBugBehavior\"\n   443→```\n   444→\n   445→#### Step 4: Implement the Fix\n   446→\n   447→Edit the source code:\n   448→```bash\n   449→# Main source files\n   450→vi source/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/conn_manager_impl.cc\n   451→vi source/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/conn_manager_impl.h\n   452→```\n   453→\n   454→Run tests to verify fix:\n   455→```bash\n   456→bazel test //test/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager:conn_manager_test --test_filter=\"HttpConnectionManagerTest.FixedBugBehavior\"\n   457→```\n   458→\n   459→#### Step 5: Verify Full Test Coverage\n   460→\n   461→Ensure 100% coverage for modified code:\n   462→```bash\n   463→# Run all HTTP connection manager tests\n   464→bazel test //test/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager:*\n   465→\n   466→# Run broader test suite\n   467→bazel test //test/extensions/filters/network/...\n   468→```\n   469→\n   470→#### Step 6: Format Code\n   471→\n   472→Auto-format and check for issues:\n   473→```bash\n   474→# Using support toolchain hooks Build Prerequisites\n\nEnvoy requires the following tools and dependencies before building:\n\n### Core Tools\n- **Bazel/Bazelisk**: The Envoy project uses Bazel as its build system. It's recommended to use [Bazelisk](https://github.com/bazelbuild/bazelisk) which automatically manages Bazel versions.\n  - **Linux**: Install via `sudo wget -O /usr/local/bin/bazel https://github.com/bazelbuild/bazelisk/releases/latest/download/bazelisk-linux-$([ $(uname -m) = \"aarch64\" ] && echo \"arm64\" || echo \"amd64\")` and `sudo chmod +x /usr/local/bin/bazel`\n  - **macOS**: Install via `brew install bazelisk`\n  - **Windows**: Download from [Bazelisk releases](https://github.com/bazelbuild/bazelisk/releases) and add to PATH\n\n### Build Dependencies\nThe following are required for building Envoy in production environments. For development, Docker containers are recommended (see section on CI Docker images).\n\n- C++ compiler (Clang 14 or GCC 9+)\n- Python 3.6+\n- Git\n\n### Development Docker Images\nFor a self-contained development environment, use the official Envoy build Docker images:\n- **Linux**: `envoyproxy/envoy-build-ubuntu` (based on Ubuntu 20.04)\n- **CentOS**: `envoyproxy/envoy-build-centos` (experimental, based on CentOS 7)\n- **Windows**: `envoyproxy/envoy-build-windows2019` (official Windows support ended August 2023)\n\nRetrieve the specific image SHA from `ci/envoy_build_sha.sh`.\n\n### Setup Development Support Toolchain\nBefore contributing, install the development support toolchain for automatic DCO signoff and pre-commit format checking:\n\n```bash\n./support/bootstrap\n```\n\nThis installs Git hooks from `support/hooks/` that:\n- Automatically append DCO signoff to commits\n- Run format and lint checks before push\n\nDocumentation: See `support/README.md`\n\n---\n\n## 2. Build System\n\nEnvoy uses **Bazel** as its build system. All build configuration is defined in `BUILD` files and `.bazelrc` configuration files.\n\n### Key Build Concepts\n- **BUILD files**: Located throughout the codebase, define build targets using Bazel rules\n- **.bazelrc**: Main configuration file in the repository root\n- **Bazel rules**: Custom Envoy-specific rules defined in `bazel/` directory (e.g., `envoy_cc_library`, `envoy_cc_extension`, etc.)\n\n### Building for Development\n\n#### Using Docker (Recommended)\nThe easiest way to build for development is using the provided Docker script:\n\n```bash\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh dev'\n```\n\nThis builds Envoy with fastbuild configuration inside a standardized container. Output binary: `/tmp/envoy-docker-build/envoy/source/exe/envoy-fastbuild`\n\nControl output directory with environment variable:\n```bash\nENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR=~/build ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh dev'\n```\n\n#### Direct Bazel Commands (Linux/macOS)\nIf you have build dependencies installed locally:\n\n```bash\n# Development build (fastbuild, fastest)\nbazel build -c fastbuild //source/exe:envoy-static\n\n# Release build (optimized)\nbazel build -c opt //source/exe:envoy-static\n\n# Debug build (with symbols)\nbazel build -c dbg //source/exe:envoy-static\n\n# Build a specific test\nbazel build //test/common/network:connection_test\n```\n\n### Build Configurations Available\n\n#### Via `./ci/do_ci.sh <TARGET>` in Docker:\n- **dev** — fastbuild with tests\n- **dev <test>** — fastbuild for specific test\n- **debug** — dbg configuration with tests\n- **debug <test>** — dbg for specific test\n- **release** — opt configuration with tests\n- **release <test>** — opt for specific test\n- **release.server_only** — opt configuration, binary only\n- **debug.server_only** — dbg configuration, binary only\n- **asan** — ASAN sanitizer build with tests\n- **msan** — MSAN sanitizer build with tests\n- **tsan** — TSAN sanitizer build with tests\n- **coverage** — coverage build with gcc\n- **compile_time_options** — test various compile flags\n- **format** — run formatting and linting\n- **clang_tidy** — run clang-tidy analysis\n\n### Building Extensions and Specific Components\n\nTo build only specific packages (not the entire repo):\n\n```bash\n# Build HTTP connection manager filter\nbazel build //source/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager:config_lib\n\n# Build and test HTTP filters\nbazel test //source/extensions/filters/http/...\n```\n\n### Build File Structure\n\nCore Bazel rules used in Envoy:\n- `envoy_cc_library` — C++ library\n- `envoy_cc_binary` — C++ binary\n- `envoy_cc_test` — C++ unit test\n- `envoy_cc_extension` — Extension (filter, etc.)\n- `envoy_integration_test` — Integration test\n- `envoy_benchmark_test` — Benchmark test\n\nLocation: `bazel/envoy_build_system.bzl` and `bazel/DEVELOPER.md`\n\n---\n\n## 3. Running Tests\n\nEnvoy uses **Google Test** framework for unit tests and a custom integration test framework for end-to-end testing.\n\n### Test Frameworks\n\n1. **Google Test (gtest)**: Unit tests using Google Test macros (EXPECT_*, ASSERT_*)\n2. **Google Mock (gmock)**: Mocking and matchers for unit tests\n3. **Integration Test Framework**: Custom framework in `test/integration/` for downstream-Envoy-upstream testing\n4. **Benchmark Tests**: Performance testing via Google Benchmark\n\n### Running All Tests\n\n#### Using Docker (Recommended):\n```bash\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh dev'\n```\n\n#### Direct Bazel:\n```bash\n# Run all tests in fastbuild\nbazel test -c fastbuild //test/...\n\n# Run with test args (e.g., verbose output)\nbazel test -c fastbuild //test/... --test_arg=\"-l trace\"\n\n# Run with multiple jobs for parallelization\nbazel test -c fastbuild //test/... --jobs 60\n```\n\n### Running Specific Tests\n\n```bash\n# Run all tests in a directory\nbazel test //test/common/network:*\n\n# Run a specific test file\nbazel test //test/common/network:connection_test\n\n# Run a specific test case\nbazel test //test/common/network:connection_test --test_filter=\"ConnectionTest.Accepted\"\n\n# Run integration tests\nbazel test //test/integration:http_integration_test\n```\n\n### Integration Tests\n\nIntegration tests validate end-to-end downstream-Envoy-upstream communication. They're located in `test/integration/`:\n\n```bash\nbazel test //test/integration:http_integration_test\nbazel test //test/integration:http2_upstream_integration_test\n```\n\nIntegration tests can be parameterized to run with different configurations (IPv4/IPv6, HTTP/1.1, HTTP/2, etc.).\n\n### Test Coverage\n\nEnvoy requires **100% test coverage for added code**. Generate coverage reports:\n\n```bash\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh coverage'\n```\n\nCoverage output: `$ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR/envoy/generated/coverage/coverage.html`\n\nOr for a specific test:\n```bash\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh coverage //test/common/network:connection_test'\n```\n\n### Test Utilities and Helpers\n\nKey test utilities located in `test/`:\n- `test/test_common/` — Common test utilities\n- `test/mocks/` — Mock implementations of core interfaces\n- `test/integration/` — Integration test framework\n- `test/config/` — Configuration utilities for tests\n\nImportant test macros and patterns (from `test/README.md`):\n- `EXPECT_THAT()` with `HeaderValueOf()`, `HttpStatusIs()`, etc. for HTTP testing\n- `SimulatedTimeSystem` for deterministic time-based tests\n- `Event::TestTimeSystem` for controlling time in tests\n\n---\n\n## 4. CI Pipeline\n\nEnvoy uses **Azure Pipelines** as the primary CI system, with additional tooling for distributed testing.\n\n### CI Platform: Azure Pipelines\n\nAzure Pipelines automatically runs on all pull requests to `envoyproxy/envoy`. Access it at:\nhttps://dev.azure.com/cncf/envoy/_build\n\n### CI Configuration Files\n\n- **`.azure-pipelines/`** — Main CI configuration directory (not present in this version but referenced in README.md)\n- **`ci/do_ci.sh`** — Main CI script that orchestrates builds and tests\n- **`ci/run_envoy_docker.sh`** — Docker runner for local CI reproduction\n- **`ci/mac_ci_steps.sh`** — macOS-specific build and test steps\n- **`ci/mac_ci_setup.sh`** — macOS dependency installation via Homebrew\n- **`ci/windows_ci_steps.sh`** — Windows build and test steps (deprecated)\n\n### CI Checks Run on Pull Requests\n\n1. **Compilation**: Build Envoy with multiple configurations (fastbuild, opt, dbg)\n2. **Testing**: Run full unit and integration test suite\n3. **Sanitizers**: ASAN, MSAN, TSAN builds and tests\n4. **Format Checking**: Code formatting, clang-tidy, proto format validation\n5. **Coverage**: Coverage build and analysis\n6. **Platform-Specific**: macOS builds via Azure Pipelines\n\n### CI Targets\n\nAll CI targets can be run locally via:\n```bash\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh <TARGET>'\n```\n\nWhere `<TARGET>` is one of: `api`, `asan`, `debug`, `dev`, `dev.contrib`, `release`, `sizeopt`, `coverage`, `msan`, `tsan`, `fuzz`, `compile_time_options`, `clang_tidy`, `format`, `check_proto_format`, `docs`.\n\n### CI Timing\n\n- Typical full CI run: **30-45 minutes**\n- Can be parallelized across multiple machines/jobs\n- PRs are checked against main branch\n\n### Triggering CI Reruns\n\nTo rerun CI without making code changes:\n\n1. **Retest failed tasks**: Add comment `/retest` to PR\n2. **Full rerun**: Push empty commit: `git commit -s --allow-empty -m 'Kick CI' && git push` (or use alias from `.gitconfig`)\n\n### Distributed Testing Infrastructure\n\n- **Remote Build Cache**: Optional for faster rebuilds\n- **RBE (Remote Build Execution)**: Can be configured for distributed test execution\n- **Bazel CI Integration**: `.bazelci/` directory contains Bazel-specific CI configs\n\n---\n\n## 5. Code Review Process\n\n### Contribution Workflow\n\n1. **Discuss major features**: Before starting work on features >100 LOC or behavior changes, open a GitHub issue to discuss with maintainers\n2. **Small patches**: Bug fixes and small patches don't require prior discussion\n3. **Fork and branch**: Fork the repository and create a feature branch\n4. **Local hooks**: Run `./support/bootstrap` to install pre-commit hooks\n5. **Code and test**: Write code and tests (100% coverage required)\n6. **Documentation**: Update docs and release notes for user-facing changes\n7. **Commit message**: Follow format: `subsystem: description`\n8. **Create PR**: Push to your fork and create PR against `main` branch\n\n### Pull Request Requirements\n\n**Before submitting:**\n- All tests pass locally\n- 100% test coverage for new code\n- Code follows `STYLE.md` guidelines\n- Commit has DCO signoff (automatic via `./support/bootstrap`)\n- Release notes added to `changelogs/current.yaml` if user-facing\n- Documentation updated in `docs/` if applicable\n\n**PR Title Format:**\n- Lowercase component/subsystem name followed by colon\n- Examples:\n  - `docs: fix grammar error`\n  - `http conn man: add new feature`\n  - `router: add x-envoy-overloaded header`\n\n**PR Description Fields** (see `PULL_REQUEST_TEMPLATE.md`):\n- **Commit Message**: What the PR does, behavior changes, bug fixes\n- **Additional Description**: Extra context for reviewers\n- **Risk Level**: Low, Medium, or High\n- **Testing**: What testing was performed\n- **Documentation**: Documentation changes\n- **Release Notes**: User-facing impact\n- **Issues**: Link with `Fixes #XXX` to auto-close issues\n\n### Code Style\n\n**File:** `STYLE.md`\n\nKey requirements:\n- **Formatting**: clang-format (checked automatically)\n- **Line length**: Max 100 columns\n- **Naming**: camelCase for functions (lowercase start), PascalCase for enums, `foo_` for member variables\n- **Language**: Google C++ style guide with Envoy deviations\n- **Tests**: Default to StrictMock for Google Mock\n- **Comments**: Use GitHub username in TODOs, e.g., `TODO(username): description`\n- **Inclusive Language**: No whitelist/blacklist/master/slave terminology\n\n### Code Review and Merging\n\n**Review Process:**\n- PR assigned to maintainer automatically\n- Expected turnaround: within one business day\n- Typically requires one senior maintainer review + domain expert\n- For new extensions: at least one approval from different organization than author\n- Anyone can review, but maintainers must approve\n\n**Before Merging:**\n- All tests pass in CI\n- All comments resolved\n- **Don't rebase after review starts** — use merge instead (CI will squash on merge)\n- PR title and description cleaned up by maintainer\n- Original PR author's DCO signoff preserved\n\n### DCO Sign-off (Developer Certificate of Origin)\n\nAll commits must be signed off with DCO. This is automatic if you run `./support/bootstrap`.\n\n**Manual sign-off:**\n```bash\ngit commit -s -m \"message\"\n# Or set up aliases\ngit config --add alias.c \"commit -s\"\ngit config --add alias.amend \"commit -s --amend\"\n```\n\n**If DCO check fails**, squash commits and add signoff:\n```bash\ngit rebase -i HEAD^^\n# Then fix signoff and force push (only for DCO fixes)\ngit push origin -f\n```\n\n### Breaking Changes and Deprecation\n\n- **API deprecation**: Must implement conversion and add tests with `DEPRECATED_FEATURE_TEST()` macro\n- **Configuration deprecation**: Must document in `changelogs/current.yaml`\n- **Breaking changes**: Clear deprecation path (warn, then fail) with runtime override option\n- **Runtime guarding**: High-risk changes should be guarded with `Runtime::runtimeFeatureEnabled(\"envoy.reloadable_features.feature_name\")`\n\nFor details, see `CONTRIBUTING.md` Breaking Change Policy section.\n\n### Getting Help\n\n- **Mailing Lists**:\n  - `envoy-dev@groups.google.com` — Developer discussion\n  - `envoy-announce@groups.google.com` — Announcements\n  - `envoy-users@groups.google.com` — User discussion\n  - `envoy-maintainers@groups.google.com` — Reach all maintainers\n\n- **Slack**: https://envoyproxy.slack.com/ (get invite at https://communityinviter.com/apps/envoyproxy/envoy)\n- **Issues**: Use GitHub Issues for bugs and feature discussions\n- **CODEOWNERS**: See `CODEOWNERS` file to find domain experts\n\n---\n\n## 6. Developer Workflow Example\n\n### Concrete Example: Fix HTTP Connection Manager Bug\n\nThis example walks through fixing a bug in the HTTP connection manager filter from cloning to PR merge.\n\n#### Step 1: Setup\n\n```bash\n# Clone the repository\ngit clone https://github.com/YOUR-USERNAME/envoy.git\ncd envoy\n\n# Install development toolchain\n./support/bootstrap\n\n# Create feature branch\ngit checkout -b bugfix/http-connman-fix\n\n# Make sure you're on the latest main\ngit checkout main\ngit pull origin main\ngit checkout bugfix/http-connman-fix\ngit merge main\n```\n\n#### Step 2: Locate the Code\n\nThe HTTP connection manager filter is in:\n- **Source**: `source/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/`\n- **Headers**: `envoy/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/http_connection_manager.h`\n- **Tests**: `test/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/`\n- **Config proto**: `api/envoy/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/v3/`\n\nStart by exploring the test files to understand existing behavior:\n```bash\n# Run existing tests\nbazel test //test/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager:*\n```\n\n#### Step 3: Write Tests First\n\nCreate or modify test in `test/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/conn_manager_test.cc`:\n\n```cpp\n#include \"test/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/config_test_base.h\"\n#include \"test/mocks/http/mocks.h\"\n\n// Add test for the bug\nTEST(HttpConnectionManagerTest, FixedBugBehavior) {\n  // Arrange: Set up test fixtures\n  // Act: Trigger the bug scenario\n  // Assert: Verify expected behavior after fix\n}\n```\n\nRun the test to confirm it fails:\n```bash\nbazel test //test/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager:conn_manager_test --test_filter=\"HttpConnectionManagerTest.FixedBugBehavior\"\n```\n\n#### Step 4: Implement the Fix\n\nEdit the source code:\n```bash\n# Main source files\nvi source/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/conn_manager_impl.cc\nvi source/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/conn_manager_impl.h\n```\n\nRun tests to verify fix:\n```bash\nbazel test //test/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager:conn_manager_test --test_filter=\"HttpConnectionManagerTest.FixedBugBehavior\"\n```\n\n#### Step 5: Verify Full Test Coverage\n\nEnsure 100% coverage for modified code:\n```bash\n# Run all HTTP connection manager tests\nbazel test //test/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager:*\n\n# Run broader test suite\nbazel test //test/extensions/filters/network/...\n```\n\n#### Step 6: Format Code\n\nAuto-format and check for issues:\n```bash\n# Using support toolchain hooks (automatic on commit)\n# Or manually:\nbazel run //tools/code_format:check_format -- fix\n\n# Check clang-tidy\nbazel run //tools/code:check -- fix -s main -v warn\n```\n\nOr in Docker:\n```bash\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh format'\n```\n\n#### Step 7: Documentation and Release Notes\n\nIf this is a user-facing fix:\n\n1. **Update release notes** in `changelogs/current.yaml`:\n```yaml\n- area: http\n  change: |\n    Fixed HTTP connection manager bug where [description]. This can be reverted with runtime guard\n    `envoy.reloadable_features.fixed_http_connman_bug` if needed.\n```\n\n2. **Update docs** if API changes:\n   - Proto inline docs in `api/envoy/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/v3/`\n   - User docs in `docs/root/configuration/listeners/`\n\n#### Step 8: Commit and Push\n\n```bash\n# Stage changes\ngit add source/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/\ngit add test/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/\ngit add changelogs/current.yaml\ngit add docs/\n\n# Commit with DCO sign-off (automatic via bootstrap hook)\ngit commit -m \"http conn man: fix bug with connection handling\n\nFixes a critical bug where [specific issue] was causing [impact].\n\nThe fix ensures that [how it's fixed].\n\nFixes #1234\"\n\n# Push to your fork\ngit push origin bugfix/http-connman-fix\n```\n\n#### Step 9: Create Pull Request\n\nOn GitHub:\n1. Go to your fork, create PR against `main` branch\n2. Fill in PR template:\n   - **Title**: `http conn man: fix connection handling bug`\n   - **Risk**: `Medium` (fixes existing code path)\n   - **Testing**: \"All unit and integration tests pass. Added test case `FixedBugBehavior` to verify fix.\"\n   - **Documentation**: Updated `changelogs/current.yaml` with release notes\n   - **Release Notes**: Added to changelogs/current.yaml\n\n#### Step 10: CI Verification\n\nGitHub automatically runs full CI suite:\n- Wait for all checks to pass (typically 30-45 minutes)\n- If failures occur, check error messages and iterate:\n  ```bash\n  git log --oneline -1\n  # Make fix\n  git commit -s --amend\n  git push origin bugfix/http-connman-fix --force-with-lease\n  ```\n\n  **Important**: Don't force push after a maintainer starts reviewing\n\n#### Step 11: Code Review\n\n1. Maintainer assigned automatically\n2. May request changes or clarifications\n3. Update code if needed without rebasing (add new commits instead)\n4. Maintainer cleans up title/message and merges\n\n#### Step 12: Post-Merge\n\n1. PR is squash-merged to `main`\n2. Your branch can be deleted\n3.
